Him who said “liable” one understands as you are saying for freeing from liability<sup class="footnote-marker">144a</sup><i class="footnote">Scribe’s text deleted by corrector, therefore iy is not found in the printed texts. But it is confirmed by K and necessary to understand R. Yose’s response. R. Jacob bar Zavdi argues that since bird sacrifices are treated as equal to animal sacrifices on the 14th, there is no liability if the owner still has leavened matter while bringing his offering, they also should be treated like animal sacrifices on the holiday and there should be liability.</i>. What is the reason of him who frees from liability? He said to him, one may infer punishment from punishment but one may not infer punishment from exemption.
The rabbis of Caesarea asked: I could think that the one who receives or carries [the blood]<sup class="footnote-marker">145</sup><i class="footnote">The Cohen who receives the blood of the sacrifice slaughtered by a layman or Levite, and the one who carries it to the altar. These two actions are biblically required. Reception of the blood in a sanctified vessel is mentioned explicitly; the action of carrying the blood is required implicitly since slaughter of the sacrifice must be performed away from the altar (North of the altar for most holy sacrifices, <a class="refLink" data-ref="Leviticus 1:11" href="/Leviticus.1.11"><i>Lev.</i> 1:11</a>; before the Tent of Meeting for simple sacrifices, <a class="refLink" data-ref="Leviticus 3:2" href="/Leviticus.3.2"><i>Lev.</i> 3:2</a>,<a class="refLink" data-ref="Leviticus 3:8" href="/Leviticus.3.8">8</a>,<a class="refLink" data-ref="Leviticus 3:13" href="/Leviticus.3.13">13</a>).</i> on leavened matter be liable. The verse says, <i>sacrifice</i>. Since slaughtering for sacrifice is particular in that one is liable for it outside [the Sanctuary], this excludes the one who receives or carries on leavened matter for which one is not liable outside<sup class="footnote-marker">146</sup><i class="footnote">In the prohibition of sacrifices outside the Sanctuary (<a class="refLink" data-ref="Leviticus 17" href="/Leviticus.17"><i>Lev.</i> 17</a>), only slaughter (v.4), pouring and burning of the parts (v. 6) are mentioned. There exists liability for extirpation or a purification sacrifice even if the slaughter was performed so that collection of the blood and carrying it was not necessary.</i>. I could think that one who burns parts on leavened matter be liable. The verse says, <i>and he atones</i><sup class="footnote-marker">147</sup><i class="footnote">This expression is never used for the <i>Pesaḥ.</i> The reference is to the verses referring to purification sacrifices, <a class="refLink" data-ref="Leviticus 4:26" href="/Leviticus.4.26"><i>Lev.</i>4:26</a>,<a class="refLink" data-ref="Leviticus 4:31" href="/Leviticus.4.31">31</a>, from which it would appear that the burning of the fat on the altar is the atoning agent but which in <a class="refLink" data-ref="Sifra, Braita d'Rabbi Yishmael" href="/Sifra,_Braita_d'Rabbi_Yishmael"><i>Sifra Wayyiqra II (Ḥovah) Pereq</i> 11 (5–6</a>) is explained to refer only to the pouring of the blood.</i>. Since pouring is particular in that it is indispensable for atonement, this excludes burning of the parts, which is not indispensable for atonement. Rebbi Jacob bar Zavdi asked before Rebbi Yose. Instead of arguing for absence of liability, argue for liability. I could think that the one who receives or carries [the blood]<sup class="footnote-marker">148</sup><i class="footnote">The argument shows that instead of “the one who receives or carries” one has to read “one who burns parts”.</i> on leavened matter not be liable. The verse says, <i>sacrifice</i>. Since slaughtering for sacrifice is particular in that for it one is liable outside [the Sanctuary], I also am adding burning of the parts for which one is liable outside. I could think that one who burns parts on leavened matter<sup class="footnote-marker">149</sup><i class="footnote">The argument shows that instead of “one who burns parts” one has to read “the one who receives or carries”.</i> not be liable. The verse says, <i>and he atones</i>. Since pouring is particular in that it is indispensable for atonement, I also am adding the one who receives or carries who is indispensable for atonement<sup class="footnote-marker">150</sup><i class="footnote">The argument of the rabbis of Caesarea is invalid since it can be turned upside down.</i>. He said to him, anything equal in both respects instructs; anything not equal in both respects does not instruct. <i>Sacrifice</i>. Since slaughtering for sacrifice is particular in that it is indispensable for atonement and for it one is liable outside [the Sanctuary], this excludes the one who receives or carries on leavened matter for which one is not liable outside; it excludes burning of the parts, which is not indispensable for atonement<sup class="footnote-marker">151</sup><i class="footnote">The statement of the rabbis of Caesarea is correct but their argument is incomplete.</i>.
<sup class="footnote-marker">152</sup><i class="footnote">This paragraph has a parallel in <i>Yom Tov</i> 1:1 (end).</i> There, we have stated<sup class="footnote-marker">153</sup><i class="footnote">Mishnah <i>Yom Tov (Beṣah)</i> 1:1.</i>: “The House of Shammai say, leavening in the volume of an olive, and leavened matter in the volume of a dried fig.” Rebbi Zeriqan in the name of Rebbi Yose ben Ḥanina: They stated this only for its elimination, but for eating the volume of an olive<sup class="footnote-marker">154</sup><i class="footnote">Even the House of Shammai agree that eating leavened matter in the volume of an olive on Passover creates liability.</i>. Rebbi Abbahu in the name of Rebbi Joḥanan , whether for elimination or eating, the volume of an olive<sup class="footnote-marker">155</sup><i class="footnote">This statement refers only to the opinion of the House of Hillel. While leavened matter is forbidden on Passover in the most minute amount, liability is created only by the volume of an olive, whether active leavening or passive leavened matter.</i>. Rebbi Mana was standing with Rebbi Ḥizqiah; he said to him, from where did the rabbi hear this?. He told him, from Rebbi Abbahu. He answered, we also are saying, Rebbi Abbahu in the name of Rebbi Joḥanan , whether for elimination or eating, the volume of an olive<sup class="footnote-marker">156</sup><i class="footnote">In this version, nothing can be learned from the discussion between RR. Mana and Ḥizqiah. In <i>Yom Tov</i> the statement of R. Abbahu continues with a proof, that if there were different standards for leavening and leavened matter, the Mishnah in <i>Keritut</i> which enumerates the transgressions causing extirpation should have enumerated them separately.</i>.
If one slaughtered on leavened matter, after what are you going? After eating or after elimination? There<sup class="footnote-marker">157</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Pesachim 3:2:2-6" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Pesachim.3.2.2-6">Halakhah 3:2</a>, beginning.</i> did Rebbi Jeremiah say in the name of Rebbi Zeˋira: Two volumes of half an olive in one house, the house does not combine them; in one vessel, the vessel does combine them. If one slaughtered on them, if they were in the house, and the house did not combine them, he is not liable; or if they were in one vessel and the vessel combines them, he is liable. If he slaughtered on leavening. Since Rav Ḥuna said in the name of Rav, he is permitted to feed it to his dog<sup class="footnote-marker">158</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Pesachim 2:1:2" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Pesachim.2.1.2">Halakhah 2:1, Note 9</a>.</i>, he is not liable; or since Rav said, one flogs for eating it, he is liable<sup class="footnote-marker">159</sup><i class="footnote">The questions are not answered.</i>.
Rebbi Simeon ben Laqish said, only if it belongs to the slaughterer who is one of the group<sup class="footnote-marker">160</sup><i class="footnote">What does it mean, “one who slaughters the <i>Pesaḥ</i> on leavened matter”? Whose leavened matter?</i>. Rebbi Joḥanan  said, to the slaughterer even if he is not of the group, to one of the group even if he is not the slaughterer. Rebbi Joḥanan  said, even if it is with him in Jerusalem; Rebbi Simeon ben Laqish said, only if it is with him in the Temple courtyard<sup class="footnote-marker">161</sup><i class="footnote">He reads “on” as meaning “physically close” (<a class="refLink" data-ref="Menachot 98a" href="/Menachot.98a">Babli <i>Menaḥot</i> 98a</a>).<br>In the text of K, the opinion of R. Joḥanan  is repeated (supported) by R. Jacob bar [Aha].</i>. <sup class="footnote-marker">162</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Yevamot 11:7:6" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Yevamot.11.7.6"><i>Yebamot</i> 11:7 Note 171</a>, Nazir 8:1 Notes 48,49. <a class="refLink" data-ref="Pesachim 64b" href="/Pesachim.64b">Babli 64b</a>, <a class="refLink" data-ref="Shevuot 3b" href="/Shevuot.3b"><i>Ševuot</i> 3b</a>.</i> Each of them follows his own opinion, since they disagreed: about the two holidays of the diaspora<sup class="footnote-marker">163</sup><i class="footnote">Before the publication of the computed calendar, communities which could not be informed by messengers about the determination of the first days of the months of Nisan and Tishri, kept two days of holidays to account for possible variations in the dates. Since each day was only one of a possible two, and in talmudic interpretation no infraction could be prosecuted unless the perpetrator was duly warned by two witnesses not to commit the crime, work on the holidays could not be prosecutable unless the warning was given for both days, the infraction occurred on both days, and this kind of long-term conditional warning was accepted in court. [After the publication of the calendar computations, the first day of a holiday is of biblical character; the second day is purely rabbinic and is kept only because the algorithm was published on condition that its users continue to keep the second day (<a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Eruvin 3:9:3" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Eruvin.3.9.3"><i>Eruvin</i> 3, Note 190</a>; <a class="refLink" data-ref="Beitzah 4b" href="/Beitzah.4b">Babli <i>Beṣah</i> 4b</a>).]</i>. Rebbi Joḥanan  said, one accepts forewarning in case of a doubt; Rebbi Simeon ben Laqish said, one does not accept forewarning in case of a doubt. Everybody agrees if it was lying opposite him in a window in Jerusalem. He who said, a doubt<sup class="footnote-marker">164</sup><i class="footnote">The disagreement of RR. Joḥanan  and Simeon ben Laqish can be explained as one about warnings in cases of doubt only if the leavened matter is not visible by the slaughterer at the moment of slaughter, for it might have been disposed of in the meantime. If it is visible to the slaughterer on the Temple Mount the doubt does not apply. But if the reason is that “on” means physical presence, R. Simeon ben Laqish still will declare the slaughterer not liable even though the leavened matter is visible in Jerusalem.</i>, it is certain. He who said, in the Temple courtyard, it is in Jerusalem.
What is Rebbi Jehudah’s reason? <i>The blood of my sacrifices,</i> the blood of <i>Pesaḥ</i> and the blood of the daily sacrifice<sup class="footnote-marker">166</sup><i class="footnote">R. Jehudah in the Mishnah includes the daily sacrifice in the prohibition of leavened matter. He reads זְבָחַי instead of זְבְחִי. <a class="refLink" data-ref="Pesachim 64a" href="/Pesachim.64a">Babli 64a</a>.</i>.
Rebbi Joḥanan  said, the reason of Rebbi Simeon: One verse says, <i>do not slaughter on leavened matter the blood of my sacrifice,</i> and another verse<sup class="footnote-marker">167</sup><i class="footnote">The second verse is <a class="refLink" data-ref="Exodus 23:18" href="/Exodus.23.18"><i>Ex.</i> 23:18</a>, where it says לֹא־תִזְבַּח, the first is <i>Ex..</i>34:25. <a class="refLink" data-ref="Pesachim 64a" href="/Pesachim.64a">Babli 64a</a>.</i> says, <i>do not sacrifice on leavened matter the blood of my sacrifice.</i> One refers to the <i>Pesaḥ</i> on the Fourteenth, one<sup class="footnote-marker">168</sup><i class="footnote">This is formulated as if the second verse referred to the intermediate days of the holiday.</i> to all other consumed sacrifices on the workdays of the holiday. How did you understand to add them on the workdays of the holiday and to exclude them from the Fourteenth? After that the verse added, it subtracted<sup class="footnote-marker">169</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Exodus 23:18" href="/Exodus.23.18"><i>Ex.</i> 23:18</a> is general, referring to sacrifices eaten by its owners in general, while <i>Ex..</i>34:25 explicitly mentions the <i>Pesaḥ</i> and therefore restricts its meaning.</i>. I am adding them on the workdays of the holiday since these are subject to “it should not be seen nor found”<sup class="footnote-marker">170</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Pesachim 2:1:16" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Pesachim.2.1.16">Chapter 2:2 Note 90</a>.</i>, and exclude them from the Fourteenth where they are not under “it should not be seen nor found”. And this parallels what Rebbi Meïr said; as Rebbi Meïr said, after noontime it is of their words<sup class="footnote-marker">171</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Pesachim 1:4:2" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Pesachim.1.4.2">Chapter 1:4, Notes 109–110</a>.</i>. Rebbi Mana said, there where it says, <i>the consumed sacrifice of the Pesaḥ holiday of pilgrimage,</i> we hold that it refers to the Fourteenth<sup class="footnote-marker">172</sup><i class="footnote"><i>Ex</i>..34:25 must refer to the 14th of Nisan; the anonymous majority is justified in rejecting R. Simeon’s position</i>.
<sup class="footnote-marker">173</sup><i class="footnote">The different commentators offer different emendations of this paragraph. The following commentary is offered as a tentative explanation of the text as it stands.</i> Rebbi Joḥanan  said, the company was asking, where are we holding<sup class="footnote-marker">174</sup><i class="footnote">Discussion of the statement of the Mishnah, “on the holiday, for its purpose he is not liable, not for its purpose he is liable.”</i>? If it was lost and found before propitiation, whether it was for its purpose or not for its purpose it is qualified and sent to grazing<sup class="footnote-marker">175</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Pesachim 9:6:1" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Pesachim.9.6.1">Mishnah 9:5</a>. If an animal had been designated as <i>Pesaḥ</i>, was lost, another animal was designated, and then the original was found before the other was slaughtered, it is qualified as sacrifice but cannot be used as <i>Pesaḥ</i>. A qualified sacrifice cannot be redeemed (<a class="refLink" data-ref="Leviticus 27:10" href="/Leviticus.27.10"><i>Lev</i>. 27:10</a>); therefore it shall graze until it develops a defect, then be sold and the money used to buy well-being offerings.</i>. If it was lost and found after propitiation, whether for its purpose or not for its purpose, it is disqualified as well-being offering<sup class="footnote-marker">176</sup><i class="footnote">While <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Pesachim 9:6:1" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Pesachim.9.6.1">Mishnah 9:5</a> states clearly that a <i>Pesaḥ</i> animal, which was lost and only found after the replacement was slaughtered, is a qualified well-being offering, there is an opinion in Halakhah 9:6 that “the body of any which was acceptable as a <i>Pesaḥ</i> cannot be brought as well-being offering.” While this is explained away in Halakhah 9:6, it seems to be the basis of the statement here.</i>. But we confirmed it when the owner became impure or acted criminally and already pushed to the Second <i>Pesaḥ</i><sup class="footnote-marker">177</sup><i class="footnote">The offering on the 14<sup class="footnote-marker">th</sup> of Iyar for those incapable of coming to the Sanctuary on the 14th of Nisan; <a class="refLink" data-ref="Numbers 9:9-14" href="/Numbers.9.9-14"><i>Num</i>. 9:9–14</a>.</i>. For its purpose, he is not liable and it is disqualified. Not for its purpose, he is liable and it is qualified<sup class="footnote-marker">134</sup><i class="footnote">R. Simeon reads the verse as referring not only to the 14th of Nisan but also to the entire Holiday of Unleavened Bread, Nisan 15–21. Since the <i>Pesaḥ</i> slaughtered for its purpose on any day other than the 14th is disqualified, it does not count. But not for its purpose it is a qualified well-being sacrifice.</i>. There they are saying in the name of Rav Ḥisda: If its year was completed between First and Second<sup class="footnote-marker">178</sup><i class="footnote">The <i>Pesaḥ</i> lamb must be a yearling., <a class="refLink" data-ref="Exodus 12:5" href="/Exodus.12.5"><i>Ex</i>. 12:5</a>. If the animal was dedicated before Passover but then its owner was prevented from coming to the Sanctuary in time, it automatically is dedicated for the Second <i>Pesaḥ</i>. If then it will be too old, it is automatically dedicated as well-being offering and can be used as such during the holiday; this is “not for its purpose” as <i>Pesaḥ</i>.</i>. Rebbi La in the name of Rebbi Joḥanan : When the time for its propitiation was passed<sup class="footnote-marker">179</sup><i class="footnote">If for some reason it was not used on the 14<sup class="footnote-marker">th</sup> and its owner is not eligible to celebrate the Second <i>Pesaḥ</i>, it may be used as well-being sacrifice during the holiday.</i>. “If a <i>Pesaḥ</i> whose time had passed was slaughtered for its purpose at its time<sup class="footnote-marker">180</sup><i class="footnote">An old animal, which had been dedicated when young, slaughtered on the 14th as <i>Pesaḥ</i>.</i>, or that he slaughtered another one for its purpose at its time<sup class="footnote-marker">181</sup><i class="footnote">An animal dedicated as well-being offering used as <i>Pesaḥ</i>.</i>, Rebbi Eliezer disqualifies and Rebbi Joshua qualifies. Rebbi Eliezer disqualifies since he is like one who slaughters a <i>Pesaḥ</i> for the purpose of a well-being sacrifice. Rebbi Joshua qualifies since he is like one who slaughters a well-being sacrifice for the purpose of a <i>Pesaḥ.</i><sup class="footnote-marker">182</sup><i class="footnote">The Babylonian version of the <i>baraita</i> is in <a class="refLink" data-ref="Zevachim 11a" href="/Zevachim.11a">Babli <i>Zevaḥim</i> 11a</a>, <a class="refLink" data-ref="Tosefta Pesachim (Lieberman) 4:5" href="/Tosefta_Pesachim_(Lieberman).4.5">Tosephta <i>Pesaḥim</i> 4:5</a>.</i>” Since its time is passed, there is no difference whether he slaughtered a <i>Pesaḥ</i> for the purpose of a well-being sacrifice or he slaughtered a well-being sacrifice for the purpose of a <i>Pesaḥ.</i> In the opinion of Rav Ḥisda, if its year was completed between First and Second. In the opinion of Rebbi La in the name of Rebbi Joḥanan , when the time for its propitiation was passed<sup class="footnote-marker">183</sup><i class="footnote">Interpretations of: “<i>Pesaḥ</i> whose time had passed.”</i>.

Halakhah 5

<strong>MISHNAH:</strong> The <i>Pesaḥ</i> was being slaughtered in three groups, as it is said<sup class="footnote-marker">184</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Exodus 12:6" href="/Exodus.12.6"><i>Ex</i>. 12:6</a>.</i>, <i>and they shall slaughter it, the entire assembly of the community of Israel,</i> assembly, community, and Israel. When the first group entered, the courtyard was filled, they locked the doors of the courtyard. They<sup class="footnote-marker">185</sup><i class="footnote">The priests whose duty it was to blow horns for the daily sacrifice. “Straight” means an extended single tone.</i> blew the trumpets, straight, modulated, and straight. The priests were standing in rows<sup class="footnote-marker">186</sup><i class="footnote">The people went in with their lamb and stood in front of the priests, one priest per lamb.</i> and in their hands were silver and golden cups; one row only silver, one row only gold, they were not mixed. The cups had no flat bottoms lest they would be put down and the blood jellying<sup class="footnote-marker">187</sup><i class="footnote">That it could no longer be sprinkled on the wall of the altar.</i>.
<strong>HALAKHAH:</strong> <sup class="footnote-marker">188</sup><i class="footnote">A sermon, introducing the recitation of the “Egyptian Hallel”, <a class="refLink" data-ref="Psalms 113-118" href="/Psalms.113-118">Ps. 113–118</a>, in the Passover night celebration. Cf. the author’s <i>The Scholar’s Haggadah</i> p. 319; <a class="refLink" data-ref="Psalms 113:2" href="/Psalms.113.2"><i>Midrash Tehillim</i> 113(2</a>), <i>Mekhilta dR. Ismael Bo Parashah</i> 14.</i> Rebbi Jacob bar Aḥa in the name of Rebbi Yasa. Power was given to Moses’s voice and his voice went through the entire land of Egypt, a distance of 40 days of travel<sup class="footnote-marker">189</sup><i class="footnote">Or 400 Egyptian parasangs.</i>. What did he say? From place X to place Y one group, from place Z to place U one group. You should not be astonished. If about dust, which does not usually move, it is said<sup class="footnote-marker">190</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Exodus 9:9" href="/Exodus.9.9"><i>Ex</i>. 9:9</a>.</i>, <i>it will be</i><i>dust in the entire land of Egypt,</i> voice which usually is moving, not so much more? Rebbi Levi said, just as power was given to Moses’s voice, so power was given to Pharao’s voice, [and his voice went through the entire land of Egypt, a distance of forty days of travel.]<sup class="footnote-marker">191</sup><i class="footnote">Addition by the corrector, confirmed by K and Medieval sources.</i> What did he say? <i>Get up, leave from the midst of my people</i><sup class="footnote-marker">192</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Exodus 12:31" href="/Exodus.12.31"><i>Ex</i>. 12:31</a>. The argument is based on the part of the verse not quoted here, but quoted in K: <i>both you and the Children of Israel and go to serve the Eternal</i>.</i><i>.</i> In the past you were servants of Pharao, from now on you are servants of the Eternal. At that moment, they were saying<sup class="footnote-marker">193</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Psalms 113:1" href="/Psalms.113.1"><i>Ps</i>. 113:1</a>.</i>, <i>Hallelujah, give praise, servants of the Eternal,</i> but not servants of Pharao.
It was stated: For the daily sacrifice, which is accompanied by libations, one blows the trumpets for the libations<sup class="footnote-marker">194</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Mishnah Tamid 7:2" href="/Mishnah_Tamid.7.2">Mishnah <i>Tamid</i> 7:2</a>; <a class="refLink" data-ref="Numbers 10:10" href="/Numbers.10.10"><i>Num.</i> 10:10</a>.</i>. For the <i>Pesaḥ,</i> which has no libations, one blows the trumpets for its slaughter.
Explanation<sup class="footnote-marker">195</sup><i class="footnote">Greek δήλωμα; cf. <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Berakhot 1:1:21" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Berakhot.1.1.21"><i>Berakhot</i> 1:1 Note 72</a>.</i>. Rebbi Zeˋira, and Rebbi Jacob bar Aḥa, and Rebbi Abinna were sitting. Rebbi Abinna said, because of the tricksters<sup class="footnote-marker">196</sup><i class="footnote">The vessels in one row of Cohanim are all of the same metal lest a Cohen bring a silver vessel from home and substitute it for a gold vessel of the Temple.</i>. Rebbi Jacob bar Aḥa said to him, a mouthful<sup class="footnote-marker">197</sup><i class="footnote">It is insolent to suspect that holy priests would steal from the Temple. Accepted by the <a class="refLink" data-ref="Pesachim 64b" href="/Pesachim.64b">Babli, 64b</a>.</i>. Rebbi Zeˋira said to him, say it with half a mouthful. There came Rebbi Jeremiah in the name of Rebbi Joḥanan : because of the tricksters.

Halakhah 6

<strong>MISHNAH:</strong> The Israel slaughters<sup class="footnote-marker">198</sup><i class="footnote">If he so wishes since slaughter is permitted to everybody.</i> and the Cohen receives<sup class="footnote-marker">199</sup><i class="footnote">The blood; an action for which only priests are qualified.</i>; he hands it to his colleague and the colleague to his colleague; he accepts the full [cup] and returns the empty one<sup class="footnote-marker">200</sup><i class="footnote">So that one Cohen may serve many slaughterers.</i>. The Cohen standing next to the altar pours it in one pouring in the direction of the foundations<sup class="footnote-marker">201</sup><i class="footnote">Foundation stones extending one cubit outside the altar proper; <a class="refLink" data-ref="Mishnah Middot 3:1" href="/Mishnah_Middot.3.1">Mishnah <i>Middot</i> 3:1</a>.</i>.
<strong>HALAKHAH:</strong> One verse says<sup class="footnote-marker">202</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Numbers 18:17" href="/Numbers.18.17"><i>Num</i>. 18:17</a>.</i>, <i>but a firstling bull, or a firstling sheep, or a firstling goat, shall not be redeemed; holy they are; and their blood you shall pour on the altar.</i> Another verse says<sup class="footnote-marker">203</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Deuteronomy 12:27" href="/Deuteronomy.12.27"><i>Deut</i>. 12:27</a>.</i>, <i>and the blood of your sacrifices shall be spilled on the altar of the Eternal, your God.</i> If spilling, why pouring, and if pouring, why spilling? It was stated, <i>shall be spilled,</i> he may not let it fall in drips. <i>Shall be spilled,</i> he shall not sprinkle. <i>Shall be spilled,</i> he shall not pour. And it is explained in tradition<sup class="footnote-marker">204</sup><i class="footnote"><i>2 Chr</i>. 35:11.</i> that the priests pour the blood from the hands of the Levites. Everybody agrees on spilling how it is done; about sprinkling how it is done. Where do they disagree? About pouring. Rebbi Mana said, pouring is like spilling. Rebbi Ḥananiah said, pouring is like sprinkling. Rebbi Joḥanan bar Marius said, a verse supports Rebbi Ḥananiah: <i>For the throwing water was not poured on him, impure he shall be</i><sup class="footnote-marker">205</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Numbers 19:20" href="/Numbers.19.20"><i>Num.</i> 19:20</a>, about sprinkling with water containing ashes of the Red Cow. Cf. <i>Zevaḥim</i> 36b/37a.</i>, etc. Does he not talk about sprinkling and calls it pouring?

Halakhah 7

<strong>MISHNAH:</strong> When the first group left, the second entered; when the second left, the third entered. Like the arrangement for the first, so is the arrangement for second and third. They read the <i>Hallel</i><sup class="footnote-marker">206</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Psalms 113-118" href="/Psalms.113-118"><i>Ps.</i> 113–118</a>, sung by the Levites (cf. <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Pesachim 5:5:2" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Pesachim.5.5.2">Note 188</a>).</i>; when they finished they repeated, after they repeated they tripled, even though they never tripled. Rebbi Jehudah says, during the existence of a third group they never reached <i>I am loving; truly the Eternal listened to my voice</i><sup class="footnote-marker">207</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Psalms 116:1" href="/Psalms.116.1"><i>Ps.</i> 116:1</a></i><i>,</i> since its people were few.
<strong>HALAKHAH:</strong> <sup class="footnote-marker">208</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Taanit 3:11:1" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Taanit.3.11.1">Mishnah <i>Taˋaniot</i> 3:14</a>, about a fast in a year of drought which was cut short by rainfall. The text is Halakhah 3:14 in <i>Taˋaniot</i> (<b>ו</b>).</i> There, we have stated: “They went, ate, and drank. In the evening they returned and red the Great <i>Hallel.</i>” What is the Great <i>Hallel</i>? Rebbi Pamakh in the name of Rebbi Ḥaninah; <i>Give thanks to Almighty</i> God<sup class="footnote-marker">209</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Psalms 136" href="/Psalms.136"><i>Ps</i>. 136</a>. <a class="refLink" data-ref="Pesachim 118a" href="/Pesachim.118a">Babli 118a</a>.</i>. Rebbi Joḥanan said, on condition of <i>who stand in the Eternal’s house</i><sup class="footnote-marker">210</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Psalms 135" href="/Psalms.135"><i>Ps</i>. 135</a> as introduction to <a class="refLink" data-ref="Psalms 136" href="/Psalms.136">Ps. 136</a>.</i><i>.</i> Why these two chapters? Because rainfall is included in them. In the opinion of Rebbi Joḥanan it is understandable, for it is written<sup class="footnote-marker">211</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Psalms 135:7" href="/Psalms.135.7"><i>Ps</i>. 135:7</a>.</i>, <i>He brings up vapors from the ends of the earth.</i> How is it for Rebbi Ḥaninah? Because it is written<sup class="footnote-marker">212</sup><i class="footnote"><i>Ps</i>.136:25.</i>, <i>He gives nourishment to all flesh; Truly, His kindness is forever.</i> Rebbi Abba, Rebbi Simon, both are saying, ours<sup class="footnote-marker">213</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Psalms 113-118" href="/Psalms.113-118"><i>Ps</i>. 113–118</a>.</i>. Rebbi Joshua ben Levi said, ours. Bar Qappara said, ours. Bar Qappara follows his opinion, as it was stated: “during the existence of a third group they never reached <i>I am loving; truly the Eternal listened to my voice, my supplication,</i> since its people were few.” Bar Qappara stated, this is the Great Hallel. A patrician stood before the Ark<sup class="footnote-marker">214</sup><i class="footnote">To be the reader in a service of thanksgiving for rain relieving a drought.</i>; he said to them, repeat after me what I am saying. This implies that it is not ours<sup class="footnote-marker">215</sup><i class="footnote">If it were the regular <i>Hallel,</i> the congregation would not repeat the verses but answer every half-verse with “Hallelujah” (cf. <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Shabbat 16:1:7" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Shabbat.16.1.7"><i>Šabbat</i> 16, Note 59</a>).</i>. Rebbi Mana said, it is ours. The miracle was great; therefore he said to them, repeat after me what I am saying<sup class="footnote-marker">216</sup><i class="footnote">Because of the extraordinary nature of the event, he changed the usual response to repetition of the entire <i>Hallel.</i></i>.
It was stated: It was called the group of the lazy ones<sup class="footnote-marker">217</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Pesachim 65a" href="/Pesachim.65a">Babli 65a</a>.</i>. Rebbi Abun said, If in a case where the commandment is followed<sup class="footnote-marker">218</sup><i class="footnote">Since “between the evenings” implies that late afternoon is preferred.</i> it is called the group of the lazy ones, in a case one is lazy in fulfilling a commandment so much more.

Halakhah 8

<strong>MISHNAH:</strong> As it is done on weekdays it is done on the Sabbath, only that the priests rinse the courtyard against the wish of the Sages<sup class="footnote-marker">219</sup><i class="footnote">Between two groups entering the courtyard they were stopping the flow of the water canal passing through the courtyard to flood the stone floor and thereby cleansing it (<a class="refLink" data-ref="Tosefta Pesachim (Lieberman) 4:12" href="/Tosefta_Pesachim_(Lieberman).4.12">Tosephta 4:12</a>). This is a rabbinic Sabbath infraction.</i>. Rebbi Jehudah says, one was filling a cup of the mixture of blood<sup class="footnote-marker">220</sup><i class="footnote">Covering the floor.</i> and poured it in a single pouring on the altar, but the Sages did not agree with him.
<strong>HALAKHAH:</strong> Rebbi Jonathan said<sup class="footnote-marker">221</sup><i class="footnote">In <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Eruvin 10:11:2" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Eruvin.10.11.2"><i>Eruvin</i> 10 (Note 133</a>), the statement is in the name of the last generation R. Yose ben R. Abun instead of the first generation R. Jonathan. The statement explained why the inundating of the Temple courtyard was frowned upon by the pharisaic establishment.</i>, not every rabbinic Sabbath prohibition was permitted in the Temple. The priest would have sunk into the blood up to their knees<sup class="footnote-marker">222</sup><i class="footnote">This would have dirtied the priestly garments and made them unfit for service. The sweeping was necessary and therefore the displeasure of the Sages misplaced.</i>. How did they do it? They made them benches<sup class="footnote-marker">223</sup><i class="footnote">The priests stood on elevated benches above the accumulated blood. Since the priestly garments are enumerated in <a class="refLink" data-ref="Exodus 28" href="/Exodus.28"><i>Ex</i>. 28</a> and shoes are not mentioned there, the priests had to officiate barefoot, their feet touching the floor of the courtyard. Therefore one has to assume that the benches were rows of stones connected to the floor and counted as floor. <a class="refLink" data-ref="Pesachim 65b" href="/Pesachim.65b">Babli 65b</a>.</i>.
There, we have stated<sup class="footnote-marker">224</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Mishnah Keritot 5:1" href="/Mishnah_Keritot.5.1">Mishnah <i>Keritut</i> 5:1</a>.</i>: “Rebbi Jehudah declares liable for squeezed blood<sup class="footnote-marker">225</sup><i class="footnote">If an animal is slaughtered by having its throat cut, the blood pumped out from the carotid arteries by the heart is called “life blood”; all other blood is “squeezed out” blood unfit for sacrificial use. For the majority, all blood is prohibited (<a class="refLink" data-ref="Leviticus 7:23" href="/Leviticus.7.23"><i>Lev.</i> 7:23</a>) but only life blood is forbidden on penalty of extirpation (<a class="refLink" data-ref="Leviticus 17:10" href="/Leviticus.17.10"><i>Lev.</i> 17:10</a>). R. Jehudah disagrees since life blood is mentioned only in <a class="refLink" data-ref="Leviticus 17:11" href="/Leviticus.17.11">v. 17:11</a>.</i>.” Rebbi Joḥanan said, Rebbi Jehudah added it only for extirpation<sup class="footnote-marker">226</sup><i class="footnote">He agrees that only life blood is qualified for the altar.</i>. There came Rebbi Ḥizqiah, Rebbi Abbahu in the name of Rebbi Joḥanan: Rebbi Jehudah added it only for extirpation. There<sup class="footnote-marker">227</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Tosefta Pesachim (Lieberman) 4:12" href="/Tosefta_Pesachim_(Lieberman).4.12">Tosephta 4:12</a>; <a class="refLink" data-ref="Pesachim 65a" href="/Pesachim.65a">Babli 65a</a>, <a class="refLink" data-ref="Zevachim 34b" href="/Zevachim.34b"><i>Zevaḥim</i>34b</a>, <a class="refLink" data-ref="Zevachim 60a" href="/Zevachim.60a">60a</a>.</i>, they are saying in the name of Rav Ḥisda: a <i>baraita</i><sup class="footnote-marker">227</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Tosefta Pesachim (Lieberman) 4:12" href="/Tosefta_Pesachim_(Lieberman).4.12">Tosephta 4:12</a>; <a class="refLink" data-ref="Pesachim 65a" href="/Pesachim.65a">Babli 65a</a>, <a class="refLink" data-ref="Zevachim 34b" href="/Zevachim.34b"><i>Zevaḥim</i>34b</a>, <a class="refLink" data-ref="Zevachim 60a" href="/Zevachim.60a">60a</a>.</i> says so: “They said to him, is that not squeezed blood? And squeezed blood is disqualified on the altar<sup class="footnote-marker">228</sup><i class="footnote">As explained at the end of the paragraph.</i>. And also from the following, most of it was not received in a vessel, and blood not received in a vessel is disqualified on the altar<sup class="footnote-marker">229</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Mishnah Zevachim 2:1" href="/Mishnah_Zevachim.2.1">Mishnah <i>Zevaḥim</i> 2:1</a>.</i>.” Does Rebbi Jehudah hold that blood invalidates blood<sup class="footnote-marker">230</sup><i class="footnote">In <a class="refLink" data-ref="Mishnah Zevachim 8:6" href="/Mishnah_Zevachim.8.6">Mishnah <i>Zevaḥim</i> 8:6</a>, R. Jehudah is quoted as saying that no blood invalidates blood. Therefore if only a small portion of the blood collected in the cup was qualified, the remainder is disregarded and the entire contents can be poured on the altar.</i>? Since he did not reply, it follows that he accepted their position<sup class="footnote-marker">231</sup><i class="footnote">A possible interpretation of the Mishnah here.</i>. Since in the other case he does not hold so but did not respond, so here he does not hold so but did not respond<sup class="footnote-marker">232</sup><i class="footnote">Since we know that R. Jehudah holds that no blood invalidates blood and he is not reported to have answered the argument in the Tosephta, nothing can be inferred from his silence in the Mishnah.</i>. Rebbi Yose ben Rebbi Abun in the name of Rav Ḥisda: a <i>baraita</i><sup class="footnote-marker">223</sup><i class="footnote">The priests stood on elevated benches above the accumulated blood. Since the priestly garments are enumerated in <a class="refLink" data-ref="Exodus 28" href="/Exodus.28"><i>Ex</i>. 28</a> and shoes are not mentioned there, the priests had to officiate barefoot, their feet touching the floor of the courtyard. Therefore one has to assume that the benches were rows of stones connected to the floor and counted as floor. <a class="refLink" data-ref="Pesachim 65b" href="/Pesachim.65b">Babli 65b</a>.</i> says so: “Not only life blood for <i>sancta,</i> matter appropriate for atonement, from where life blood for profane animals and squeezed blood for both <i>sancta</i> and profane animals? The verse says <i>blood</i> and <i>all blood.</i> When it is about life it mentions atonement, for squeezed blood it does not mention atonement<sup class="footnote-marker">234</sup><i class="footnote">This is R. Jehudah’s argument. In <a class="refLink" data-ref="Leviticus 17:10" href="/Leviticus.17.10"><i>Lev.</i>17:10</a> <i>all blood</i> is prohibited under penalty of extirpation. In <a class="refLink" data-ref="Leviticus 17:11" href="/Leviticus.17.11"><i>Lev.</i> 17:11</a> <i>blood</i> is the carrier of life, showing that life blood used for atonement is less than <i>all blood.</i> <a class="refLink" data-ref="Pesachim 65a" href="/Pesachim.65a">Babli 65a</a>.</i>.

Halakhah 9

<strong>MISHNAH:</strong> How does one hang and skins<sup class="footnote-marker">235</sup><i class="footnote">The <i>Pesaḥ</i> has to be roasted whole; for this it has to be skinned. For this purpose the carcass it hung on its hind feet and stripped from there to the head. This has to be done in the Temple enclosue since the required innards have to be burned on the altar and sacrificial meat which leaves the Temple precinct becomes disqualified for the altar.</i>? Iron hooks<sup class="footnote-marker">236</sup><i class="footnote">Greek ἀγκύλη, ἡ.</i> were fixed in the walls and on the pillars where one hangs and skins. For anybody who does not find a place to hang and skin there were thin smooth rods; he puts one on his shoulder and another’s shoulder, and hangs and skins. Rebbi Eliezer says, if the Fourteenth falls on a Sabbath, he puts his arm on another’s shoulder who puts his arm on the first person’s shoulder<sup class="footnote-marker">237</sup><i class="footnote">Since he holds that the rods are <i>muqṣeh</i> and may not be used on the Sabbath.</i>, and hangs and skins.
<strong>HALAKHAH:</strong> Rebbi Zeˋira in the name of Rebbi Eleazar: Half-pipes and rods were stated before the permission of vessels<sup class="footnote-marker">238</sup><i class="footnote">This is quoted from <i>Šabbat</i> 17 (Notes 32,33), <a class="refLink" data-ref="Shabbat 123b" href="/Shabbat.123b">Babli <i>Šabbat</i> 123b</a>. The half-pipes mentioned in <a class="refLink" data-ref="Mishnah Menachot 11:6" href="/Mishnah_Menachot.11.6">Mishnah<i>Menaḥot</i> 11:6</a> which separate between the loaves of the shew-bread, where it is mentioned that they cannot be removed or put in on the Sabbath. This clearly contradicts <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Shabbat 17:1:1" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Shabbat.17.1.1">Mishnah <i>Šabbat</i> 17:1</a> which declares that all implements may be moved on the Sabbath.<br>The rods are mentioned here. In view of <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Shabbat 17:1:1" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Shabbat.17.1.1">Mishnah <i>Šabbat</i> 17:1</a> there is no reason not to use the rods on the Sabbath. It would be easy to say that practice does not follow R. Eliezer, but since he is a very reliable historical source there can be no doubt that he accurately reports Temple practice from his own experience. One has to conclude that the general permission to use all implements (with the exception of expensive tools of trade) has to be dated to the council of Jabneh after the destruction of the Second Temple.</i>.

Halakhah 10

<strong>MISHNAH:</strong> He tears it open and removes the parts<sup class="footnote-marker">50</sup><i class="footnote">Greek αἱ μοῖραι [τοῦ θεοῦ], the fat which is forbidden for human consumption.</i> which he<sup class="footnote-marker">239</sup><i class="footnote">The officiating priest.</i> puts in a tureen and burns on the altar. The first group left and sat on the Temple Mount<sup class="footnote-marker">240</sup><i class="footnote">According to Rashi and Maimonides, this refers only to a Sabbath, when they could not carry outside the enclosure of the Temple Mount.</i>, the second within the inner wall of the Temple Mount, the third stood<sup class="footnote-marker">241</sup><i class="footnote">Being inside the sacred district, they could not sit down.</i> at its place. When it got dark, they left and roasted their <i>Pesaḥ.</i>
<strong>HALAKHAH:</strong> It is written, <i>he sprinkled from it</i><sup class="footnote-marker">242</sup><i class="footnote">There is no verse like this; probably what is meant is <a class="refLink" data-ref="Leviticus 8:11" href="/Leviticus.8.11"><i>Lev.</i> 8:11</a>: וַיַּז֥ מִמֶּ֛נּוּ. Cf. <a class="refLink" data-ref="Bekhorot 39b" href="/Bekhorot.39b">Babli <i>Bekhorot</i> 39b</a>.</i>, from its entirety. Rebbi Abuna said, only from a complete sacrifice. <sup class="footnote-marker">243</sup><i class="footnote"><i>Sifra Wayyiqra I Parsheta</i> 14(10).</i>“It is written, <i>they shall burn it, and he shall burn it, and he shall burn them</i><sup class="footnote-marker">244</sup><i class="footnote">The three expressions, from <a class="refLink" data-ref="Leviticus 3:5" href="/Leviticus.3.5"><i>Lev</i>. 3:5</a>, <a class="refLink" data-ref="Leviticus 3:11" href="/Leviticus.3.11">3:11</a>, <a class="refLink" data-ref="Leviticus 3:16" href="/Leviticus.3.16">3:16</a>, all refer to well-being sacrifices, the first of cattle, the second of sheep, the third of goats. All three expressions are taken to refer to all three kinds, each one implying a different rule.</i>. Why does the verse say <i>they shall burn it,</i> the qualified, not the disqualified<sup class="footnote-marker">245</sup><i class="footnote">Since “it” is expressed by a separate word, it is for emphasis: This one but not one which does not follow the rules.</i>. <i>And he shall burn it,</i> that he may not mix fat with fat. <i>And he shall burn them,</i> all of them together.” Here you are saying, <i>and he shall burn it,</i> that he may not mix fat with fat; and there you are saying, <i>and he shall burn them,</i> all of them together. Rebbi La said, here in the tureen, there on the top of the altar<sup class="footnote-marker">246</sup><i class="footnote">Once the priest has started, he may not stop before all parts lifted from one animal are burned.</i>.
Did not Rebbi Ḥiyya state, “nobody could sit in the Temple courtyard except kings of the Davidic dynasty”<sup class="footnote-marker">247</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Yoma 25a" href="/Yoma.25a">Babli <i>Yoma</i> 25a</a>,<a class="refLink" data-ref="Yoma 69b" href="/Yoma.69b">69b</a>, <a class="refLink" data-ref="Sotah 40a" href="/Sotah.40a"><i>Soṭah</i> 40a</a>, <a class="refLink" data-ref="Tamid 27a" href="/Tamid.27a"><i>Tamid</i> 27a</a>, <a class="refLink" data-ref="Sanhedrin 101b" href="/Sanhedrin.101b"><i>Sanhedrin</i> 101b</a>; <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Yoma 3:2:2-7" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Yoma.3.2.2-7">Yerushalmi <i>Yoma</i> 3:2</a>, <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Sotah 7:7:2-3" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Sotah.7.7.2-3"><i>Soṭah</i> 7:7</a>.</i>? And Rebbi Immi said in the name of Rebbi Simeon ben Laqish, even the kings of the Davidic dynasty could not sit in the Temple courtyard. Explain it that he leaned on the wall as if sitting. But is it not written, <i>King David came and sat before the Eternal</i><sup class="footnote-marker">248</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="I Chronicles 17:16" href="/I_Chronicles.17.16"><i>1Chr</i>. 17:16</a>.</i>, etc.? Rebbi Ayvo bar Naggari said, he concentrated<sup class="footnote-marker">249</sup><i class="footnote">Since in Mishnaic Hebrew יִשׂוּב דַּעַת means “concentration”.</i> for prayer.
“The first group left and sat on the Temple Mount, the second within the inner wall of the Temple Mount, the third at its place.” Rebbi Naḥman in the name of Rebbi Mana: Did we state “sat at its place”? “Stood at its place<sup class="footnote-marker">250</sup><i class="footnote">The preceding paragraph explains why the third group is required to stand.<br>The text implies that the reading in the Mishnah was simply שְׁלִישִׁית בִּמְקוֹמָהּ “the third at its place.”</i>”.

Chapter 6



Halakhah 1

<strong>MISHNAH:</strong> The following items about the <i>Pesaḥ</i> push aside the Sabbath<sup class="footnote-marker">1</sup><i class="footnote">If the 14th of Nisan falls on a Sabbath.</i>: Its slaughter, and the pouring of its blood, and emptying its intestines<sup class="footnote-marker">2</sup><i class="footnote">Cleaning out the bowels so the carcass will not start to smell before nightfall when it can be roasted.</i>, and the burning of its fat. But its roasting and washing of its intestines<sup class="footnote-marker">3</sup><i class="footnote">To clean them thoroughly to prepare them as food.</i> do not push aside. Carrying it<sup class="footnote-marker">4</sup><i class="footnote">Carrying the lamb on one’s shoulder.</i>, or bringing it from outside the Sabbath domain, or cutting its wart<sup class="footnote-marker">5</sup><i class="footnote">Since a wart is a defect which disqualifies an animal as sacrifice (<a class="refLink" data-ref="Leviticus 22:22" href="/Leviticus.22.22"><i>Lev</i>. 22:22</a>), the animal could not have been dedicated if it had developed one by the time of dedication. If it was dedicated without defect, a wart which developed later may be cut.</i>, do not push aside; Rebbi Eliezer says, they push aside<sup class="footnote-marker">6</sup><i class="footnote">He holds that if an action supersedes the rules of the Sabbath, all preparatory actions also supersede the Sabbath (<i>Šabbat</i> 19:1).</i>.
<strong>HALAKHAH:</strong> “The following items about the <i>Pesaḥ</i>,” etc. <sup class="footnote-marker">7</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Pesachim 66a" href="/Pesachim.66a">Babli 66a</a>; <a class="refLink" data-ref="Tosefta Pesachim (Lieberman) 4:13-14" href="/Tosefta_Pesachim_(Lieberman).4.13-14">Tosephta 4:13–14</a>.</i> This question left the Elders of Bathyra at a loss. Once the Fourteenth fell on the Sabbath and they did not know whether <i>Pesaḥ</i> pushes aside the Sabbath or not. They said, we have here a Babylonian who served Shemaya and Avtalion<sup class="footnote-marker">8</sup><i class="footnote">The heads of the Pharisaic establishment in the preceding generation.</i> and knows whether <i>Pesaḥ</i> pushes aside the Sabbath or not. It is possible that there be hope from him. They sent and called him. The said to him, did you ever hear, if the Fourteenth falls on the Sabbath, whether <i>Pesaḥ</i> pushes aside the Sabbath or not? He told them, do we have only one <i>Pesaḥ</i> which pushes aside the Sabbath every year? Are there not many <i>Pesaḥim</i> which push aside the Sabbath every year? There are Tannaim who state: 100. There are Tannaim who state: 200. There are Tannaim who state: 300. He who says 100, the daily sacrifices of the Sabbath. He who says 200, the daily and additional sacrifices of the Sabbath. He who says 300, the daily and additional sacrifices of the Sabbath, and of holidays, and of New Moons, and of semi-holidays. They told him, already we said, there is hope from you. He started to explain to them by analogy, by an argument <i>de minore ad majus,</i> and by equal cut. By analogy: The daily sacrifice is a public offering and <i>Pesaḥ</i> is a public offering. Since the daily sacrifice as a public offering pushes aside the Sabbath, also <i>Pesaḥ</i> as a public offering pushes aside the Sabbath. By an argument <i>de minore ad majus.</i> Since the daily sacrifice, whose action is not subject to extirpation, pushes aside the Sabbath, it is only logical that <i>Pesaḥ,</i> whose action is subject to extirpation, push aside the Sabbath. By equal cut. It is said about the daily sacrifice, <i>at its fixed time</i><sup class="footnote-marker">9</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Numbers 28:2" href="/Numbers.28.2"><i>Num</i>. 28:2</a>.</i>, and it is said about <i>Pesaḥ, at its fixed time</i><sup class="footnote-marker">10</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Numbers 9:2" href="/Numbers.9.2"><i>Num</i>. 9:2</a>.</i>. They said to him, we already said, is there hope from a Babylonian? The analogy which you proposed can be answered. No, if you said this about daily sacrifices which are fixed in number, what can you infer for <i>Pesaḥ</i> which is not fixed in number? The argument <i>de minore ad majus</i> which you proposed can be answered. No, if you said this about daily sacrifices which are most holy, what can you infer for <i>Pesaḥ</i> which is a simple sacrifice<sup class="footnote-marker">11</sup><i class="footnote">The relationship between daily sacrifice and <i>Pesaḥ</i> is not that of minor and major; the argument is intrinsically invalid.</i>? Concerning the equal cut which you proposed, nobody can introduce an equal cut by himself<sup class="footnote-marker">12</sup><i class="footnote">Equal expressions in the Pentateuch imply equal legal status only if there is a documented tradition that these words were written for this purpose. <a class="refLink" data-ref="Pesachim 66a" href="/Pesachim.66a">Babli 66a</a>.</i>.
<sup class="footnote-marker">13</sup><i class="footnote">Here a Genizah fragment (<i>Ginze Schechter</i> pp. 446–447) becomes readable again (<b>ג</b>).</i> Rebbi Yose ben Rebbi Abun said in the name of Rebbi Abba bar Mamal: If a person could construct an equal cut by himself, he could make a creeping animal causing impurity in a tent and a corpse causing impurity in the volume of a lentil, by explaining <i>textile, leather; textile, leather</i><sup class="footnote-marker">14</sup><i class="footnote">A dead creeping animal (of the list <a class="refLink" data-ref="Leviticus 11:29-30" href="/Leviticus.11.29-30"><i>Lev</i>. 11:29–30</a>) imparts impurity in the volume of a lentil; a human corpse only in the volume of an olive. A human corpse imparts impurity to everything under the same roof with it, a dead creeping one imparts impurity only by contact. The argument is incomprehensible but the text is confirmed not only by ג but also by <i>Sefer Hapardes</i> from the school of Rashi (<i>Pardes Gadol</i> §175, ed. H. L. Ehrenreich p. 230), and <i>Meïri Pesaḥim</i> (ed. Y. Klein, col. 290a). While <i>textile</i> <i>and</i> <i>leather</i> are written about the creeping animal in <a class="refLink" data-ref="Leviticus 11:32" href="/Leviticus.11.32"><i>Lev</i>. 11:32</a>, they are not mentioned in the Chapter about tent impurity (<a class="refLink" data-ref="Numbers 19" href="/Numbers.19"><i>Num</i>. 19</a>). It is mentioned in the Chapter about <i>ṣāraˋ</i> at impurity of textiles (<a class="refLink" data-ref="Leviticus 13:47-59" href="/Leviticus.13.47-59"><i>Lev</i>. 13:47–59</a>) although not in the exact wording of 11:32. The argument should be that the equal cut is illegitimate since minimal sizes for impurity of animals are determined by volume while those of textiles by surface area; the rules cannot be transferred.</i>. So if a creeping animal is in a person’s hand, even if he immerses himself in the waters of the Siloam, or in waters of a primeval ocean, he never can achieve purity. If he throws it away, immediately he becomes pure<sup class="footnote-marker">15</sup><i class="footnote">This argument does not belong here, it is not in ג, nor in <i>Pardes</i>, nor in Meïri. It is part of a sermon in <i>Taˋanti</i> (Yerushalmi 2:1 69a line 69, <a class="refLink" data-ref="Pesachim 16a" href="/Pesachim.16a">Babli 16a</a>.)</i>. Rebbi Yose ben Rebbi Abun in the name of Rebbi Abba bar Mamal: A person may use an equal cut to confirm what he has learned; nobody may use an equal cut to invalidate what he has learned<sup class="footnote-marker">16</sup><i class="footnote">Since it is part of oral tradition.</i>. Rebbi Yose ben Rebbi Abun in the name of Rebbi Abba bar Mamal: A person may argue <i>de minore ad majus</i> by himself; a person may not argue an equal cut by himself<sup class="footnote-marker">16</sup><i class="footnote">Since it is part of oral tradition.</i>. Therefore one can contradict an argument <i>de minore ad majus</i>; one cannot contradict an equal cut.
Even though he was sitting and explaining the entire day they did not accept it from him until he said, it should come over me, so I heard from Shemaya and Avtalion. When they heard this from him, they rose and appointed him Patriarch over them. After they had appointed him Patriarch over them, he started to goad<sup class="footnote-marker">16*</sup><i class="footnote">Greek κεντρόω “to spur, goad, hit with a sharp instrument”.</i> them with words, and said: What caused you to need this Babylonian? Not that you did not serve the two greats of the world, Shemaya and Avtalion? When he started to goad them with words, practice disappeared from him.
<sup class="footnote-marker">17</sup><i class="footnote">This is copied from <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Shabbat 19:1:9-10" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Shabbat.19.1.9-10"><i>Šabbat</i> 19, Notes 59–66</a>, where readings are noted and the text is explained. While the text fits in here, its origin is in <i>Šabbat</i> since the disagreement between R. Immi and R. Simon mentioned in the paragraph does not refer to anything discussed here.</i> They said to him: What to do with people who did not bring their knives with them? He told them, I was informed of the practice, but I forgot. But let Israel act; if they are not prophets they are descendants of prophets. Then everybody whose Passover sacrifice was a lamb stuck them in its fleece, for a kid goat he bound them to its horns; it turned out that the Passover sacrifices brought their knives with them. When he saw the action he remembered the practice. He told them, this is what I heard from Shemaya and Avtalion.
Rebbi Zeˋira in the name of Rebbi Eleazar. Any teaching which has no pedigree is no teaching. There, we have stated<sup class="footnote-marker">18</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Mishnah Parah 2:3" href="/Mishnah_Parah.2.3">Mishnah <i>Parah</i> 2:3</a>. The text in parentheses was added by the corrector from the Mishnah.</i>: “If he rode on it, leaned on it, hung on it, used it to cross a river, folded the bridle on it, put his toga on it, it is disqualified. [But if he tied it with the bridle, made it a shoe lest it slip, put his toga on it because of flies, it is qualified. This is the principle: Anything for its needs, it is qualified. For any other need, it is disqualified.]” This learns from that and that learns from this. This learns from that that if he hung on it a knife to slaughter it it remains qualified. That learns from this, that any action which is done for <i>sancta</i> is not work. Why did they not allow it to them by means of walls of people? It must follow Rebbi Immi. Even if you are saying following Rebbi Simon, just as they could not remember this so they did not remember that. Rebbi Abun said, but it is impossible that in two Sabbatical periods there should be no 14<sup>th</sup> which falls on the Sabbath! How could they not have remembered? To confer greatness on Hillel.
Rebbi Mana said, I heard from Rebbi Yudan and from all the rabbis, why does one honor the lower house<sup class="footnote-marker">19</sup><i class="footnote">Following <b>ג</b>, we read “the earthly House”, meaning the Patriarchate (as recognized by L. Ginzberg), not “the earthly court”. While Hillel became Patriarch because of his intellectual stature, in Talmudic times the descendants of Rebbi were no longer the leading scholars. The question then is asked, why they should retain their status as Patriarchs. They are needed since their pronouncements can guarantee unity of practice in Judaism.</i>? So that divisions should not grow in Israel. Three put down their crowns in this world and inherited the life of the Future World. And these are: Jonathan the son of Saul, and Eleazar ben Azariah, and the Elders of Bathyra. Jonathan the son of Saul. Rebbi La said, even the women behind the loom<sup class="footnote-marker">20</sup><i class="footnote">Greek καῖρος, ό.</i> did know that David would rule in the future. Eleazar ben Azaria was Second in rank<sup class="footnote-marker">21</sup><i class="footnote">While he volunteered to re-establish Rabban Gamliel as Patriarch (<a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Berakhot 4:1:33" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Berakhot.4.1.33"><i>Berakhot</i> 4:1 Notes 114–124</a>). <b>ג</b> reads “there was a stipulation,” that he would remain Chief Justice if Rabban Gamliel was re-instated as Patriarch.</i>. There are among these only the Elders of Bathyra who freed themselves of the Patriarchate and appointed him Patriarch. The rabbis of Caesarea said, also Rebbi Ḥanina of Sepphoris for Rebbi Mana. Rebbi Joshua ben Qabusai<sup class="footnote-marker">22</sup><i class="footnote">Since the name tradition is not uniform, it cannot be determined who exactly was the person referred to.</i> said, all my days I fled from authority. Now that I entered, anybody who would remove me I would treat like a water kettle. As the kettle burns, and injures, and chars, so I would treat him. Rebbi Yose ben Rebbi Bun said, heaven forbid that he wanted this. But he said, who could tell me that he would sanctify the Name of Heaven as I am doing.
Because of three questions Hillel immigrated from Babylonia. <i>He is pure.</i> I could think that he was rid of it and may take leave, the verse says, <i>the Cohen shall declare him pure.</i> If <i>the Cohen shall declare him pure</i> then I could think that if the Cohen declared him pure while he was impure that he was pure, the verse says, <i>he is pure and the Cohen shall declare him pure</i><sup class="footnote-marker">23</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Leviticus 13:37" href="/Leviticus.13.37"><i>Lev</i>. 13:37</a>.</i>. For this Hillel immigrated from Babylonia<sup class="footnote-marker">24</sup><i class="footnote"><i>Sifra Tazriaˋ Pereq</i> 9(15).</i>.
One verse says<sup class="footnote-marker">25</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Deuteronomy 16:2" href="/Deuteronomy.16.2"><i>Deut</i>. 16:2</a>.</i>, <i>you shall sacrifice a Pesaḥ to the Eternal, your God, small cattle and large cattle.</i> Another verse says<sup class="footnote-marker">26</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Exodus 12:5" href="/Exodus.12.5"><i>Ex</i>. 12:5</a>.</i>,<i>from sheep and goats you shall take.</i> How is this? Small cattle for <i>Pesaḥ,</i> small and large cattle for the festival sacrifice<sup class="footnote-marker">27</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Pesachim 70b" href="/Pesachim.70b">Babli 70b</a>, <i>Sifry Deut</i>. 129, not in the name of Hillel.</i>.
One verse says<sup class="footnote-marker">28</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Deuteronomy 16:8" href="/Deuteronomy.16.8"><i>Deut</i>. 16:8</a>.</i>, <i>you shall eat mazzot for six days;</i> another verse says<sup class="footnote-marker">29</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Exodus 12:5" href="/Exodus.12.5"><i>Ex</i>. 12:5</a>.</i>, <i>seven days you shall eat mazzot.</i> How is this? Six days from the new crop<sup class="footnote-marker">30</sup><i class="footnote">After the <i>Omer</i> ceremony on the second day of the Holiday of Unleavened Bread, when grain from the new harvest becomes permitted (<a class="refLink" data-ref="Leviticus 23:14" href="/Leviticus.23.14"><i>Lev.</i> 23:14</a>). <i>Sifry Deut.</i> 134 in the name of R. Simeon, 5 generations after Hillel; <i>Mekhilta dR. Ismael Bo, Parašah</i> 8, anonymous.</i>, seven days from the old. He interpreted, and agreed, and immigrated, and received practice<sup class="footnote-marker">31</sup><i class="footnote">He had found the solutions himself; he immigrated into Palestine to have his explanations accepted by Shemaya and Avtalion and to have it harmonized with existing practice.</i>.
“Emptying its intestines”. Rebbi Joḥanan said, <i>all the Eternal’s works are for Himself</i><sup class="footnote-marker">32</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Proverbs 16:4" href="/Proverbs.16.4"><i>Prov.</i> 16:4</a>. Quoted <a class="refLink" data-ref="Shabbat 116b" href="/Shabbat.116b">Babli <i>Šabbat</i>116b</a>.</i>; that it should not look as if he took the parts from a disgusting sacrifice<sup class="footnote-marker">33</sup><i class="footnote">Since for profane use the emptying of the intestines would be a Sabbath violation.</i>. Rebbi Ismael stated, its skinning pushes the Sabbath aside<sup class="footnote-marker">34</sup><i class="footnote">But for profane use it would be a Sabbath violation.</i>. It was stated: Rebbi Ismael the son of Rebbi Joḥanan ben Beroqa says, on the Sabbath one was skinning the breast<sup class="footnote-marker">35</sup><i class="footnote">With <a class="refLink" data-ref="Tosefta Pesachim (Lieberman) 4" href="/Tosefta_Pesachim_(Lieberman).4">Tosephta 4</a>:10 one has to read: “One was skinning up to the breast (starting with the feet).”</i>. What is Rebbi Ismael’s reason? That it should not look as if he took the parts from a disgusting sacrifice. What does Rebbi Ismael the son of Rebbi Joḥanan ben Beroqa do with this? Because he turns it around, it is not as if he was taking the parts from a disgusting sacrifice<sup class="footnote-marker">36</sup><i class="footnote">Since it is obvious that one skins from the feet for sacrificial use, it is not necessary to push aside the Sabbath more than a minimum.</i>. Rebbi Joḥanan said, Rebbi Ismael and Rebbi Ismael the son of Rebbi Joḥanan ben Beroqa said the same. As Rebbi Ismael said, choice pushes aside but choicest does not push aside<sup class="footnote-marker">37</sup><i class="footnote">In <a class="refLink" data-ref="Mishnah Menachot 6:1" href="/Mishnah_Menachot.6.1">Mishnah <i>Menaḥot</i> 6:1</a>, R. Ismael states that while on a Sabbath the <i>ˋOmer</i>(3/10 of a <i>seah</i>) of barley flour was sifted from three <i>seah</i> of grain while on weekdays it was from five. This implies that for the Temple service one uses choice material but only on weekdays it must be of the choicest kind if it is a matter of pushing aside Sabbath prohibitions.</i>, so Rebbi Ismael the son of Rebbi Joḥanan ben Beroqa said choice pushes aside but choicest does not push aside. If you are saying, this is choice, can he not tear it open and remove the parts<sup class="footnote-marker">38</sup><i class="footnote">If we interpret R. Ismael ben R. Joḥanan ben Beroqa in this way, then R. Ismael would be inconsistent by requiring total stripping of the <i>Pesaḥ.</i> Also R. Ismael ben R. Joḥanan ben Beroqa could obtain the desired result with much less Sabbath desecration. Therefore R. Joḥanan’s statement cannot be correct.</i>? Rebbi Yose ben Rebbi Abun said, it only follows Rebbi Simeon.
<sup class="footnote-marker">39</sup><i class="footnote">This is from <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Shabbat 12:1:7" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Shabbat.12.1.7"><i>Šabbat</i> 12, Notes 47–49</a>.</i> as it was stated<sup class="footnote-marker">7</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Pesachim 66a" href="/Pesachim.66a">Babli 66a</a>; <a class="refLink" data-ref="Tosefta Pesachim (Lieberman) 4:13-14" href="/Tosefta_Pesachim_(Lieberman).4.13-14">Tosephta 4:13–14</a>.</i>: “One who scratches, who drills, who chops anything is liable; Rebbi Simeon ben Eleazar says, one who scratches only if he scratches completely, one who drills only if he drills completely, one who chops only if he chopped completely, one who tans hides only if he tanned completely.” And Rebbi Jacob bar Ada said, this only follows Rebbi Simeon since Rebbi Simeon did not treat partial work as whole work, but the rabbis do treat partial work as whole work<sup class="footnote-marker">40</sup><i class="footnote">Therefore R. Ismael ben R. Joḥanan ben Beroqa disagrees with R. Ismael and holds that skinning the <i>Pesaḥ</i> on the Sabbath is forbidden as action for profane use; he only permits partial skinning since for him it is not a Sabbath desecration. Cf. <i>Menaḥot</i>63b–64a.</i>.
<sup class="footnote-marker">41</sup><i class="footnote">This paragraph, continuation of the preceding one, is copied from <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Shabbat 12:1:8-3:5" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Shabbat.12.1.8-3.5"><i>Šabbat</i> 12, Notes 50–53</a>; it refers to <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Shabbat 12:1:1" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Shabbat.12.1.1">Mishnah <i>Šabbat</i> 12:1</a> and has no meaning here.</i> And it is difficult about Rabban Simeon ben Gamliel. If one took [tools] to harvest but did not harvest, is that perhaps anything? Rebbi Ada said, Rabban Simeon ben Gamliel parallels Rebbi Jehudah, as it was stated: “One who hits or smooths a piece of weaving is liable. He is liable because he equalizes with his hand.” And here because he equalizes with his hand.
<sup class="footnote-marker">42</sup><i class="footnote">This paragraph also appears word for word in <i>Roš Haššanah</i> 1:1 (56c l. 13), which seems to be the original source.</i>“And the burning of its fat.” <i>The fat of my holiday offering shall not stay until the morning</i><sup class="footnote-marker">43</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Exodus 23:18" href="/Exodus.23.18"><i>Ex.</i> 23:18</a>. The first part of the verse is about slaughtering the <i>Pesaḥ</i> (<a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Pesachim 5:4:3" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Pesachim.5.4.3">Chapter 5, Note 130</a>). The second part quoted here explicitly mentions the holiday offering, the required family sacrifice on the occasion of the holiday pilgrimage, but is interpreted to include the fat of the <i>Pesaḥ.</i></i>. But could parts from weekday be brought on a holiday<sup class="footnote-marker">44</sup><i class="footnote">Since the 15th of Nisan is a holiday, it seems obvious that parts of a sacrifice brought on the 14th have to be burned before the start of the holiday; the verse seems to be meaningless.</i>? Rebbi Abbahu said, I confirmed it, if the Fourteenth fell on a Šabbath. Rebbi Jonah asked, if the Fourteenth fell on a Šabbath, no holiday offering comes with it, that the Torah has to say, bring it to the altar when it is still daylight lest it come to “not stay”<sup class="footnote-marker">45</sup><i class="footnote">Even if we restrict the meaning of the sentence to holiday offerings, since there is none if the 14th falls on a Sabbath, the explanation of R. Abbahu seems pointless.</i>? (And here, bring it to the altar when it is still daylight lest it come to “not tarry”<sup class="footnote-marker">46</sup><i class="footnote">This sentence, referring to <a class="refLink" data-ref="Deuteronomy 23:22" href="/Deuteronomy.23.22"><i>Deut.</i> 23:22</a>, belongs to <i>Roš Haššanah</i> and has no meaning here.</i>.) Rebbi Ḥinena said, if he transgressed and brought, is it not qualified<sup class="footnote-marker">47</sup><i class="footnote">This argument that a holiday offering, brought in error on the 14th which is a Sabbath, is qualified and the person who brought it is not liable for a Sabbath infraction, is not found in the Babli and the surviving Tosephta mss.; it is quoted as R. Meïr’s opinion in the Tosephta of the Bomberg Babli, 5:4.</i>? Since it is qualified if he transgressed and brought, he would transgress<sup class="footnote-marker">48</sup><i class="footnote">If one brings a holiday offering on a 14th which is a Sabbath, the explanation of R. Abbahu applies. The verse is not meaningless.</i>.
“But its roasting, and washing of its intestines, do not push aside.” We have stated, “When it got dark, they left and roasted their <i>Pesaḥ</i>”, and you are saying so? For hanging into the oven<sup class="footnote-marker">49</sup><i class="footnote">In Mishnah <i>Šabbat</i> 1:15 roasting the <i>Pesaḥ</i> on the Sabbath is permitted if the 14th is a Friday. Why is it prohibited if the 14th is a Sabbath? The roasting essentially os automatic; it is starting the process which is forbidden on a Sabbath, whether the 14th is a Friday or a Sabbath.</i>.
“Carrying it, or bringing it from outside the Sabbath domain.” He said only, from outside Jerusalem. Therefore from outside the Temple courtyard it is permitted because of rabbinic Sabbath restriction<sup class="footnote-marker">50</sup><i class="footnote">Since Jerusalem is a walled city, inside the city there can be no public domain by biblical standards; restrictions of carrying within the city walls are rabbinic.</i> which they permitted in the Temple.
“Cutting its wart.” There, we have stated<sup class="footnote-marker">51</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Eruvin 10:13:1" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Eruvin.10.13.1">Mishnah <i>Eruvin</i> 10:11</a>.</i>: “One cuts a wart at the Temple but not in the countryside; using an implement is forbidden here and there.” Here<sup class="footnote-marker">52</sup><i class="footnote">In <i>Eruvin,</i> showing that this is the origin of the Halakhah.</i>, you are saying, it pushes aside; there, you are saying, it does not push aside.
<sup class="footnote-marker">53</sup><i class="footnote">This paragraph is from <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Eruvin 10:12:3" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Eruvin.10.12.3"><i>Eruvin</i> 10, Notes 141–148</a>.</i> Rebbi Simon in the name of Rebbi Joshua ben Levi in the name of Bar Pedaya: Because of vitiation of the lotteries. Rebbi Yose said, but only if they drew lots. Rebbi Simeon ben Laqish said in the name of Rebbi Sobaya: Whether it can be scraped off or cannot be scraped off. Rebbi Simeon ben Yaqim said, one if it is moist, the other if it is dry. Rebbi Yose ben Ḥanina said, here by hand, there by implement. It turns out that Rebbi Simeon ben Laqish parallels Bar Qappara, and Rebbi Yose ben Ḥanina Rebbi Joḥanan, as it was stated: All who destroy are not liable, except the incendiary and one causing an injury. Bar Qappara said, even if he did not need the blood, even if he did not need the ashes. Rebbi Joḥanan said, only if he needed the blood or the ashes. Rebbi Aḥa, Rebbi Ḥanina in the name of Rebbi Joḥanan: In both cases if it is moist, and only if he needs the blood.
Is bringing it from outside the Sabbath domain a matter of Sabbath rest<sup class="footnote-marker">58</sup><i class="footnote">Since the argument of R. Eliezer and R. Joshua is about rabbinic restrictions because of Sabbath rest, it is implied that the list of items in <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Pesachim 6:2:1" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Pesachim.6.2.1">Mishnah 2</a> about which R. Eliezer dissents contains only rabbinic prohibitions. But bringing anything from outside the Sabbath domain is a biblical prohibition.</i>? <sup class="footnote-marker">59</sup><i class="footnote">The next sentences are from <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Eruvin 3:4:5" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Eruvin.3.4.5"><i>Eruvin</i> 3, Notes 127–131</a>.</i> This supports what Rebbi Jonathan said before the Elder Rebbi Ḥiyya in the name of Rebbi Simeon ben Rebbi Yose ben Laqonia: One whips because of Sabbath domains as word of the Torah. Rebbi Ḥiyya the Elder said to him, but for Sabbath there is only stoning or extirpation! He said to him, is there not written<sup class="footnote-marker">60</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Exodus 12:9" href="/Exodus.12.9"><i>Ex.</i> 12:9</a>. This belongs to the discussion there whether all pentateuchal prohibitions are legally prosecutable, or only those formulated as לֹא whereas those introduced by the negation אַל are simply moral obligations. Since the latter then cannot be enforced in court by biblical standards, they are equal in rank to rabbinic prohibitions.</i>, <i>do not eat from it raw</i>? He said to him, is there written לֹא? No, it is written אַל! He said to him, is there not written<sup class="footnote-marker">61</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Exodus 16:28" href="/Exodus.16.28"><i>Ex.</i> 16:28</a>.</i>, <i>stay everybody where he is, no person shall leave his place on the Seventh day</i>? He said to him, is there written לֹא? No, it is written אַל. Rebbi Yose ben Rebbi Abun said, nevertheless each one kept to his tradition<sup class="footnote-marker">62</sup><i class="footnote">This is the end of the parallel in <i>Eruvin</i>3.</i>. Is cutting its wart with an implement a matter of Sabbath rest<sup class="footnote-marker">63</sup><i class="footnote">This is making a wound, biblically forbidden under the category of slaughtering.</i>? Rebbi Abbahu said, Rebbi Yose ben Ḥanina stated only carrying it and bringing it; therefore not cutting its wart<sup class="footnote-marker">64</sup><i class="footnote">In <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Pesachim 6:1:1-18" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Pesachim.6.1.1-18">Mishnah 1</a>, he does not read “cutting its wart”.</i>. That is because he thinks it<sup class="footnote-marker">65</sup><i class="footnote">Cutting the wart. Everybody agrees that biting off the wart is unprofessional, therefore does not create liability, and is only rabbinically forbidden.</i> is with an implement. Therefore if he were not of the opinion that it was with an implement, would it be a matter of Sabbath rest? <sup class="footnote-marker">66</sup><i class="footnote">Quoted from <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Eruvin 10:1:8" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Eruvin.10.1.8"><i>Eruvin</i> 10(7), Note 64</a>. It is stated there that cutting the wart creates liability only if done professionally with a surgeon’s knife.</i> Did not Rebbi Abbahu say in the name of Rebbi Yose ben Ḥanina, where do they disagree? If he removed it with an implement. But if another person removed it it is disgusting<sup class="footnote-marker">67</sup><i class="footnote">Therefore not causing biblical liability. <a class="refLink" data-ref="Shabbat 94b" href="/Shabbat.94b">Babli <i>Šabbat</i> 94b</a>.</i>, and is not the sacrifice another? Rebbi Yose said, there is a difference because there is written “a sacrifice”. Rebbi Mana said, sprinkling<sup class="footnote-marker">68</sup><i class="footnote">Purifying a person impure by the impurity of the dead by sprinkling with water containing of the ashes of the Red Cow. In Second Temple times this was a public act (<a class="refLink" data-ref="Mishnah Parah 11:4" href="/Mishnah_Parah.11.4">Mishnah <i>Parah</i> 11:4</a>) not performed on the Sabbath.</i> is a matter of Sabbath rest, and these are because of Sabbath rest. Sprinkling is pushed aside<sup class="footnote-marker">69</sup><i class="footnote">If the 14th of Nisan is a Sabbath and a person’s seventh day of impurity falls on that day, he may not be purified by sprinkling, but this is not biblically forbidden, and he has to celebrate his <i>Pesaḥ</i> on the 14th of Iyar. Cf. <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Pesachim 6:3:1" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Pesachim.6.3.1">Mishnaiot 3</a>,<a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Pesachim 4:1:1-9:1" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Pesachim.4.1.1-9.1">4</a>.</i> but these should not be pushed aside? Only that these are about the sacrifice and this is for the person who sacrifices. The word of Rebbi Zeˋira implies that there is no difference between sacrifice and sacrificer: Rebbi Jehudah bar Pazi stated Bar Qappara’s before Rebbi Zeˋira: I wonder how Rebbi Eliezer received Rebbi Joshua’s answer that these are about the sacrifice and this is for the person who sacrifices<sup class="footnote-marker">70</sup><i class="footnote">Since R. Joshua’s argument is about the slaughterer, not the animal being slaughtered.</i>? He told him, Bar Qappara was wondering, Rebbi Eliezer was not wondering<sup class="footnote-marker">71</sup><i class="footnote">Their discussion makes sense only if there is no difference whether one speaks about sacrifice or sacrificer. This confirms what R. Zeˋira said.</i>.

Halakhah 2

<strong>MISHNAH:</strong> Rebbi Eliezer said, if slaughter which is work<sup class="footnote-marker">54</sup><i class="footnote">Slaughter is one of the 49 categories of work biblically forbidden on the Sabbath.</i> pushes the Sabbath aside, should not these<sup class="footnote-marker">55</sup><i class="footnote">The Mishnah is a continuation of <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Pesachim 6:1:1-18" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Pesachim.6.1.1-18">Mishnah 1</a>, where R. Eliezer holds that all actions needed for the <i>Pesaḥ</i> push aside the Sabbath. The discussion in particular is about the list of rabbinically prohibited actions at the end of <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Pesachim 6:1:1-18" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Pesachim.6.1.1-18">Mishnah 1</a>, which are permitted by R. Eliezer but prohibited by the Sages (represented by R. Joshua.)</i>, which are because of Sabbath rest, push the Sabbath aside? Rebbi Joshua said to him, holiday is a counter example, where He permitted the work but forbade because of Sabbath rest<sup class="footnote-marker">56</sup><i class="footnote">Since preparation of food is permitted on a holiday, slaughter for meat is permitted. But the rules of rabbinic Sabbath rest apply to holiday as to the Sabbath.</i>. Rebbi Eliezer answered whim, what is this, Joshua? What proof is option for obligation<sup class="footnote-marker">57</sup><i class="footnote">Rules of preparation of profane food cannot teach anything for sacrifices.</i>?
<strong>HALAKHAH:</strong> What does Sabbath rest mean? Did we not state<sup class="footnote-marker">72</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Pirkei Avot 3:11" href="/Pirkei_Avot.3.11">Mishnah <i>Avot</i> 3:11</a>. Since there is an obligation to honor the holidays, is there not an obligation to slaughter animals for holiday meals. How can R.
