Here it is presumed that he is pure.</i> slaughtered and pure<sup class="footnote-marker">92</sup><i class="footnote">Obviously one has to read: impure. (K is not legible at this point.) The impure (by the impurity of the dead) priest does not come into direct contact with the sacrificial animal. While the blood collected in the vessel which he holds will be impure, it does not make the carcass impure through the stream of blood falling into his vessel.</i> ones poured. Rebbi Hila said, <i>any meat that touched anything impure may not be eaten</i><sup class="footnote-marker">75</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Leviticus 7:19" href="/Leviticus.7.19"><i>Lev.</i> 7:19</a>.</i>, but here it was not touched by anybody impure. <i>The meat, anybody pure may eat meat</i><sup class="footnote-marker">75</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Leviticus 7:19" href="/Leviticus.7.19"><i>Lev.</i> 7:19</a>.</i>; there are pure ones available to eat it<sup class="footnote-marker">93</sup><i class="footnote">The people, as stated in the Mishnah.</i>. Rebbi Zeˋira: Since <i>Pesaḥ</i> made in impurity is eaten, [this one is as if brought in impurity]<sup class="footnote-marker">94</sup><i class="footnote">Since the people are pure, the argument of R. Hoshaia is superfluous.</i>. And where was this<sup class="footnote-marker">95</sup><i class="footnote">The source of R. Zeˋira’s argument.</i> said? Rebbi Samuel said, Rebbi Zeˋira asked: If it comes with impurity of the blood<sup class="footnote-marker">96</sup><i class="footnote">The carcass is pure, the priests are pure, but the blood has become impure. Since only the blood pumped out at the moment of slaughter is acceptable on the altar (<a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Pesachim 5:8:3" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Pesachim.5.8.3">Chapter 5, Note 234</a>), it cannot be replaced.</i>, what is done? Since one does not permit him to pour, is it as if brought in impurity? Or since if he transgressed and poured, it was made acceptable, is it as if not brought in impurity? Let us hear from the following which was said by [Rebbi Elazar in the name of <sup class="footnote-marker">87</sup><i class="footnote">Reading of K.</i> Rebbi Hoshaia: <i>Aaron shall carry the iniquities of the sacrifices</i><sup class="footnote-marker">97</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Exodus 28:38" href="/Exodus.28.38"><i>Ex.</i> 28:38</a>. Explained in more detail in the <a class="refLink" data-ref="Pesachim 16b" href="/Pesachim.16b">Babli 16b</a>, <a class="refLink" data-ref="Yoma 7a" href="/Yoma.7a"><i>Yoma</i> 7a</a>, <a class="refLink" data-ref="Zevachim 23a" href="/Zevachim.23a"><i>Zevaḥim</i> 23a</a>.</i>, the iniquities of the sacrifices, not the iniquities of the sacrificers<sup class="footnote-marker">98</sup><i class="footnote">The diadem will not cover deficiencies in either the owners or the officiants of a sacrifice. <a class="refLink" data-ref="Zevachim 23b" href="/Zevachim.23b">Babli <i>Zevaḥim</i> 23b</a>.</i>. He separated between what is offered on behalf of an individual and what is offered on behalf of the public. If offered for an individual, if he has another one<sup class="footnote-marker">99</sup><i class="footnote">Another animal to offer.<br>The following text in brackets is a corrector’s addition which by the concurrent testimony of the original scribe and K should be deleted.</i>, one tells him, bring! If not, [one does not permit him to pour the blood;] if he transgressed and poured, it was made acceptable. The sacrificers for an individual, whether he has or does not have, [it was not made acceptable. If offered for the public, if he has another one, one tells him, bring! If not, one permits him to pour the blood <i>a priori.</i> The sacrificers for the public, whether he has or does not have,] it was made acceptable.
Rebbi Eleazar said, the Mishnah is about one “which comes in impurity from the start.”<sup class="footnote-marker">100</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Tosefta Pesachim (Lieberman) 6:1" href="/Tosefta_Pesachim_(Lieberman).6.1">Tosephta 6:1</a>.</i> But if it came in purity and then became impure, it cannot be eaten in impurity. “If it was slaughtered in purity but then the public became impure, the blood shall be poured in purity<sup class="footnote-marker">101</sup><i class="footnote">Obviously if everybody is impure, the blood in the vessel carried by the impure Cohen cannot remain pure. One has to read with the Tosephta: impure.</i> but the meat not eaten in impurity.” (Should one not say the same for pouring?<sup class="footnote-marker">102</sup><i class="footnote">Text written by the scribe and deleted by the corrector; missing in K, which supports the corrector’s text. There seems to be no reason why the blood could be poured in impurity if the blood is only needed to permit the meat to be consumed when the meat is forbidden for consumption.</i>) [Rebbi La in the name of Rebbi Joḥanan: It is Rebbi Nathan’s, as Rebbi Nathan said, one has fulfilled his duty by pouring without eating<sup class="footnote-marker">103</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Pesachim 78b" href="/Pesachim.78b">Babli 78b</a>. The pouring of the blood frees the group subscribing to this particular <i>Pesaḥ</i> from having to bring another animal at the Second <i>Pesaḥ.</i></i>. “If it was slaughtered in purity but then the blood collected became impure<sup class="footnote-marker">104</sup><i class="footnote">This sentence does not make any sense, although it is confirmed by the <i>editio princeps</i> of the <a class="refLink" data-ref="Tosefta Pesachim (Lieberman) 6:1" href="/Tosefta_Pesachim_(Lieberman).6.1">Tosephta (6:1</a>). One has to read with K and the Tosephta mss. either וצבור or והציבור: “If it was slaughtered in purity but then the public became impure, the blood may be poured in impurity but the meat may not be eaten in impurity.”</i>, the blood may be poured in impurity but the meat may not be eaten in impurity.” Rebbi Jeremiah in the name of Rebbi Joḥanan: Because of the bad impression, lest they say, we have seen a <i>Pesaḥ</i> brought in purity which was [poured] {eaten}<sup class="footnote-marker">105</sup><i class="footnote">As the following shows, one has to prefer {the text of K} over [the corrector’s text].</i> in impurity. Then should not the blood be poured in impurity?] Lest they say, we have seen a <i>Pesaḥ</i> brought in purity for which it was poured in impurity. You have to end up saying that it is Rebbi Nathan’s. Rebbi Nathan agrees for a sick or an old person<sup class="footnote-marker">106</sup><i class="footnote">R. Nathan only declares pouring the blood as sufficient if at the start there was a possibility that the meat would be eaten, “since from the start this is what it is for.” If nobody in the group is able to eat a full olive-sized piece, there can be no <i>Pesaḥ.</i></i>. Rebbi Nathan agrees for a group whose officiant became impure<sup class="footnote-marker">107</sup><i class="footnote">If the slaughterer makes the sacrifice impure, there can be no pouring of the blood.</i>, that they are pushed to the Second <i>Pesaḥ.</i> Rebbi Nathan agrees for a group where a wart was found<sup class="footnote-marker">108</sup><i class="footnote">If the animal from the start was unfit to be a sacrifice, there can be no sacrifice.</i>, that they are pushed to the Second <i>Pesaḥ.</i>
“If the skins of the <i>Pesaḥ</i> sacrifices of five groups were intermingled and a wart was found on one of them, all of them<sup class="footnote-marker">109</sup><i class="footnote">The sacrifices have to be brought to the spot where disqualified sacrifices were burned outside the sacred precinct.</i> have to be brought to the place of burning, but they<sup class="footnote-marker">110</sup><i class="footnote">The members of the groups. Since the animal with the wart never was a potential sacrifice, the group bringing this particular animal must be considered as not having offered a <i>Pesaḥ</i> at all, and obligated to bring a Second <i>Pesaḥ.</i> But since for each person there only is a 20% probability that his <i>Pesaḥ</i> was the invalid one, and a Second <i>Pesaḥ</i> may not be brought by a person not obligated, nobody is provably obligated and therefore nobody is entitled to bring a Second <i>Pesaḥ.</i></i> are not liable to bring a Second <i>Pesaḥ.</i><sup class="footnote-marker">111</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Pesachim 88b" href="/Pesachim.88b">Babli 88b</a>.</i>” They wanted to say that this is Rebbi Nathan’s. Explain it following everybody, {they made it}<sup class="footnote-marker">87</sup><i class="footnote">Reading of K.</i> like one which has become impure by a doubt of a grave of the abyss<sup class="footnote-marker">112</sup><i class="footnote">Since if the blood was poured for the <i>Pesaḥ</i> of a person who assumes that he was pure and between this act and the consumption of the sacrifice he was informed that possibly he was made impure by stepping over a previously unknown grave, he cannot eat, so also here all members of the group whose <i>Pesaḥ</i> possibly was a non-sacrifice cannot eat from it.</i>. Following Rebbi Nathan would he have poured the blood<sup class="footnote-marker">113</sup><i class="footnote">Even following R. Nathan, the situation is possible only if the wart was discovered after the blood was poured; even R. Nathan does not allow pouring the blood of a non-sacrifice. <a class="refLink" data-ref="Pesachim 88b" href="/Pesachim.88b">Babli 88b</a>, opinion of Abbai.</i>?
<sup class="footnote-marker">114</sup><i class="footnote">Discussion of the statement of the Mishnah that both the <i>Omer</i> and the Two Breads are brought in impurity even though they cannot be consumed by the priest and it is questionable whether a fistful of the <i>Omer</i> can be burned or the breads presented before the altar if that action seems purposeless since it does not serve to permit anything to be eaten.</i> Rebbi Joḥanan, Rebbi Ismael in the name of Rebbi Joshua: One verse says, <i>but a firstling of cattle, or a firstling of sheep, or a firstling of goats</i><sup class="footnote-marker">115</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Numbers 18:17" href="/Numbers.18.17"><i>Num.</i> 18:17</a>. The verse continues: <i>pour their blood on the altar, and burn their fat</i>, … <i>and their meat shall be yours.</i></i>, etc. And another verse says<sup class="footnote-marker">116</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Leviticus 17:6" href="/Leviticus.17.6"><i>Lev.</i> 17:6</a>.</i> <i>the Cohen shall pour the blood on the Eternal’s altar at the door of the Tent of Meeting, and burn the fat for a pleasant smell before the Eternal.</i> Only if there be there either meat be be eaten or parts to be burned<sup class="footnote-marker">117</sup><i class="footnote">Since <a class="refLink" data-ref="Numbers 18:17" href="/Numbers.18.17"><i>Num.</i> 18:17</a> mentions fat and meat but <i>Lev</i>.17:6 only fat, it follows that the sacrifice is acceptable if the blood is poured either to permit the fat to be burned or the meat to be eaten.</i>. There we have stated<sup class="footnote-marker">118</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Mishnah Menachot 3:4" href="/Mishnah_Menachot.3.4">Mishnah <i>Menaḥot</i>3:4</a>. For flour offerings, the fistful to be burned on the altar permits the remainder to be eaten by the Cohanim; the relationship of the fistful taken by the priest for the altar to the remainder to be consumed in the sacred domain is parallel to that of blood to be poured and the parts to be burned or the meat to be eaten.</i>: “If the remainders became impure, the remainders were burned, the remainders were lost. In the rules of Rebbi Eliezer it is qualified, in the rules of Rebbi Joshua it is disqualified. [Not in a vessel of service it is disqualified; Rebbi Ismael<sup class="footnote-marker">119</sup><i class="footnote">The second part of the Mishnah was added by the corrector; by the testimony of K this should be deleted. “R. Ismael” is a scribal error for “R. Simeon” in the Mishnah and in a quote of the Mishnah in <i>Yoma</i> 2:1, 39c line 32.</i> qualifies. If he burned the fistful in two parts it is qualified.”] In Rebbi Eliezer’s opinion, if there is no blood there is no meat; even though if there is no meat there is blood<sup class="footnote-marker">120</sup><i class="footnote">For him, pouring the blood is a sacral act independent of the fact that pouring the blood is needed to enable the parts to be burned and the meat to be eaten.</i>. If there is no fistful there are no remainders, even though if there are no remainders there is a fistful. In Rebbi Joshua’s opinion, if there is no blood there is no meat; if there is no meat there is no blood<sup class="footnote-marker">121</sup><i class="footnote">If nothing is to be enabled, the act of pouring becomes meaningless and therefore has to be avoided. But then R. Joshua cannot permit the <i>Omer</i> to be brought in impurity, since this also would be a meaningless act.</i>. If there is no fistful there are no remainders, if there are no remainders there is no fistful. Rebbi Mana said, explain it<sup class="footnote-marker">114</sup><i class="footnote">Discussion of the statement of the Mishnah that both the <i>Omer</i> and the Two Breads are brought in impurity even though they cannot be consumed by the priest and it is questionable whether a fistful of the <i>Omer</i> can be burned or the breads presented before the altar if that action seems purposeless since it does not serve to permit anything to be eaten.</i> following Rebbi Eliezer, since Rebbi Eliezer said, even though there are no remainders there is a fistful. Rebbi Yose ben Rebbi Abun said, Rav and Rebbi Joḥanan both are saying, Rebbi Joshua agrees that if he transgressed and poured the blood that it was made acceptable<sup class="footnote-marker">122</sup><i class="footnote">Since the diadem justifies the act retroactively, the same can be said for the <i>Omer</i> and the entire Mishnah may be R. Joshua’s.</i>.

Halakhah 6

<strong>MISHNAH:</strong> If the public or a majority of it were impure or the Cohanim were impure and the public pure, it should be brought in impurity<sup class="footnote-marker">78</sup><i class="footnote">Since the <i>Pesaḥ</i> cannot be slaughtered without Cohanim ready to receive and pour the blood.</i>. If a minority of the public were impure, the pure people make the first and the impure the second<sup class="footnote-marker">79</sup><i class="footnote">The Second <i>Pesaḥ</i> is made on the 14<sup>th</sup> of Iyar; <a class="refLink" data-ref="Numbers 9:10-12" href="/Numbers.9.10-12"><i>Num.</i> 9:10–12</a>.</i>.
<strong>HALAKHAH:</strong> Who is the Tanna of “majority”<sup class="footnote-marker">123</sup><i class="footnote">Discussion of the statement in the Mishnah, that <i>Pesaḥ</i> is celebrated in impurity if most (50%+1) of the people are impure. The following is an extended version of <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Pesachim 1:5:6" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Pesachim.1.5.6">Halakhah 1:6</a> in <i>Horaiot</i>, where the problem is what is called “community”.</i>? Rebbi Meïr<sup class="footnote-marker">124</sup><i class="footnote">He holds that everywhere 50%+1 represent “all”; <a class="refLink" data-ref="Horayot 5b" href="/Horayot.5b">Babli <i>Horaiot</i> 5b</a>.</i>, as it was stated: Either half of the tribes or half of each tribe, if only it be a majority<sup class="footnote-marker">125</sup><i class="footnote">In order to trigger the ceremony required if <i>all the community acts in error</i>(<a class="refLink" data-ref="Leviticus 4:14" href="/Leviticus.4.14"><i>Lev.</i> 4:14</a>), by following an erroneous ruling either of the High Court at the central sanctuary or of a majority of tribal High Courts.</i>. Rebbi Jehudah says, half of each tribe, but only a majority of entire tribes<sup class="footnote-marker">126</sup><i class="footnote">The language is somewhat self-contradictory. He also requires that a majority of Israel follow the erroneous ruling but in addition he demands that in a majority of tribes a majority follow the ruling. <a class="refLink" data-ref="Horayot 5b" href="/Horayot.5b">Babli <i>Horaiot</i> 5b</a>.</i>. One tribe drags all tribes<sup class="footnote-marker">127</sup><i class="footnote">If one tribe has more members than all the others together, the action of one tribe triggers the obligation of all of them. He does not hold that the law about erroneous rulings of the High Court became moot with the exile of the Ten Tribes. Even later, when the tribe of Jehudah represented the overwhelming majority of Israel, a majority of the people can be considered a majority of all twelve tribes and the majority of Judeans triggers the obligation for all tribes.</i>. Rebbi Meïr says, all tribes are called “the public”<sup class="footnote-marker">128</sup><i class="footnote">The purification sacrifice for an erroneous ruling by the Court has to be brought by “the public” (<a class="refLink" data-ref="Leviticus 4:14" href="/Leviticus.4.14"><i>Lev.</i> 4:14</a>). The difference of opinions in the Mishnah is traced to different interpretations of this notion. R. Meïr holds that only the entire people of Israel qualify as “public”; RR. Jehudah and Simeon consider each tribe as a separate public. (<a class="refLink" data-ref="Horayot 5b" href="/Horayot.5b">Babli <i>Horaiot</i> 5b</a>, <a class="refLink" data-ref="Pesachim 80a" href="/Pesachim.80a"><i>Pesaḥim</i> 80a</a>, <a class="refLink" data-ref="Menachot 15a" href="/Menachot.15a"><i>Menaḥot</i>15a</a>).</i>. Rebbi Jehudah says, each single tribe is called “public”. What is between them? Dragging. Rebbi Meïr says, a single tribe does not drag all tribes<sup class="footnote-marker">129</sup><i class="footnote">Therefore he requires a separate sacrifice for the people of Israel in their entirety.</i>, but Rebbi Jehudah says, one tribe drags all tribes. And Rebbi Jehudah follows Rebbi Simeon. Just as Rebbi Simeon said, one tribe drags all tribes<sup class="footnote-marker">130</sup><i class="footnote">In <i>Horaiot,</i> the opposite is asserted, that in this particular R. Simeon sides with R. Meïr; this also is required by the later statements in this Halakhah. R. Simeon agrees that each single tribe is called “public”.</i>, so Rebbi Jehudah says, one tribe drags all tribes. Even though Rebbi Jehudah says, one tribe drags all tribes, he agrees that only if the ruling came from the ashlar hall<sup class="footnote-marker">131</sup><i class="footnote">Even though each tribe has to bring its own sacrifice, the ruling of a tribal High Court cannot trigger an obligation of any other tribe; only the Court sitting at the central sanctuary has this power.</i>. Rebbi Yose said, the reason of that Tanna: <i>From this place which the Eternal will choose</i><sup class="footnote-marker">132</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Deuteronomy 17:10" href="/Deuteronomy.17.10"><i>Deut.</i> 17:10</a>.</i>. What is the reason of Rebbi Jehudah? <i>The entire community of the Children of Israel will be forgiven</i><sup class="footnote-marker">133</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Numbers 15:26" href="/Numbers.15.26"><i>Num.</i> 15:26</a>. R. Jehudah argues that the verse promises forgiveness for all of Israel even if only one tribe followed an erroneous ruling; this proves that “one tribe drags all the other tribes.” R. Simeon disagrees since the last clause in the verse states that the <i>entire</i> people have to be in error; only a majority of the tribes triggers the obligation.</i>. What is the reason of Rebbi Simeon? <i>Since the entire people acted in error</i><sup class="footnote-marker">133</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Numbers 15:26" href="/Numbers.15.26"><i>Num.</i> 15:26</a>. R. Jehudah argues that the verse promises forgiveness for all of Israel even if only one tribe followed an erroneous ruling; this proves that “one tribe drags all the other tribes.” R. Simeon disagrees since the last clause in the verse states that the <i>entire</i> people have to be in error; only a majority of the tribes triggers the obligation.</i>. How does Rebbi Simeon uphold Rebbi Jehudah’s reason, <i>the entire community of the Children of Israel will be forgiven?</i> Except women and children<sup class="footnote-marker">134</sup><i class="footnote">Not that they will not be forgiven but they are not counted in determining what is a majority.</i>. How does Rebbi Jehudah uphold Rebbi Simeon’s reason, <i>since the entire people acted in error</i>? Except if the beginning was criminal and the conclusion in error. Rebbi Abun in the name of Rebbi Benjamin bar Levi: The verse supports him who said that each tribe is called “public”, as it is written<sup class="footnote-marker">137</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Genesis 35:11" href="/Genesis.35.11"><i>Gen.</i> 35:11</a>, said to Jacob after the birth of 11 sons. <a class="refLink" data-ref="Horayot 5b" href="/Horayot.5b">Babli <i>Horaiot</i> 5b</a>.</i>: <i>A people and a public of peoples will come from you,</i> and Benjamin was not yet born. Rebbi Ḥiyya bar Abba said, just as they differ here, so they differ about impurity, as it was stated: If the public was half pure and half impure; pure [people] celebrate the first [<i>Pesaḥ</i>] and impure the second, the words of Rebbi Meïr. Rebbi Jehudah says, the pure ones celebrate for themselves, and the impure ones celebrate for themselves<sup class="footnote-marker">138</sup><i class="footnote">Both offer their sacrifices in the Temple, in separate groups. For this to happen, the number of pure people in Jerusalem on the 14<sup class="footnote-marker">th</sup> of Nisan must be <i>exactly</i> equal to the number of impure ones. <a class="refLink" data-ref="Tosefta Pesachim (Lieberman) 6:2" href="/Tosefta_Pesachim_(Lieberman).6.2">Tosephta 6:2</a> in the name of R. Simeon. This latter attribution seems to be correct since in the paragraph after the next the Amoraim explain that R. Jehudah never considers this case but requires that the number of pure people present be diminished.</i>. They told him, there is no split Passover; either all celebrate in purity or all celebrate in impurity. Who is “they told him”? Rebbi Meïr. The argument of Rebbi Jehudah seems inverted, as we have stated there<sup class="footnote-marker">139</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Mishnah Menachot 2:2" href="/Mishnah_Menachot.2.2">Mishnah <i>Menaḥot</i>2:2</a>.<br>The Mishnah refers to the two public cereal offerings which have to be baked, <i>viz.,</i> the weekly show-bread and the two leavened loaves presented at Pentecost. The 12 show-breads were presented in two rows, here called “orders” <a class="refLink" data-ref="Leviticus 24:6" href="/Leviticus.24.6"><i>(Lev.</i> 24:6</a>).</i>: “If one of the loaves or one of the orders became impure, Rebbi Jehudah said, both have to be brought to be burned<sup class="footnote-marker">140</sup><i class="footnote">Outside the Temple precinct.</i> for a public offering cannot be split<sup class="footnote-marker">141</sup><i class="footnote">Cf. <a class="refLink" data-ref="Pesachim 79a" href="/Pesachim.79a">Babli 79a</a>.</i>. But the Sages say, the impure in its impurity, and the pure shall be eaten<sup class="footnote-marker">142</sup><i class="footnote">By the officiating priests.</i>.” Rebbi Yose ben Rebbi Abun in the name of Rebbi Joḥanan: who is “they told him”? The Sages who argue like Rebbi Meïr<sup class="footnote-marker">143</sup><i class="footnote">In <i>Horaiot:</i> R. Jehudah. In any case, the question should not arise since the objecting Sages, while adopting the point of view of one of the protagonists, are not bound to follow him in all details.</i>.
In Rebbi Meïr’s opinion<sup class="footnote-marker">144</sup><i class="footnote">This name attribution seems to be in error since R. Meïr is quoted in the preceding paragraph that in this case the pure persons celebrate the First <i>Pesaḥ</i> and the impure the Second. One has to read “R. Simeon”.</i>, how does one act if they are half and half? As majority or as minority? If you are saying as a majority, the pure persons cannot make the First. If you are saying as a minority, the impure persons cannot make the Second<sup class="footnote-marker">145</sup><i class="footnote">The formulation is not very clear. If one considers the impure (by the impurity of the dead) as a majority, then the service in the Temple is conducted in impurity, and the pure persons cannot make their sacrifice in purity. If the pure are considered a minority, there is no Second <i>Pesaḥ</i> for the impure.</i>. Rebbi Yose said, he did not say that a majority of pure persons cannot make the First, a majority of impure persons cannot make the Second. He only said, a majority of impure persons is not pushed to the Second <i>Pesaḥ</i><sup class="footnote-marker">146</sup><i class="footnote">The problem only is apparent, not real. For the <i>Pesaḥ</i> to be offered in impurity one needs a real majority; a 50–50 split in practice is equal to a majority of the pure.</i><i>.</i>
In Rebbi Jehudah’s opinion, how does one act if they are half and half? Rebbi Abba in the name of Rav: One defiles one person with a crawling animal<sup class="footnote-marker">147</sup><i class="footnote">He is impure, but can become free of impurity by immersion in a <i>miqweh,</i> which will make him pure for <i>sancta</i> at sundown. This kind of impurity does not prevent a person to be counted in a group eating the <i>Pesaḥ</i> in purity; accepting the person in the count of the impure is questionable; <a class="refLink" data-ref="Pesachim 80a" href="/Pesachim.80a">Babli 80a</a>, <a class="refLink" data-ref="Pesachim 80b" href="/Pesachim.80b">80b</a>.</i>. Samuel said, one sends one person on a far-away trip<sup class="footnote-marker">148</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Pesachim 80a" href="/Pesachim.80a">Babli 80a</a>. He automatically must bring the Second <i>Pesaḥ.</i></i>. This follows him who said, a single person clinches for impurity<sup class="footnote-marker">149</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Pesachim 80a" href="/Pesachim.80a">Babli 80a</a>, <a class="refLink" data-ref="Tosefta Pesachim (Lieberman) 6:2" href="/Tosefta_Pesachim_(Lieberman).6.2">Tosephta 6:2</a>.</i>. But for him who said, a single person does not clinch for impurity, one has to send two persons away. Rav’s opinion parallels Rebbi Eleazar, as Rebbi Eleazar said, if the public was touching carcasses, touching crawling animals, one makes it in impurity if there is not water there to immerse in; but if there is water to immerse in, one does not make it in impurity<sup class="footnote-marker">150</sup><i class="footnote">Since these are impurities which are eliminated by immersion in water.</i>. Rebbi Eleazar said, if it comes while the Temple vessels are impure, comes in impurity; if it comes in impurity of Temple vessels, comes in impurity of hands, comes in impurity of knives<sup class="footnote-marker">151</sup><i class="footnote">This means that <i>Pesaḥ</i> is brought in impurity if the necessary Temple implements are impure and cannot be purified in time; this could happen only in times of a siege of Jerusalem.</i>.
If the public were one third sufferers from gonorrhea<sup class="footnote-marker">152</sup><i class="footnote">A person who suffers a single episode of gonorrhea is impure for the day and can be purified by immersion in a <i>miqweh.</i> If he has two episodes in at most two consecutive days, he is impure for seven days; after seven days in remission he can be purified by immersion in a <i>miqweh.</i> After three episodes he still needs seven days in remission but then is still prohibited <i>sancta</i> unless on the eighth day he brings a couple of birds as sacrifice to the Temple. A sufferer from gonorrhea who is impure for seven days, on the seventh day is a questionable candidate for <i>Pesaḥ</i> since if he suffers another episode he has to start all over again.</i>, one third impure<sup class="footnote-marker">153</sup><i class="footnote">Impure in impurity of the dead.</i>, and one third pure. Rebbi Mana in the name of Ḥizqiah: The sufferers from gonorrhea and the impure form a majority against the pure and one brings in impurity. The sufferers from gonorrhea bring neither the First nor the Second<sup class="footnote-marker">154</sup><i class="footnote">The First he cannot bring being impure. If he should be healed between the 14th of Nisan and the 14th of Iyar, in this case he cannot bring the Second <i>Pesaḥ</i> since the latter is instituted for people impure in the impurity of the dead or away on a trip <a class="refLink" data-ref="Numbers 9:9" href="/Numbers.9.9"><i>(Num.</i>9:9</a>). While healed sufferers from gonorrhea can bring the Second <i>Pesaḥ</i> (<a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Pesachim 9:7:2" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Pesachim.9.7.2">Halakhah 9:1</a>), there can be no Second <i>Pesaḥ</i> if the First was celebrated in impurity.</i>. Rebbi Zeˋira said, they made the sufferer from gonorrhea like the apostate for ruling<sup class="footnote-marker">155</sup><i class="footnote">If it is a question whether most of the people followed an erroneous ruling of the Supreme Court, apostates are not counted as part of the people. Applied to the case here, sufferers from gonorrhea are counted neither with the impure nor with the pure, in opposition to the rule stated earlier.</i>. As one says there, the apostate in matters of ruling neither adds nor subtracts, also here he neither adds nor subtracts.
If one of the members of a group became impure<sup class="footnote-marker">153</sup><i class="footnote">Impure in impurity of the dead.</i> but it is not known who it is, they must make the Second. If one of the public became impure but it is not known who it is, Rebbi Zeˋira said, they shall make the Second. Rebbi Hoshaia stated, they shall be treated as a case of doubt<sup class="footnote-marker">156</sup><i class="footnote">They cannot bring a <i>Pesaḥ</i> since they cannot risk that one of the group eat <i>sanctum</i> while impure, a deadly sin punishable by extirpation.</i>. It is reasonable following Rebbi Hoshaia, not to subject the individual to punishment of extirpation.
<sup class="footnote-marker">157</sup><i class="footnote">This paragraph also is in <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Horayot 1:2:8" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Horayot.1.2.8"><i>Horaiot</i> 1:2, Notes 92–97</a>.</i> Rebbi Immi in the name of Rebbi Simeon ben Laqish: For ruling<sup class="footnote-marker">158</sup><i class="footnote">To determine whether a majority of the people followed an erroneous ruling of the Supreme Court, the entire adult male population of the Land is counted.</i> they went after the population of the Land of Israel; for impurity they went after a majority of those entering the Temple courtyard. Does one estimate according to all groups or does one estimate only for the first group? Rebbi Yose ben Rebbi Abun said, they have to estimate by themselves as long as they are outside<sup class="footnote-marker">159</sup><i class="footnote">Since the impure are not permitted on the Temple Mount unless a majority of the people are impure, it is obvious that the count of a majority cannot be determined by the people entering the Temple precinct but must be made before people enter the Temple Mount. The <a class="refLink" data-ref="Pesachim 94b" href="/Pesachim.94b">Babli 94b</a> has only the statement which is rejected here.</i>. Rebbi Joshua ben Levi said, for appearance<sup class="footnote-marker">160</sup><i class="footnote">The duty for <i>all your men to be seen before the Eternal three times a year (Deut.</i>15:16).</i> they went from Lavo-Hamat to the Brook of Egypt. Rebbi Tanḥuma in the name of Rebbi Ḥuna: The reason of Rebbi Joshua ben Levi, <i>At that time Solomon made the pilgrimage holiday, and all of Israel with him</i><sup class="footnote-marker">161</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="I Kings 8:65" href="/I_Kings.8.65"><i>1K.</i> 8:65</a>. The verse continues: <i>a big crowd, from Levo-Hamat to the Brook of Egypt</i> (Central Syria to Wadi El-Arish).</i><i>,</i> etc.

Halakhah 7

<strong>MISHNAH:</strong> If blood was poured of a <i>Pesaḥ</i> when later it became known that it was impure, the diadem makes acceptable<sup class="footnote-marker">80</sup><i class="footnote">The golden diadem worn by the High Priest, whose object is <i>to carry away the iniquities of the sacrifices offered by the Children of Israel; Ex.</i> 28:37.</i>. An impurity of the body<sup class="footnote-marker">81</sup><i class="footnote">The body of the offerer.</i> the diadem does not make acceptable since they said that for the <i>nazir</i> and the offerer of the <i>Pesaḥ</i> the diadem makes impurity of the blood acceptable but not impurity of the body. If the impurity was caused by impurity of the abyss<sup class="footnote-marker">82</sup><i class="footnote">Impurity buried in the ground which previously was totally unknown and is only recently uncovered. Since it is impossible to guard against this kind of impurity there can be no penalty for “tent impurity” of this kind.</i>, the diadem makes acceptable.
<strong>HALAKHAH:</strong> <sup class="footnote-marker">162</sup><i class="footnote">Discussion of the last part of <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Pesachim 7:12:2" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Pesachim.7.12.2">Mishnah 5</a> (in the independent Mishnah mss. <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Pesachim 7:9:2-10:1" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Pesachim.7.9.2-10.1">Mishnah 7</a>), that the diadem covers up impurity of the blood for <i>Pesaḥ</i> and the <i>nazir.</i></i> The Mishnah if it became impure after it fell into the vessel. But if it became impure when still higher it is as if he received water<sup class="footnote-marker">163</sup><i class="footnote">If the Cohen received pure blood in a sacred vessel, the owner’s act in the sacrifice is completed. If then something happens in the custody of the Cohen, the High Priest’s diadem covers the fault; the blood may be poured on the walls of the altar and the meat consumed. But if the blood becomes impure before being received in the vessel, there is no qualified sacrifice; the carcass has to be burned outside the Temple district.</i>.
<sup class="footnote-marker">164</sup><i class="footnote">From here on, the text is also found in <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Nazir 9:2:6-9" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Nazir.9.2.6-9"><i>Nazir</i> 9:2, Notes 58–94</a>.</i> From where about a doubtful case of a grave in the abyss<sup class="footnote-marker">165</sup><i class="footnote">Both for the person going to celebrate the <i>Pesaḥ</i> and the <i>nazir</i> who finished his term, the impurity caused by a doubtful case of a grave in the abyss is disregarded. In view of the central role of purity in everything connected with the Sanctuary, it is obvious that some biblical justification has to be found for the rule. In the case of Passover, the argument notes that <a class="refLink" data-ref="Numbers 9:9" href="/Numbers.9.9"><i>Num.</i> 9:9</a> could have stated that a person <i>on a far trip</i> was required to celebrate the Second <i>Pesaḥ.</i> The addition <i>for you</i> seems to be superfluous. It is interpreted to mean just as the road is open to the wanderer, so the impurity has to be in the open for the impure person. The same argument is in the <a class="refLink" data-ref="Pesachim 81b" href="/Pesachim.81b">Babli 81b</a>.</i>? Rebbi Jacob bar Aḥa in the name of the rabbis: <i>Or on a far trip for you.</i> What is in the open for you, including everything in the open. This excludes the case of a grave in the abyss which is not open. So far for the people celebrating Passover. From where the <i>nazir?</i> Rebbi Joḥanan in the name of Rebbi [Yannai]<sup class="footnote-marker">87</sup><i class="footnote">Reading of K.</i>: <i>If a person dies suddenly on him</i><sup class="footnote-marker">166</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Numbers 6:9" href="/Numbers.6.9"><i>Num.</i> 6:9</a>.</i><i>.</i> Since on him it is in the open, so everything in the open. This eliminates the grave in the abyss which is not in the open<sup class="footnote-marker">167</sup><i class="footnote">The same argument as before; <a class="refLink" data-ref="Pesachim 81b" href="/Pesachim.81b">Babli 81b</a>, <i>Sifry Num.</i> 28.</i>.
If the public became impure in a doubtful case of a grave in the abyss, does the diadem make it acceptable? It is a conclusion <i>de minore ad maius.</i> Since in the case of a single person, whose position you clarified to his disadvantage in the case of known impurity<sup class="footnote-marker">168</sup><i class="footnote">Since a single person impure on the 14th of Nisan is required to celebrate the Second <i>Pesaḥ,</i> his standing is inferior to that of the public who celebrate the First <i>Pesaḥ</i> in impurity.</i>, you clarified to his advantage in the case of a grave in the abyss<sup class="footnote-marker">169</sup><i class="footnote">The case of a grave in the abyss can arise only in a private domain since in a public domain all doubts are automatically resolved in favor of purity <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Sotah 1:2:5" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Sotah.1.2.5"><i>(Sotah</i> 1:2, Note 88</a>). For a private person, a case of doubt in matters of a grave in the abyss in a private domain is treated as if it were occurring in the public domain.</i>, for the public, whose position you clarified to its advantage in the case of known impurity<sup class="footnote-marker">170</sup><i class="footnote">In that they may bring the <i>Pesaḥ</i> in impurity.</i>, it only is logical that you should clarify it to its advantage in a doubtful case of a grave in the abyss. A leniency which you apply to a single person you treat as a restriction for the public<sup class="footnote-marker">171</sup><i class="footnote">This is how one intends to disprove the argument <i>de minore ad majus.</i></i>. A leniency which you apply to a single person, so that if it became known to him<sup class="footnote-marker">172</sup><i class="footnote">The impurity of a grave in the abyss never forces a person to the Second <i>Pesaḥ;</i> so if he was told before pouring it is as if he became otherwise impure after pouring, where the sacrificial act was completed and while he cannot eat his part of the <i>Pesaḥ</i> he has discharged all his obligations.</i> before pouring he should be treated as if he became impure after pouring, that he should not be pushed to the Second <i>Pesaḥ,</i> you restrict him in public, so that if it became known to him after pouring he should be treated as if he became impure before pouring, that he should not be able to eat the meat<sup class="footnote-marker">173</sup><i class="footnote">If the public are impure, the <i>Pesaḥ</i> is slaughtered and eaten in impurity. But if it was slaughtered as pure and then it became impure or became known to be impure, it cannot be eaten.</i>. The leniency which you apply to the pure <i>nazir,</i> so that if it became known to him before pouring he is treated as impure after pouring, that he should not have to bring a sacrifice of impurity<sup class="footnote-marker">174</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Nazir 9:2:1" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Nazir.9.2.1">Mishnah <i>Nazir</i> 9:2</a>. Corrector’s addition supported by K.</i>, you treat as a restriction for the impure <i>nazir,</i> that if it became known to him after pouring he is treated as somebody repeatedly becoming impure; he has to bring a sacrifice of impurity for each single case<sup class="footnote-marker">175</sup><i class="footnote">But if the <i>nazir</i> became aware of the second impurity before he offered his sacrifice of impurity, he has to bring only one sacrifice.</i>. [As it was stated: If he repeatedly became impure, he has to bring a sacrifice for each single case<sup class="footnote-marker">176</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Nazir 6:6:2" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Nazir.6.6.2"><i>Nazir</i> Halakhah 6:8, Note 198</a>.</i>.] If somebody is officiating for the <i>Pesaḥ,</i> does the diadem make it acceptable? It is a conclusion <i>de minore ad majus.</i> Since for the owner [of the <i>Pesaḥ]</i> whose position you clarified to his disadvantage in the case of the infirm and the aged<sup class="footnote-marker">177</sup><i class="footnote">While a person unable to eat the volume of an olive of the <i>Pesaḥ</i> may not subscribe to it, an old or sick priest is able to serve in the Temple as long as his infirmity is not of the kind listed in <i>Lev,</i> 21:18–20.</i>, you clarified to their advantage in the case of a grave in the abyss, it should be only logical that for the officiating, whose position you clarified to his advantage in the case of the infirm and the aged, you should clarify it to his advantage in the case of a grave in the abyss. No. Since for the owner you clarify to his disadvantage in the case of impurity during the rest of the year; what can you say for the officiating where you clarify his position to his disadvantage in the case of impurity during the rest of the year<sup class="footnote-marker">178</sup><i class="footnote">An impure person, including a <i>nazir</i> not impure by the impurity of the dead, can send his sacrifice other than the <i>Pesaḥ</i> to the Temple by a pure agent, but an impure priest cannot officiate, irrespective of the nature of his impurity.</i>. Since you clarify his position to his disadvantage in the case of impurity during the rest of the year, you also clarify his position to his disadvantage in the case of the impurity of the dead on Passover. How is it really? <i>For you</i><sup class="footnote-marker">165</sup><i class="footnote">Both for the person going to celebrate the <i>Pesaḥ</i> and the <i>nazir</i> who finished his term, the impurity caused by a doubtful case of a grave in the abyss is disregarded. In view of the central role of purity in everything connected with the Sanctuary, it is obvious that some biblical justification has to be found for the rule. In the case of Passover, the argument notes that <a class="refLink" data-ref="Numbers 9:9" href="/Numbers.9.9"><i>Num.</i> 9:9</a> could have stated that a person <i>on a far trip</i> was required to celebrate the Second <i>Pesaḥ.</i> The addition <i>for you</i> seems to be superfluous. It is interpreted to mean just as the road is open to the wanderer, so the impurity has to be in the open for the impure person. The same argument is in the <a class="refLink" data-ref="Pesachim 81b" href="/Pesachim.81b">Babli 81b</a>.</i><i>,</i> whether for him or for the one officiating for him. So far for the people celebrating Passover. From where the <i>nazir?</i> Rebbi Yose in the name of Rav Ḥisda: We thought to say, <i>on him</i><sup class="footnote-marker">166</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Numbers 6:9" href="/Numbers.6.9"><i>Num.</i> 6:9</a>.</i><i>,</i> not on the one officiating for him. Since we stated that the same rules apply to the <i>nazir</i> and to those celebrating Passover, it means that what holds for the one holds for the other<sup class="footnote-marker">179</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Pesachim 80b" href="/Pesachim.80b">Babli 80b</a>.</i>.
“What is a grave of the abyss? A corpse buried in stubble, straw, dust, or pebbles<sup class="footnote-marker">180</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Tosefta Zavim 2:5" href="/Tosefta_Zavim.2.5">Tosephta <i>Zavim</i> 2:9</a>; quoted in the <a class="refLink" data-ref="Pesachim 81b" href="/Pesachim.81b">Babli, 81b</a>, and <a class="refLink" data-ref="Nazir 63b" href="/Nazir.63b"><i>Nazir</i> 63b</a>, without further discussion. As explained in the next paragraph, “grave of the abyss” is that of a person killed by an accident not witnessed by anybody. If one finds a corpse buried under a heap of straw, one has to assume that he suffocated when the straw fell on him. A corpse buried in dust or pebbles probably was the victim of an accident.</i>. But if it was buried in water, a dark spot, or rock crevices, it does not create a grave of the abyss<sup class="footnote-marker">181</sup><i class="footnote">In this case, the person also probably was the victim of an accident. But since it could have been seen by a passer-by, the competent authorities should have been alerted; this is not an unknown body.</i>.” The principle: Any place from where it can be removed creates a grave of the abyss; any place from where it cannot be removed does not create a grave of the abyss<sup class="footnote-marker">182</sup><i class="footnote">Obviously, the clauses in this sentence are switched (here and in <i>Nazir).</i> As explained in the preceding notes, one must read: “Any place from where it cannot be removed creates a grave of the abyss; any place from where it can be removed does not create a grave of the abyss.” A corpse whose existence is unknown cannot be removed.</i>. Can stubbles and straw not be removed? Does the Mishnah not follow Rebbi Yose, since Rebbi Yose said, straw said to be disregarded is disregarded<sup class="footnote-marker">183</sup><i class="footnote">The remainder of this paragraph also is in <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Eruvin 7:3:2" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Eruvin.7.3.2"><i>Eruvin</i> 7, Notes 58–62</a>.<br>This refers to the rules of the tent-impurity caused by a corpse. A “tent” is any covered space in which there is at least one hand-breadth of space between the corpse and the roof. If the space is enclosed, the impurity is restricted to the “tent”; anything above the ceiling and below the floor of the “tent” is pure. But if the entire space between floor and ceiling is filled with matter, there is no tent and the impurity extends indefinitely above and below the tent space. This is known as “squeezed impurity” (<a class="refLink" data-ref="Mishnah Oholot 15:1" href="/Mishnah_Oholot.15.1">Mishnah <i>Ahilut</i> 15:1</a>,<a class="refLink" data-ref="Mishnah Oholot 15:5" href="/Mishnah_Oholot.15.5">5</a>,<a class="refLink" data-ref="Mishnah Oholot 15:6" href="/Mishnah_Oholot.15.6">6</a>). It is implied in <a class="refLink" data-ref="Tosefta Oholot 15:5" href="/Tosefta_Oholot.15.5">Tosephta <i>Ahilut</i>15:5</a> that R. Yose restricts “squeezed impurity” to material permanently deposited; but a storage of straw which is to be removed in the future is not counted as filler.</i>? Rebbi Yose ben Rebbi Abun in the name of Rav Ḥisda: It is everybody’s opinion. What Rebbi Yose said, if he mixed it with dust<sup class="footnote-marker">184</sup><i class="footnote">Not really “mixed with”, but “treated like,” as formulated in the Tosephta.</i>. “There is straw which is treated like dust and dust which is treated like straw. Straw not to be removed is like dust; dust to be removed is like straw.<sup class="footnote-marker">185</sup><i class="footnote">Statement of R. Yose in <a class="refLink" data-ref="Tosefta Oholot 15:5" href="/Tosefta_Oholot.15.5">Tosephta <i>Ahilut</i> 15:5</a>; quoted in <a class="refLink" data-ref="Eruvin 79a" href="/Eruvin.79a"><i>Eruvin</i> 79a</a>. “Straw” stands here for “material to be removed,” “dust” for “permanent filling.”</i>” In the House of Rebbi Yannai they said: If he covered it with mats it is disregarded. Come and see: If he filled it with mats it is not disregarded<sup class="footnote-marker">186</sup><i class="footnote">Since the filling can easily be removed, the ditch still separates.</i>, if he covered it with mats it is disregarded<sup class="footnote-marker">187</sup><i class="footnote">If a ditch is filled with any material, even straw, but this is covered with mats to create a floor from one side to the other, the courtyards become one and require one <i>eruv. Šabbat</i> 100a.</i>. If he filled it with branches of date palms it is problematic<sup class="footnote-marker">188</sup><i class="footnote">No ruling is available in this case.</i>. Rebbi Zeriqan, Rebbi Immi, in the name of Rebbi Simeon ben Laqish: Even thin sheets<sup class="footnote-marker">189</sup><i class="footnote">This translation is tentative; it follows the <i>Pesaḥim</i> text, reading רַק. Neither the text in <i>Eruvin</i> רוֹק “spittle” nor the one in K and <i>Nazir</i> רֵיק “emptiness” are appropriate.</i>.
“What is a grave of the abyss? Any which nobody remembers.” Should we not be cautious and say, maybe one at the end of the world knows<sup class="footnote-marker">190</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Tosefta Zavim 2:5" href="/Tosefta_Zavim.2.5">Tosephta <i>Zavim</i> 2:9</a>, <a class="refLink" data-ref="Pesachim 81b" href="/Pesachim.81b">Babli 81b</a>.</i>? And is the permanence of the living not like living<sup class="footnote-marker">191</sup><i class="footnote">He might know of the grave even if we do not.</i>? Explain that he was found compressed<sup class="footnote-marker">192</sup><i class="footnote">Cf. <i>Giṭtin</i> 3:3, Notes 81,87. If any person left from here, when that person left he was alive and we have to apply the legal principle of permanence of the status quo and consider him permanently alive, disregarding the notion of “unknown grave”.</i>.
It was stated: “Only a corpse creates a grave of the abyss.”<sup class="footnote-marker">193</sup><i class="footnote">Which clearly shows that he was not buried by humans but was the victim of an accident. Since the accident was not noticed when it occurred, there is nobody “at the end of the world” who would know of it.<br><a class="refLink" data-ref="Tosefta Zavim 2:5" href="/Tosefta_Zavim.2.5">Tosephta <i>Zavim</i> 2:9</a>, <a class="refLink" data-ref="Pesachim 80b" href="/Pesachim.80b">Babli 80b</a>.</i> Therefore, not a carcass<sup class="footnote-marker">194</sup><i class="footnote">Obviously, only a human corpse has a grave that presents problems of impurity. A buried animal carcass does not produce impurity. Carcasses cause impurity only when touched or carried. The meaning of this sentence can be clarified: Only for the impurity of the dead do we find a rule that sometimes allows one to disregard biblical impurity.</i>&lt;sub&gt;.&lt;/sub&gt; An argument <i>de minore ad maius.</i> Since a corpse, which does not cause impurity of couch and seat, creates a grave of the abyss, should a carcasss which causes impurity of couch and seat not create a grave of the abyss? Why was it said that only a corpse creates a grave of the abyss? To exclude couch and seat<sup class="footnote-marker">195</sup><i class="footnote">This argument does not make any sense. There are several distinct ways to emend the passage to create sense; therefore, no textual emendation is proposed but the meaning can easily be clarified.<br>A person who is the source of his own impurity (a male or female sufferer from genital discharges) causes original impurity to any couch or personal seat he is using (<a class="refLink" data-ref="Leviticus 15:4-6" href="/Leviticus.15.4-6">Lev. 15:4–6</a>,<a class="refLink" data-ref="Leviticus 21-22" href="/Leviticus.21-22">21–22</a>,<a class="refLink" data-ref="Leviticus 15:26" href="/Leviticus.15.26">26</a>). But any impurity induced on an inanimate object by a corpse is only derivative. The argument shows that the rules of the impurity of the dead and impurity produced by a living human body are not comparable: Each kind of impurity has its own severities and leniencies not found in the other.<br>Here ends the parallel to <i>Nazir.</i></i>.
There, we have stated<sup class="footnote-marker">196</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Mishnah Zevachim 2:1" href="/Mishnah_Zevachim.2.1">Mishnah <i>Zevaḥim</i> 2:1</a>.</i>: “All sacrifices whose blood was collected by a non-Cohen, a deep mourner<sup class="footnote-marker">197</sup><i class="footnote">A person obligated to bury a close relative, such as defined in <a class="refLink" data-ref="Leviticus 21:2-3" href="/Leviticus.21.2-3"><i>Lev.</i> 21:2–3</a>, who from the moment of the death to the burial is barred from all sacral acts; inferred from <a class="refLink" data-ref="Deuteronomy 26:14" href="/Deuteronomy.26.14"><i>Deut.</i> 26:14</a>.</i>, one immersed on this day<sup class="footnote-marker">198</sup><i class="footnote">Who is no longer impure but barred from sacral acts until sundown; <a class="refLink" data-ref="Leviticus 22:7" href="/Leviticus.22.7"><i>Lev.</i> 22:7</a>.</i>, missing garments<sup class="footnote-marker">199</sup><i class="footnote">A Cohen serving while not wearing all priestly garments commits a deadly sin; <a class="refLink" data-ref="Exodus 28:43" href="/Exodus.28.43"><i>Ex.</i>28:43</a>.</i>, missing atonement<sup class="footnote-marker">200</sup><i class="footnote">A person healed from skin disease or gonorrhea who needs not only immersion in water and waiting for sundown but is excluded from sacral rites until be bring a purifying sacrifice, <a class="refLink" data-ref="Leviticus 14:1-32" href="/Leviticus.14.1-32"><i>Lev.</i> 14:1–32</a> for skin disease, 15:14–15 for the sufferer from gonorrhea.</i>, with unwashed hands or feet<sup class="footnote-marker">201</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Exodus 30:19-20" href="/Exodus.30.19-20"><i>Ex</i>. 30:19–20</a>.</i>, uncircumcised<sup class="footnote-marker">202</sup><i class="footnote">As the Babli points out, <a class="refLink" data-ref="Zevachim 22b" href="/Zevachim.22b"><i>Zevaḥim</i> 22b</a>, there is no pentateuchal verse forbidding service to an uncircumcised priest, but there is one in <a class="refLink" data-ref="Ezekiel 44:9" href="/Ezekiel.44.9">Ezechiel, 44:9</a>, which forbids entry to the Temple domain to any uncircumcised person, including a hemophiliac who may not be circumcised.</i>, impure<sup class="footnote-marker">203</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Leviticus 22:2-3" href="/Leviticus.22.2-3"><i>Lev.</i> 22:2–3</a>.</i>, sitting<sup class="footnote-marker">204</sup><i class="footnote">Since the verses never permit any action in sitting, and the priests are required to be barefoot, no service is possible unless the priest is standing with his feet in direct contact with the floor of the Temple court, the Temple interior, or the altar.</i>, standing on utensils, on [an animal, on] another person<sup class="footnote-marker">205</sup><i class="footnote">Meaning that another priest puts his hands under the feet of the officiating priest. Then he is not in contact with the floor.</i>, disqualified it.” The Southerners say, we hold this for those impure by the impurity of gonorrhea or the impurity of skin disease<sup class="footnote-marker">206</sup><i class="footnote">They read the expression “impurity of the body” used in the Mishnah to describe what the diadem does not make acceptable as impurity caused by the person’s body (i. e., in addition to skin disease and gonorrhea also sexual activity, <a class="refLink" data-ref="Leviticus 15:15" href="/Leviticus.15.15"><i>Lev.</i> 15:15</a>,<a class="refLink" data-ref="Leviticus 15:18" href="/Leviticus.15.18">18</a>.)</i>, but impurity of the dead does not desecrate since it was permitted in case of the impurity of the many for the <i>Pesaḥ.</i> Rebbi Simeon ben Laqish objected to the Southerners: Since for the owner, where you clarified to his advantage in case of all other impurities during the course of the year<sup class="footnote-marker">207</sup><i class="footnote">They may send their sacrifices through an agent if they are disabled by impurity.</i>, you clarified to his disadvantage in case of impurity of the dead for <i>Pesaḥ</i><sup class="footnote-marker">208</sup><i class="footnote">He must celebrate the Second <i>Pesaḥ.</i></i><i>,</i> for the officiant, where you clarified to his disadvantage in case of all other impurities during the course of the year<sup class="footnote-marker">209</sup><i class="footnote">He may never serve being impure.</i>, it is only logical that you should clarify to his disadvantage in case of impurity of the dead for <i>Pesaḥ.</i> In addition to what Rebbi stated, “the diadem makes impurity of the blood acceptable but not impurity of the body.” If you want to say that this refers to the impurity of gonorrhea or the impurity of skin disease, you cannot, since we have stated, “if the impurity was caused by impurity of the abyss<sup class="footnote-marker">82</sup><i class="footnote">Impurity buried in the ground which previously was totally unknown and is only recently uncovered. Since it is impossible to guard against this kind of impurity there can be no penalty for “tent impurity” of this kind.</i>, the diadem makes acceptable.<sup class="footnote-marker">210</sup><i class="footnote">Since impurity of the abyss only is caused by a corpse, it is not caused by the person’s body. If it is stated that the diadem makes acceptable in this case, it follows that the diadem is inactive in all cases of known impurity caused by external influences.</i>” What are the Southerners doing with this? They explain if for the owner<sup class="footnote-marker">211</sup><i class="footnote">The diadem only covers abyss impurity of the owner, but not proven impurity of the dead; one may still read “impurity of the body” as referring to impurity produced by the body.</i>. But did we not state “a <i>nazir”</i><sup class="footnote-marker">212</sup><i class="footnote">The only impurity forbidden for the <i>nazir</i> is the impurity of the dead, so in <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Pesachim 7:12:2" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Pesachim.7.12.2">Mishnah 5</a> the reference must be to this kind of impurity.</i><i>?</i> They explain it for the officiant. In Rebbi Simeon ben Laqish’s opinion, there is no difference; it is equal for owner or officiant. Rebbi Jeremiah said, this is an argument <i>de minore ad maius</i> that can be contradicted, for they can say to him, no. If you argue about the owner whose position you clarified to his disadvantage in the case of the infirm and the aged<sup class="footnote-marker">177</sup><i class="footnote">While a person unable to eat the volume of an olive of the <i>Pesaḥ</i> may not subscribe to it, an old or sick priest is able to serve in the Temple as long as his infirmity is not of the kind listed in <i>Lev,</i> 21:18–20.</i>, what can you say about the officiating, whose position you clarified to his advantage in the case of the infirm and the aged. And any argument <i>de minore ad majus</i> that can be contradicted, the argument <i>de minore ad majus</i> is invalid. Rebbi Ḥananiah said, this is an argument <i>de minore ad majus</i> that can be contradicted, for they can say to him, no. If you argue about the owner for whom the circumcision of his males and his slaves are indispensable for him<sup class="footnote-marker">213</sup><i class="footnote">Since <a class="refLink" data-ref="Exodus 12:48" href="/Exodus.12.48"><i>Ex</i>. 12:48</a> notes that <i>no one uncircumcised may eat it</i> [the <i>Pesaḥ],</i> in <a class="refLink" data-ref="Exodus 12:44" href="/Exodus.12.44">v. 44</a>, <i>a man’s slave, bought with money, if you circumcise him he may eat it,</i> “he” is read to refer to the owner; the owner may not eat <i>Pesaḥ</i> if there are uncircumcised males in his <i>familia. Mekhilta dR. Ismael Bo</i> 15, <i>dR. Simeon ben Yoḥai</i> p. 35</i>, what can you say about the officiating, for whom the circumcision of his males and his slaves are not indispensable<sup class="footnote-marker">214</sup><i class="footnote">Cf. <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Pesachim 7:7:8" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Pesachim.7.7.8">Note 202</a>. An uncircumcised Cohen may not serve; nothing is said about his dependents.</i>. And any argument <i>de minore ad majus</i> that can be contradicted, the argument <i>de minore ad majus</i> is invalid.
Rebbi Isaac bar Gufta asked before Rebbi Mana: If an individual could learn from the public for the <i>Pesaḥ,</i> the officiant during the rest of the year might infer from the public for the <i>Pesaḥ</i><sup class="footnote-marker">215</sup><i class="footnote">But since the individual must make a Second <i>Pesaḥ</i> which the public never makes, the original argument of R. Simeon ben Laqish is incorrect.</i><i>.</i> Rebbi Immi asked: how do you explain this “impure”? Impure by the impurity of gonorrhea or the impurity of skin disease? But did we not state, “missing atonement”? If he desecrates when he had been immersed, not so much more before he was immersed<sup class="footnote-marker">216</sup><i class="footnote">The statement of <a class="refLink" data-ref="Mishnah Zevachim 2:1" href="/Mishnah_Zevachim.2.1">Mishnah <i>Zevaḥim</i> 2:1</a> seems redundant.</i>! How do you explain “immersed on this day”? If he immersed himself on that day because of a corpse. Come and see: the one impure from a corpse does not desecrate, not so much more one immersed on that day because of a corpse? But he must be immersed on that day because of a crawling animal<sup class="footnote-marker">147</sup><i class="footnote">He is impure, but can become free of impurity by immersion in a <i>miqweh,</i> which will make him pure for <i>sancta</i> at sundown. This kind of impurity does not prevent a person to be counted in a group eating the <i>Pesaḥ</i> in purity; accepting the person in the count of the impure is questionable; <a class="refLink" data-ref="Pesachim 80a" href="/Pesachim.80a">Babli 80a</a>, <a class="refLink" data-ref="Pesachim 80b" href="/Pesachim.80b">80b</a>.</i>. Come and see: the immersed on that day because of a corpse does not desecrate, not so much more one immersed on that day because of a crawling animal<sup class="footnote-marker">217</sup><i class="footnote">And from impurity of a corpse one has to wait for seven days while of a dead crawling animal one may immerse himself immediately.</i>? Rebbi Samuel bar Yudan said, people having touched sufferers from gonorrhea<sup class="footnote-marker">218</sup><i class="footnote">Who are impure until sundown after immediate immersion in water, <a class="refLink" data-ref="Leviticus 15:4" href="/Leviticus.15.4"><i>Lev.</i> 15:4</a>,<a class="refLink" data-ref="Leviticus 15:7" href="/Leviticus.15.7">7</a>.</i>. The rabbis of Caesarea explain everything from a sufferer from gonorrhea<sup class="footnote-marker">152</sup><i class="footnote">A person who suffers a single episode of gonorrhea is impure for the day and can be purified by immersion in a <i>miqweh.</i> If he has two episodes in at most two consecutive days, he is impure for seven days; after seven days in remission he can be purified by immersion in a <i>miqweh.</i> After three episodes he still needs seven days in remission but then is still prohibited <i>sancta</i> unless on the eighth day he brings a couple of birds as sacrifice to the Temple. A sufferer from gonorrhea who is impure for seven days, on the seventh day is a questionable candidate for <i>Pesaḥ</i> since if he suffers another episode he has to start all over again.</i>. “One immersed on this day<sup class="footnote-marker">198</sup><i class="footnote">Who is no longer impure but barred from sacral acts until sundown; <a class="refLink" data-ref="Leviticus 22:7" href="/Leviticus.22.7"><i>Lev.</i> 22:7</a>.</i>,” if he had one episode. “Impure” (in the impurity of the dead)<sup class="footnote-marker">218*</sup><i class="footnote">The text in parentheses has to be deleted even though it is confirmed by K.</i> if he had two episodes. “Missing atonement<sup class="footnote-marker">200</sup><i class="footnote">A person healed from skin disease or gonorrhea who needs not only immersion in water and waiting for sundown but is excluded from sacral rites until be bring a purifying sacrifice, <a class="refLink" data-ref="Leviticus 14:1-32" href="/Leviticus.14.1-32"><i>Lev.</i> 14:1–32</a> for skin disease, 15:14–15 for the sufferer from gonorrhea.</i>,” if he had three episodes. Are people having touched a sufferer from gonorrhea like a sufferer from gonorrhea in the opinion of the Southerners? Let us hear from the following, as Rebbi Eleazar said in the name of Rebbi Hoshaia: <i>Aaron shall carry the iniquities of the sacrifices</i><sup class="footnote-marker">97</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Exodus 28:38" href="/Exodus.28.38"><i>Ex.</i> 28:38</a>. Explained in more detail in the <a class="refLink" data-ref="Pesachim 16b" href="/Pesachim.16b">Babli 16b</a>, <a class="refLink" data-ref="Yoma 7a" href="/Yoma.7a"><i>Yoma</i> 7a</a>, <a class="refLink" data-ref="Zevachim 23a" href="/Zevachim.23a"><i>Zevaḥim</i> 23a</a>.</i><i>,</i> the iniquities of the sacrifices, not the iniquities of the sacrificers<sup class="footnote-marker">98</sup><i class="footnote">The diadem will not cover deficiencies in either the owners or the officiants of a sacrifice. <a class="refLink" data-ref="Zevachim 23b" href="/Zevachim.23b">Babli <i>Zevaḥim</i> 23b</a>.</i>. What is iniquity of the sacrifices? The blood of a sufferer from gonorrhea? No, what was touched by a sufferer from gonorrhea<sup class="footnote-marker">219</sup><i class="footnote">Since gonorrhea causes impurity only in humans, the impurity cannot be the victim’s.</i>. Similarly, the iniquity of the sacrificers, who touched a sufferer from gonorrhea. This implies that if the public were impure because they had touched sufferers from gonorrhea or women suffering from flux, they cannot make it<sup class="footnote-marker">220</sup><i class="footnote">The only cause for <i>Pesaḥ</i> in impurity is the impurity of the dead.</i> in impurity.

Halakhah 8

<strong>MISHNAH:</strong> If it became impure whole or most of it, one burns it before the citadel on altar wood. If a minor part became impure or leftovers<sup class="footnote-marker">220a</sup><i class="footnote">What was not eaten by midnight (<a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Pesachim 7:12:1" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Pesachim.7.12.1">Mishnah 10</a>:)</i> one burns in the courtyards or on their roofs on their own wood. The misers burn it before the citadel in order to profit from altar wood.
<strong>HALAKHAH:</strong> Rebbi Ḥama bar Uqba in the name of Rebbi Yose ben Ḥanina: To publicize him, to make it known that he spoiled it<sup class="footnote-marker">221</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Pesachim 81b" href="/Pesachim.81b">Babli 81b</a>.</i>. If he said, I am going to burn it before the citadel on my own wood, one does not listen to him; it is not necessary to note that if he says, I will burn it on my roof on my own wood that one does not listen to him<sup class="footnote-marker">222</sup><i class="footnote">Here it refers to the Mishnah here; but the statement in <a class="refLink" data-ref="Tosefta Pesachim (Lieberman) 3:13" href="/Tosefta_Pesachim_(Lieberman).3.13">Tosephta 3:13</a> that before the citadel one may not use private wood refers to Mishnah 3:8 (Note 150), and emphasizes that before the citadel one never uses any but altar wood.</i>.
Rebbi Jeremiah in the name of Rebbi Hila: To inform the next in line that he is a miser. You should know that nowhere else is he called miser, but here you are calling him miser<sup class="footnote-marker">223</sup><i class="footnote">This now refers to the end of the Mishnah. In <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Pesachim 3:8:1" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Pesachim.3.8.1">Mishnah 3:8</a>, where people burn disqualified private sacral meat before the citadel on altar wood, they are not called miser.</i>. They made it easy for the guest<sup class="footnote-marker">224</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Pesachim 82a" href="/Pesachim.82a">Babli 82a</a>. Most people in Jerusalem at holiday time are guests, without their own supply of fire wood.</i>.
<sup class="footnote-marker">225</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Yoma 2b" href="/Yoma.2b"><i>Yoma</i> 2b</a>, <a class="refLink" data-ref="Zevachim 104b" href="/Zevachim.104b"><i>Zevaḥim</i> 104b</a>.</i> Rebbi Joḥanan said, a tower was standing on the Temple Mount which was called “citadel”. Rebbi Simeon ben Laqish said, the entire Temple Mount was called citadel, <i>to do everything and to build the citadel which I prepared</i><sup class="footnote-marker">226</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="I Chronicles 28:19" href="/I_Chronicles.28.19"><i>1Chr.</i> 28:19</a>.</i>.

Halakhah 9

<strong>MISHNAH:</strong> <i>Pesaḥ</i> which left<sup class="footnote-marker">227</sup><i class="footnote">The walls of Jerusalem.</i> or which became impure has to be burned immediately<sup class="footnote-marker">228</sup><i class="footnote">On the 14th of Nisan.</i>. If the owners became impure or died it shall lose its shape<sup class="footnote-marker">229</sup><i class="footnote">Be spoiled and become unusable as sacral meat.</i> and be brought to the place of burning<sup class="footnote-marker">229a</sup><i class="footnote">The place where disqualified sacrifices and those to be burned outside the sacred domain have to be disposed of.</i>. Rebbi Joḥanan ben Beroqa says, this one also has to be burned immediately since it has no eaters.
<strong>HALAKHAH:</strong> Rebbi Ḥiyya stated<sup class="footnote-marker">230</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Pesachim 34b" href="/Pesachim.34b">Babli 34b</a>, <a class="refLink" data-ref="Pesachim 73b" href="/Pesachim.73b">73b</a>, <a class="refLink" data-ref="Pesachim 82b" href="/Pesachim.82b">82b</a>; <a class="refLink" data-ref="Tosefta Pesachim (Lieberman) 6:6" href="/Tosefta_Pesachim_(Lieberman).6.6">Tosephta 6:6</a>. As K shows, the corrector’s additions are superfluous and should be deleted.</i>: “A disqualification of the body [is <i>piggul</i> and] is immediately burned. [If the owners became impure or died it is] a disqualification of enabler and needs to lose its shape. Rebbi Yose said, the Mishnah says so: <i>“Pesaḥ</i> which left or which became impure is a disqualification of the body and has to be burned immediately. If the owner became impure or died it is a disqualification of the enabler and it shall lose its shape.”
Rebbi Ḥama bar Uqba in the name of Rebbi Yose bar Ḥanina: Rebbi Nehemiah and Rebbi Joḥanan ben Beroqa both said the same<sup class="footnote-marker">231</sup><i class="footnote">That under certain circumstances a disqualified sacrifice must be burned immediately, without waiting that it lose its shape, even if the disqualification is not in the victim’s body.</i>, as it was stated<sup class="footnote-marker">232</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Sifra, Braita d'Rabbi Yishmael" href="/Sifra,_Braita_d'Rabbi_Yishmael"><i>Sifra Šeminy Pereq</i> 2(8–10</a>).</i>: “it was burned because of deep mourning<sup class="footnote-marker">233</sup><i class="footnote">This is R. Nehemiah’s statement. The discussion refers to <a class="refLink" data-ref="Leviticus 10:16-17" href="/Leviticus.10.16-17"><i>Lev.</i> 10:16–17</a>. Since tradition fixes the inauguration of Tabernacle and Priesthood on a First of Nisan <i>(Seder Olam</i> Chapter 7, in the author’s edition p. 82; cf. Rashi <i>ad</i> 9:1), there were three goats as purification offering: the one required for every New Moon <a class="refLink" data-ref="Numbers 28:15" href="/Numbers.28.15"><i>(Num.</i> 28:15</a>), the people’s initiation sacrifice <a class="refLink" data-ref="Leviticus 10:3" href="/Leviticus.10.3"><i>(Lev.</i> 10:3</a>), and the one offered by the chief of the tribe of Judah <a class="refLink" data-ref="Numbers 7:16" href="/Numbers.7.16"><i>(Num.</i> 7:16</a>). Only the first of these was presented pursuant a permanent law; the other two were one time affairs from which no conclusions could be drawn for generally valid principles. R. Nehemiah holds that since a  deep mourner on the day of burial is biblically excluded from all sacral rites, the order given in 18:12–15 to Aaron and his sons to eat <i>sancta</i> even though Aaron’s sons Nadav and Avihu had been buried on that day necessarily was restricted to the one time offerings of that day, to the exclusion of offerings presented following a permanent prescription. But the mourning of the priests is a condition of the enablers, not of the victim, and nevertheless Moses agreed that the purification offering correctly had been burned and not eaten.</i>? Was it not burned only because of impurity? But it was not burned because of impurity, since if it had been burned because of mourning, all three of them<sup class="footnote-marker">234</sup><i class="footnote">Since in Moses’s order to eat the <i>sancta</i> purification offerings are not mentioned.</i> should have been burned. Another opinion, was not Phineas with them<sup class="footnote-marker">235</sup><i class="footnote">Phineas was born in Egypt <a class="refLink" data-ref="Exodus 6:25" href="/Exodus.6.25"><i>(Ex.</i> 6:25</a>). As a nephew of Nadav and Avihu he had no biblical obligation to mourn and could legally have eaten all sacrifices. Since there was one eater, R. Joḥanan ben Beroqa would agree that the sacrifice cannot be burned.</i>? Another opinion, would it not have been permitted to be eaten in the evening<sup class="footnote-marker">236</sup><i class="footnote">Since the talmudic rule is that only the day of burial is biblically forbidden. While his sons would have to observe seven days of mourning, the High Priest is forbidden mourning where it is not prescribed; in the following night he could have joined Phineas. Purification offerings are eaten by the priests during the day of offering and the following night.</i>?” In the opinion of Rebbi Nehemiah it should be burned but be counted<sup class="footnote-marker">237</sup><i class="footnote">There is no doubt that the obligation for which the sacrifice was brought had been fulfilled.</i>. Rebbi Nehemiah is of the opinion that all three of them were burned. Should not Phineas have eaten? He was not yet appointed {High} Priest<sup class="footnote-marker">238</sup><i class="footnote">In the initiation rites <a class="refLink" data-ref="Leviticus 8" href="/Leviticus.8"><i>(Lev.</i> Chapter 8</a>), only Aaron and his sons are mentioned, not his grandson Phineas. This is the basis of the opinion that Phineas was not originally included in the priesthood; priesthood was conferred on him only after the incident with Zimry <a class="refLink" data-ref="Numbers 25:13" href="/Numbers.25.13"><i>(Num.</i> 25:13</a>); <a class="refLink" data-ref="Zevachim 101b" href="/Zevachim.101b">Babli <i>Zevaḥim</i> 101b</a>.</i>. Should not Aaron have eaten in the evening? Rebbi Nehemiah is of the opinion that deeo mourning in the night is from the Torah. Rebbi Jeremiah said, also Rebbi Yose the Galilean is with them<sup class="footnote-marker">239</sup><i class="footnote">In the same Chapter of <i>Sifra</i> (Halakhah 5), he deduces from <a class="refLink" data-ref="Leviticus 10:18" href="/Leviticus.10.18"><i>Lev.</i> 10:18</a> that any purification sacrifice whose blood was brought into the sanctuary is disqualified and must be burned immediately. This proves that he agrees with R. Nehemiah that the verses have to be interpreted referring to the ordinary Temple service, and that disqualification of the enabler may trigger an obligation of immediate burning.</i>. <sup class="footnote-marker">240</sup><i class="footnote">This paragraph has no direct connection with the preceding; the connection being that R. Yose the Galilean interprets <a class="refLink" data-ref="Leviticus 10:18" href="/Leviticus.10.18"><i>Lev.</i>10:18</a>.</i> And we have stated there:<sup class="footnote-marker">241</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Mishnah Zevachim 8:12" href="/Mishnah_Zevachim.8.12">Mishnah <i>Zevaḥim</i> 8:12</a>.</i> “A purification sacrifice whose blood was received in two cups, of which one was brought outside<sup class="footnote-marker">242</sup><i class="footnote">Since purification sacrifice has to be eaten by the priests in the Temple courtyard <a class="refLink" data-ref="Leviticus 6:19" href="/Leviticus.6.19"><i>(Lev.</i> 6:19</a>), if any part leaves the sacred domain it becomes disqualified. Since pouring the blood on the walls of the altar enables the meat to be eaten, if blood is brought outside before it was poured the sacrifice is disqualified.</i>; the one inside is qualified. If one of them was brought to the interior<sup class="footnote-marker">243</sup><i class="footnote">As noted later, this is required/permitted only in extraordinary cases. The Mishnah here refers to ordinary sacrifices. Since then the blood is not in the courtyard, it is outside its prescribed domain and disqualified.</i>, Rebbi Yose the Galilean declares qualified but the Sages declare disqualified. [Rebbi Yose the Galilean said, since in a case where intent disqualifies outside<sup class="footnote-marker">244</sup><i class="footnote">Slaughtering a victim with the intent of pouring the blood outside the sacred precinct disqualifies the sacrifice; <a class="refLink" data-ref="Mishnah Zevachim 2:2" href="/Mishnah_Zevachim.2.2">Mishnah <i>Zevaḥim</i> 2:2</a>.<br>The text in brackets was added by a corrector from a different source; it is neither in the scribe’s text nor in K.</i> the remainder was not made equal to what was brought outside, in a case where intent does not disqualify in the interior<sup class="footnote-marker">245</sup><i class="footnote">The intent to pour the blood in the Temple itself does not disqualify; <a class="refLink" data-ref="Mishnah Zevachim 3:6" href="/Mishnah_Zevachim.3.6">Mishnah <i>Zevaḥim</i> 3:6</a>.</i> is it not logical that we not make the remainder to what was brought inside? If it was brought into the interior to atone, even if it did not atone it is disqualified, the words of Rebbi Eliezer<sup class="footnote-marker">246</sup><i class="footnote">The fact that the blood was inside when it should not have been makes it “outside its place” and disqualifies.</i>. Rebbi Simeon says, only if it atones<sup class="footnote-marker">247</sup><i class="footnote">Only if something was done against the rules with the blood; the interior of the Temple still is sacred domain.</i>. Rebbi Jehudah says, if it was brought into the interior in error, it remains qualified. Of all disqualified blood which one gave on the altar, the diadem only makes the impure acceptable; for the diadem makes the impure acceptable but not what was brought outside.”] Rebbi Eleazar said, you have to know that for Rebbi Yose the Galilean it is disqualification of the enabler since the other part is outside<sup class="footnote-marker">248</sup><i class="footnote">In the case that one cup was brought to the interior.</i> and it is qualified. You have to know that for the rabbis it is disqualification of the body since it is within its enclosure<sup class="footnote-marker">249</sup><i class="footnote">Since one cup remained outside, it could be poured on the walls of the altar even if the cup inside became unusable.</i> and it is disqualified.
