A can pay for B’s sacrifices as long as no money comes into B’s hand, since sacrifices dedicated for B are Heaven’s, not B’s property.</i>. Explain it if nothing was given into his hand; you should know as it was stated there<sup class="footnote-marker">73</sup><i class="footnote">This paragraph also is in <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Beitzah 5:2:2-16" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Beitzah.5.2.2-16"><i>Beṣah</i> 5:2</a> (<b>צ</b>).</i>, “he can bring for him nests for male or female sufferers from genital discharges, nests for childbirth;” not if nothing came into his hands? Here also if nothing came into his<sup class="footnote-marker">71</sup><i class="footnote">This must be “her”. R. Simeon ben Laqish holds that a sacrifice in the hands of a prostitute is barred from the Temple, but if the prostitute is paid by a subscription to his <i>Pesaḥ</i> or his festival offering it is an acceptable arrangement. <a class="refLink" data-ref="Temurah 30b" href="/Temurah.30b"><i>Temurah</i> 30b</a>.</i> hands.
<sup class="footnote-marker">73</sup><i class="footnote">This paragraph also is in <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Beitzah 5:2:2-16" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Beitzah.5.2.2-16"><i>Beṣah</i> 5:2</a> (<b>צ</b>).</i> Rebbi Jacob bar Aḥa in the name of Rebbi Immi: Rebbi Joḥanan and Rebbi Simeon ben Laqish disagreed. One said, one dedicates; the other said, one does not dedicate. The rabbis of Caesarea make it explicit: Rebbi Joḥanan  said, one dedicates without problems on a holiday; Rebbi Simeon ben Laqish said, one does not dedicate, without problems on a holiday<sup class="footnote-marker">74</sup><i class="footnote">There is no doubt that biblically one is permitted to dedicate animals as sacrifices on a holiday; the question is whether there is a rabbinic prohibition.</i>. There are Tannaim who state, he goes to sellers of lambs; there are Tannaim who state, he goes to sellers of <i>Pesaḥim</i><sup class="footnote-marker">75</sup><i class="footnote">If the 14th of Nisan is a Sabbath. In the first formulation, the lambs are profane and have to be dedicated on the Sabbath to be permitted into the Temple court; in the second version they already are dedicated (cf. <a class="refLink" data-ref="Shabbat 148b" href="/Shabbat.148b">Babli <i>Šabbat</i> 148b</a>).</i><i>.</i> He who says, he goes to sellers of lambs, follows him who says, one dedicates. He who says, he goes to sellers of <i>Pesaḥim,</i> follows him who says, one does not dedicate. This implies that it does not become profane and then dedicated again. If you would say that it becomes profane and then dedicated again, it should be forbidden because of dedicating, and we have stated, “one does not dedicate.<sup class="footnote-marker">76</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Beitzah 5:2:1" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Beitzah.5.2.1">Mishnah <i>Beṣah</i> 5:2</a>.</i>” Rebbi Ḥananiah and Rebbi Mana, one said, if he dedicates for the next day; but the other said, if he dedicated for the upkeep of the Temple<sup class="footnote-marker">77</sup><i class="footnote">Dedication of a sacrifice to be eaten on the holiday has to be considered part of the preparation of food and is permitted; what the Mishnah forbids are dedications either not for use on the holiday or not for food at all.</i>. Rebbi Shammai said, even for him who said that one dedicates<sup class="footnote-marker">78</sup><i class="footnote">It seems that one has to read “that one does not dedicate”. Since <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Beitzah 5:2:1" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Beitzah.5.2.1">Mishnah <i>Beṣah</i>5:2</a> explicitly declares that the prohibition of dedication of sacrifices is rabbinical, it implies that inside the Temple precinct proper the prohibition does not apply. In this situation there is no disagreement between R. Joḥanan and R. Simeon ben Laqish and no inference may be drawn about the status of monies dedicated for <i>Pesaḥ.</i></i>, in the Temple Court because rabbinic Sabbath prohibitions were permitted in the Temple.
From where that one subscribes? The verse says, <i>by the number of souls</i><sup class="footnote-marker">79</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Exodus 12:4" href="/Exodus.12.4"><i>Ex.</i> 12:4</a>. By biblical decree a person not counted as participant is barred from eating the <i>Pesaḥ.</i> <a class="refLink" data-ref="Pesachim 89a" href="/Pesachim.89a">Babli 89a</a>.</i><i>.</i> From where that one appoints<sup class="footnote-marker">80</sup><i class="footnote">Appoints people as eaters.</i>? It is said here <i>a lamb,</i> and it is said in Egypt <i>a lamb.</i> Since the lamb quoted in Egypt is live, not slaughtered, so the lamb quoted here is live, not slaughtered<sup class="footnote-marker">81</sup><i class="footnote">“Lamb” is mentioned in v. 12:4 which, since its topic is not otherwise dealt with in the Pentateuch, refers to <i>Pesaḥ</i> at all times. “Lamb” also is mentioned in v. 12:3 which uniquely refers to the <i>Pesaḥ</i> in Egypt since only there was the lamb selected on the 10th of Nisan. Since the lamb was slaughtered only in the evening of the 14th; on both occasions the reference is to a living lamb. This implies that the count must be made while the lamb is alive, the position of the anonymous majority.</i>. What is Rebbi Simeon’s reason? If he dies between slaughtering and pouring, would it not count for the owner as merit? What is the difference between the owner dying or the owner withdrawing from it<sup class="footnote-marker">83</sup><i class="footnote">A person subscribed to a <i>Pesaḥ</i> as an individual but now appears with several people which he has invited without paying for them. They may give him the portion of an individual and tell him to divide it among his guests while everybody else get the full volume for which he has paid.</i>.

Halakhah 4

<strong>MISHNAH:</strong> If somebody lets others subscribe to his part, they are empowered to give him his part, so that he eats of his and they eat of theirs<sup class="footnote-marker">83</sup><i class="footnote">A person subscribed to a <i>Pesaḥ</i> as an individual but now appears with several people which he has invited without paying for them. They may give him the portion of an individual and tell him to divide it among his guests while everybody else get the full volume for which he has paid.</i>.
<strong>HALAKHAH:</strong> The members of a group of which one had beautiful hands<sup class="footnote-marker">84</sup><i class="footnote">The traditional explanation is: He grabs a lot and eats an inordinate amount of food. <a class="refLink" data-ref="Pesachim 89b" href="/Pesachim.89b">Babli 89b</a>, <a class="refLink" data-ref="Tosefta Pesachim (Lieberman) 7:9" href="/Tosefta_Pesachim_(Lieberman).7.9">Tosephta 7:9</a>.</i> were entitled to tell him, take your part and eat alone Not only <i>Pesaḥ,</i> but even if they made a meal by contributions<sup class="footnote-marker">85</sup><i class="footnote">Greek συμβόλαια, τὰ, “contributions to partake in a common meal/”</i> they are entitled to tell him, take your part and eat alone, if they did know him<sup class="footnote-marker">86</sup><i class="footnote">They did know from the start that letting him participate might be unfair to the remainder of the group.</i>, since this was a stipulation from the start.
Rav Huna said, if somebody dedicated his <i>Pesaḥ</i> and said, on condition that nobody else subscribe with me, nobody else can subscribe with him. If he dedicated it without specification, any who join are its subscribers<sup class="footnote-marker">87</sup><i class="footnote">From the start the <i>Pesaḥ</i> is dedicated for anybody who will come to join.</i>. Rebbi Jacob bar Aḥa in the name of Rebbi Zeˋira: Does the Mishnah say so? “<i>If the</i><i>house be less</i><sup class="footnote-marker">88</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Exodus 12:4" href="/Exodus.12.4"><i>Ex.</i> 12:4</a>.</i><i>,</i> this teaches that they may continuously diminish, on condition that there always be one of the first group and one of the second group, the words of Rebbi Jehudah. Rebbi Yose says, either from the first or from the second, if only the <i>Pesaḥ</i> not be left alone.<sup class="footnote-marker">89</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Pesachim 99a" href="/Pesachim.99a">Babli 99a</a>, <a class="refLink" data-ref="Tosefta Pesachim (Lieberman) 7:7" href="/Tosefta_Pesachim_(Lieberman).7.7">Tosephta 7:7</a>, <i>Mekhilta dR. Ismael Bo</i> 3, <i>dR. Simeon ben Yoḥai</i> p. 9. It is presumed that practice follows R. Yose (the Tanna, ben Ḥalafta.)</i>” If you are saying that any who join are its subscribers, then the members of the first group are the members of the second group<sup class="footnote-marker">90</sup><i class="footnote">According to Rav Ḥuna, every subscriber is counted as original subscriber; there can be no first and second group.</i>. What is the difference between them? If he dedicated his <i>Pesaḥ,</i> withdrew from it but another person subscribed to it. In the opinion of Rav Ḥuna it is qualified, in the opinion of Rebbi Zeˋira disqualified<sup class="footnote-marker">91</sup><i class="footnote">For Rav Ḥuna, the second person is an original subscriber. For R. Zeˋira the <i>Pesaḥ</i> was left without subscriber for a moment; this disqualifies.</i>. In the opinion of Rav Ḥuna it is dedication by an individual and subject to the laws of substitution; in the opinion of Rebbi Zeˋira it is dedication by partners and dedication of partners is not subject to the laws of substitution<sup class="footnote-marker">92</sup><i class="footnote">If the first subscriber left; his replacement now is the original dedicator and all the rules of Tractate <i>Temurah (Lev.</i>27:10) do apply. But for R. Zeˋira, supposing that the second subscriber came before the first one left and the <i>Pesaḥ</i> still is qualified, it now is dedication by partners and any attempt at substitution is invalid and therefore inconsequential.</i>. If a hundred people subscribed to it simultaneously, Rav Ḥuna said, if there is the volume [of an olive for each of them], it is qualified, otherwise disqualified. Rebbi Zeˋira said, as long as there is the volume of an olive for each of them, it is qualified, otherwise disqualified<sup class="footnote-marker">93</sup><i class="footnote">Since for Rav Ḥuna all subscribers are original dedicators, simultaneous subscription is possible. The subscriptions either are all valid or all invalid. For R. Zeˋira only sequential subscriptions are possible; as long as there is the volume of an olive available for a new subscriber he is accepted, otherwise he is rejected, but the rejection has no influence on the status of subscribers accepted earlier.</i>. And it was stated thus: “If they subscribed and added subscribers, as long as there is the volume of an olive for each of them, it is qualified, otherwise disqualified.<sup class="footnote-marker">94</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Pesachim 78b" href="/Pesachim.78b">Babli 78b</a>.</i>”

Halakhah 5

<strong>MISHNAH:</strong> For a sufferer from gonorrhea after two episodes one slaughters on the seventh {day}, if he had three episodes one slaughters for him on the eighth. Similarly for a woman watching day for day one slaughters on the second, if she had episodes on two consecutive days one slaughters on the third; but for the sufferer from flux one slaughters on the eighth<sup class="footnote-marker">95</sup><i class="footnote">A person who suffers a single episode of gonorrhea is impure for the day and can be purified by immersion in a <i>miqweh.</i> If he has two episodes in at most two consecutive days, he is impure for seven days; after seven days in remission he can be purified by immersion in a <i>miqweh.</i> After three episodes he still needs seven days in remission but then is still prohibited <i>sancta</i> unless on the eighth day he brings a couple of birds as sacrifice to the Temple. He can subscribe to a <i>Pesaḥ</i> if there is a reasonable chance that he will be permitted <i>sancta</i> after nightfall.<br>A menstruating woman is impure for seven days, <a class="refLink" data-ref="Leviticus 15:19" href="/Leviticus.15.19"><i>Lev.</i> 15:19</a>. A woman having non-menstrual discharges for <i>many days (Lev.</i> 15:25), interpreted as three days, is in the same situation as a male sufferer from gonorrhea after three episodes (15:28–29). For isolated episodes on one or two days, she may immerse herself in a <i>miqweh</i> on the next day and become pure for <i>sancta</i> at nightfall.</i>.
<strong>HALAKHAH:</strong> Rebbi Ḥiyya stated: “For the menstruating woman one slaughters on her eighth day. For a man having had intercourse with a menstruating woman one slaughters on his seventh day.” Rebbi Yose said, this implies that a man having had intercourse with a menstruating woman is pure on his seventh day<sup class="footnote-marker">96</sup><i class="footnote">For a woman it is written <i>seven days she shall stay in her separation</i>(Lev.. 15:19) which is read to mean that she can go to a <i>miqweh</i> only after nightfall at the end of the seventh day. The next sundown which permits her to partake of <i>sancta</i> therefore is the sundown of the eighth day (<a class="refLink" data-ref="Pesachim 90b" href="/Pesachim.90b">Babli 90b</a>). But for a male who lies with her it says (Lev.. 15:24) <i>he is impure for seven days,</i> and since part of a day is counted as a full day, he can purify himself on the seventh day before nightfall (<a class="refLink" data-ref="Yoma 6a" href="/Yoma.6a">Babli <i>Yoma</i> 6a</a>).</i>.

Halakhah 6

<strong>MISHNAH:</strong> One slaughters for the deep mourner<sup class="footnote-marker">97</sup><i class="footnote">The status of a person a close relative of whom has died, between the time of death and burial. As a deep mourner he is barred from all religious rites, but if he does not become impure by the impurity of the dead by nightfall he is able to participate in religious ceremonies.</i>, and one who digs out a collapsed building<sup class="footnote-marker">98</sup><i class="footnote">He searches for survivors or for the corpses of the slain. If he finds no corpses he remains pure and can eat the <i>Pesaḥ,</i> but this is very uncertain.</i>, and one who was promised that he would be freed from jail, the sick person or the old who are able to eat the volume of an olive. But for all of these one does not slaughter for themselves lest the <i>Pesaḥ</i> become disqualified<sup class="footnote-marker">99</sup><i class="footnote">If something happened, the <i>Pesaḥ</i> would be without eaters and would have to be burned.</i>. Therefore if a disqualification should occur they are not liable for the Second <i>Pesaḥ</i> except for one who digs out a collapsed building who from the start could expect to be impure.
<strong>HALAKHAH:</strong> Rebbi Yose ben Rebbi Abun, Abba bar bar Hana in the name of Rebbi Joḥanan : The Mishnah<sup class="footnote-marker">100</sup><i class="footnote">About the person who had been promised that he would be freed.</i> if he was jailed by Jews. But if he was jailed by gentiles, <i>whose mouth speaks vanity and whose oath is false oath</i><sup class="footnote-marker">101</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Psalms 144:8" href="/Psalms.144.8"><i>Ps.</i> 144:8</a>.</i><i>.</i> If he was held outside of Jerusalem, but if he was held in Jerusalem even if they did not promise it is as if they had promised<sup class="footnote-marker">102</sup><i class="footnote">Since they can bring the <i>Pesaḥ</i> to the jail and eat there with him.</i>.
Rebbi Jonah and Rebbi Yose both are saying, in the beginning we used to say that one may sprinkle on an uncircumcised Jew; but we were saying nothing<sup class="footnote-marker">103</sup><i class="footnote">Sprinkling with water mixed with ashes of the Red Cow belongs to the ritual of cleansing the impurity of the dead; it is applicable to all Jews including those uncircumcised (cf. <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Pesachim 8:8:9" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Pesachim.8.8.9">Note 160</a>). But for people intending to eat <i>Pesaḥ,</i> this applies only to those already circumcised, as explained in the following sentence.</i>. Rebbi Simon bar Zavdi stated before Rebbi Hila: It is said here <i>then he shall come near to make it,</i> and it is said there, <i>then he may eat of it</i><sup class="footnote-marker">104</sup><i class="footnote">In the rules of the <i>Pesaḥ, Ex.</i> 12:43–50, it is said of the slave (v.44) that he must be circumcised, <i>then he may eat of it,</i> and of the proselyte (v.48) that all his males have to be circumcised, <i>then he may come near to make it.</i> Since the verse about the slave states that circumcision is what is needed before he can eat, the same is true for the proselyte, and he must be circumcised and receive sprinkling before he can eat. <a class="refLink" data-ref="Yevamot 71a" href="/Yevamot.71a">Babli <i>Yebamot</i> 71a</a>.</i><i>.</i> Since <i>then</i> mentioned there presumes that he is qualified at the time of eating, so also <i>there</i> mentioned here presumes that he is qualified at the time of (eating) [slaughter]<sup class="footnote-marker">105</sup><i class="footnote">The text in parentheses was first written by the scribe who then corrected it to the text in brackets. It is obvious that the original text is the correct one.</i>.
Sometimes he<sup class="footnote-marker">106</sup><i class="footnote">The person digging for victims in a collapsed building who is obligated for Second <i>Pesaḥ.</i></i> has the status of them and sometimes they have the status of him. Sometimes he has the status of them, a long collapsed building. I am saying that the blood was poured for him before he reached the impurity<sup class="footnote-marker">107</sup><i class="footnote">Then he may not bring a Second <i>Pesaḥ.</i> <a class="refLink" data-ref="Pesachim 91a" href="/Pesachim.91a">Babli 91a</a>.</i>. Sometimes they have the status of him, at a circular collapsed building<sup class="footnote-marker">108</sup><i class="footnote">Where in all likelihood he stood over the corpse if any was found at all, then he is impure by “tent impurity”.</i>; if a disqualification occurred for them between slaughter and pouring, they have the status of him at a circular collapsed building.

Halakhah 7

<strong>MISHNAH:</strong> One does not slaughter the <i>Pesaḥ</i> for a single person, the words of Rebbi Jehudah; but Rebbi Yose permits. One does not slaughter for a group, even of a hundred, if none of them can eat the volume of an olive<sup class="footnote-marker">109</sup><i class="footnote">Even though together they eat more than the volume of an olive.</i>, and one does not form a group of women, slaves, and minors.
<strong>HALAKHAH:</strong> Rebbi Joḥanan said, the season of Rebbi Jehudah: <i>You may not sacrifice the Pesaḥ in one of your gates</i><sup class="footnote-marker">110</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Deuteronomy 16:5" href="/Deuteronomy.16.5"><i>Deut.</i> 16:5</a>. Halakhah 9:9, <a class="refLink" data-ref="Pesachim 91a" href="/Pesachim.91a">Babli 91a</a>, <a class="refLink" data-ref="Pesachim 99a" href="/Pesachim.99a">99a</a>; <i>Sifry Deut.</i> #132.</i> How does Rebbi Yose interpret Rebbi Jehudah’s reason? He explains it following Rebbi Eleazar ben Matthew, as it was stated: Rebbi Eleazar says, I could think that a single person clinches for impurity, the verse says, <i>you may not sacrifice the Pesaḥ in one</i><sup class="footnote-marker">111</sup><i class="footnote">Cf. <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Pesachim 7:6:4" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Pesachim.7.6.4">Chapter 7, Note 149</a>.</i>. Rebbi Joḥanan said, Rebbi Jehudah concedes that if he transgressed and poured, it was made acceptable; if he transgressed and slaughtered one permits him to pour.
It was stated: one does not form a group of women, slaves, and minors, since they increase lewd behavior<sup class="footnote-marker">112</sup><i class="footnote">Without the presence of adult free males.</i>. Bar Qappara stated, because they bring <i>sancta</i> to disqualification<sup class="footnote-marker">113</sup><i class="footnote"><i>Cf. Šabbat</i> 11, Note 58.</i>. Rebbi Jacob bar Aḥa in the name of Rebbi Issy: One does not form a group from proselytes. Since they are [faulty they are not]<sup class="footnote-marker">114</sup><i class="footnote">The text in brackets is an addition at the margin of the ms. The text without the addition is that of the <a class="refLink" data-ref="Pesachim 91b" href="/Pesachim.91b">Babli 91b</a>, the text with the addition is quoted there by <a class="refLink" data-ref="Tosafot on Pesachim 65a:9:1" href="/Tosafot_on_Pesachim.65a.9.1">Tosaphot <i>s.v</i>. שמא</a>.</i> diligent about it and bring it to disqualification.

Halakhah 8

<strong>MISHNAH:</strong> The deep mourner immerses himself and eats his <i>Pesaḥ</i> in the evening but not [other] <i>sancta</i><sup class="footnote-marker">97,115</sup><i>.</i> He who hears about a death or for whom bones were collected immerses himself and eats <i>sancta</i><sup class="footnote-marker">116</sup><i class="footnote">If he did not become impure by the impurity of the dead, the immersion required for <i>sancta</i> is purely rabbinical; this rabbinic extension of the rules of deep mourning in no case extends to the night (<a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Chagigah 3:3:1" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Chagigah.3.3.1">Mishnah <i>Ḥagigah</i> 3:3</a>.</i><i>.</i> A proselyte who converted on Passover eve, the House of Shammai say that he immerses himself<sup class="footnote-marker">117</sup><i class="footnote">An immersion for <i>sancta,</i> additional to that required for conversion.</i> and eats his <i>Pesaḥ</i> in the evening, but the House of Hillel say that he who separates from the prepuce is like one who separates from a grave<sup class="footnote-marker">118</sup><i class="footnote">After conversion he has to be sprinkled with water containing ashes of the Red Cow on the 3rd and 7th days after conversion.</i>.
<strong>HALAKHAH:</strong> Rebbi Yose ben Rebbi Abun said, the Mishnah is about one who newly became a deep mourner between slaughter and pouring<sup class="footnote-marker">119</sup><i class="footnote">It may have occurred earlier. The reason for this formulation is explained at the end of the paragraph.</i>. But if he became a deep mourner after atonement it already was accepted<sup class="footnote-marker">120</sup><i class="footnote">Since the sacrifice is accepted, there is no reason to wave any rules and the deep mourner may not eat from the <i>Pesaḥ</i> but he has fulfilled his religious duty.</i>.
<sup class="footnote-marker">121</sup><i class="footnote">This also is in <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Sanhedrin 2:1:6" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Sanhedrin.2.1.6"><i>Sanhedrin</i> 2:1 (Notes 52–55</a>), <i>Horaiot</i> 3:2.</i> And it was stated<sup class="footnote-marker">122</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Zevachim 100b" href="/Zevachim.100b"><i>Babli Zevaḥim</i> 100b</a>; a suspect text in <i>Semaḥot</i> 4:4.</i>: “What is deep mourning? From the moment of death until the moment of burial, the word of Rebbi. But the Sages say, the entire day.” It turns out that one describes leniencies and stringencies following Rebbi, leniencies and stringencies following the rabbis. What leniencies following Rebbi? If he died and was buried within the hour. Following Rebbi he is forbidden only that hour, following the rabbis he is forbiddden the entire day. Leniencies following the rabbis? If he died and was buried after three days. Following the rabbis, he is forbidden the entire day; following Rebbi he is forbidden up to three days. There came Rebbi Abbahu in the name of Rebbi Joḥanan, and Rav Ḥuna, both of whom said that Rebbi agrees with the Sages that he is forbidden only during the first day, as it was stated<sup class="footnote-marker">123</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Zevachim 100b" href="/Zevachim.100b"><i>Babli Zevaḥim</i> 100b</a>.</i>: Rebbi said, you know that deep mourning [in the night] is not biblical, since they said, “the deep mourner immerses himself and eats his <i>Pesaḥ</i> in the evening.” But they declared deep mourning during daytime as biblical. Rebbi Yose ben Rebbi Abun in the name of Rav Ḥisda: Explain it that he was buried close to sundown and one cannot infer anything.<sup class="footnote-marker">124</sup><i class="footnote">The Mishnah only refers to the unlikely case that the deep mourner was not defiled with the impurity of the dead in a case in which both Rebbi and the Sages will agree on the duration of the deep mourning.</i>
<sup class="footnote-marker">121</sup><i class="footnote">This also is in <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Sanhedrin 2:1:6" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Sanhedrin.2.1.6"><i>Sanhedrin</i> 2:1 (Notes 52–55</a>), <i>Horaiot</i> 3:2.</i> Rebbi Abbahu in the name of Rebbi Eleazar: “Deep sorrow”<sup class="footnote-marker">125</sup><i class="footnote">In its legal implications, that the person not only be forbidden to eat sanctified food but also cannot be counted in a quorum for religious services; cf. <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Berakhot 3:1:10" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Berakhot.3.1.10"><i>Berakhot</i>3:1, Note 42</a>.</i> is only for the dead, for it is written<sup class="footnote-marker">126</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Isaiah 3:26" href="/Isaiah.3.26"><i>Is.</i> 3:26</a>. The gates of Jerusalem are in sorrow because all its men are dead.</i>: <i>Its gates are in deep sorrow and mourning.</i>Ḥiyya bar Ada objected: Is it not written<sup class="footnote-marker">127</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Isaiah 19:8" href="/Isaiah.19.8"><i>Is.</i> 19:8</a>. The fishermen are in <i>deep sorrow</i> (and they <i>mourn</i> as quoted in the two parallel texts) because the Nile dried up. This proves that both terms used for the religious obligations of a person whose close relative died are used in the Bible also to describe other situations.</i>: <i>the fishermen are in deep sorrow, and mourning all who throw a fishing hook into the Nile?</i> Rebbi Ḥanina said, so is the <i>baraita:</i> there is no deep sorrow in impurity except for the dead.
It was stated<sup class="footnote-marker">128</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Zevachim 100b" href="/Zevachim.100b">Babli <i>Zevaḥim</i> 100b</a>; <i>Semaḥot</i> 12:1. In both sources, “and eats <i>sancta</i> in the evening.” From the following it is clear that this also was the reading of the Yerushalmi.</i>: “The day of information is like the day of burial as regards tearing<sup class="footnote-marker">129</sup><i class="footnote">The obligation to tear his clothes.</i>, and mourning<sup class="footnote-marker">130</sup><i class="footnote">To observe the rules of the seven days of intensive followed by the thirty days of lesser mourning.</i>, and counting Seven and Thirty; but to eat <i>sancta</i> it is like gathering bones, (he immerses himself and eats <i>sancta)</i><sup class="footnote-marker">131</sup><i class="footnote">The text in parentheses was written by the scribe but then was deleted. The deletion is in error as shown by the question following the statement.</i><i>.”</i> About gathering bones, may he immerse himself and eat <i>sancta</i><sup class="footnote-marker">132</sup><i class="footnote">Why is the qualification “in the evening” missing in the Mishnah?</i><i>?</i> Rebbi Yose ben Rebbi Abun in the name of Rav Ḥisda, explain it if he was buried after nightfall<sup class="footnote-marker">133</sup><i class="footnote">Then he can eat <i>sancta</i> only a day later.</i>. “In both cases they immerse themselves and eat their <i>Pesaḥ</i> in the evening.<sup class="footnote-marker">134</sup><i class="footnote">Since the Mishnah states that the rules of deep mourning are waved for <i>Pesaḥ</i> but not for other <i>sancta,</i> it seems that here one should read <i>sancta</i> for <i>Pesaḥ.</i></i>” After burial may one eat <i>sancta?</i> Rebbi Yose ben Rebbi Abun said, both are about information. If he was informed that a relative died the day before, he immerses himself and eats <i>sancta;</i> if he was informed that bones were collected the day before, he immerses himself and eats <i>sancta</i><sup class="footnote-marker">135</sup><i class="footnote">But in the evening of the day itself only <i>Pesaḥ</i> may be eaten, not <i>sancta</i> in general.</i><i>.</i>
<sup class="footnote-marker">136</sup><i class="footnote">This text is from <i>Moˋed qaṭan</i> 1:5 (<b>מ</b>). There also exists a Genizah text for most of the Halakhah there.</i> It was stated: If a person transports a casket from place to place the rules<sup class="footnote-marker">137</sup><i class="footnote">Prescribing mourning rites.</i> of collecting bones do not apply. Rebbi Aḥa said, that only is about a stone sarcophagus. But to a wooden casket the rules of collecting bones do apply. Rebbi Yose said, even to a wooden casket the rules of collecting bones do not apply. When is there collecting bones? If one transports them in a striped garment<sup class="footnote-marker">138</sup><i class="footnote">Greek ἐπικάρσιον, τό.</i> from place to place. Rebbi Haggai in the name of Rebbi Zeˋira: Collecting bones [is] what it means<sup class="footnote-marker">139</sup><i class="footnote">The rules apply only to the act of collecting bones, not of transporting.</i>. And it was stated thus: In collecting bones one collects them bone by bone after the flesh has decomposed. It was stated: There is no information<sup class="footnote-marker">140</sup><i class="footnote">No prescribed mourning rites when one is informed of the act.</i> about collecting bones. Rebbi Ḥaggai said, that is if he was informed the next day. But on the day itself there is information about collecting bones. Is there a minimum for collecting bones? Nikomachos stated before Rebbi Zeˋira: There is no minimum about collecting bones. About this, Rebbi Mana instructed Rebbi Hillel from Kifra to tear and mourn following Rebbi Aḥa but not to defile himself following Rebbi Yose<sup class="footnote-marker">141</sup><i class="footnote">R. Hillel was a Cohen; he was instructed to follow R. Aḥa to observe mourning rites when his parents’ bone were brought in ossuaries but not to violate the biblical rules which prohibit a Cohen from becoming impure in the impurity of the dead except for the burial of close relatives. The rules spelled out by R. Aḥa are purely rabbinic.</i>. It was stated: When collecting bones one does not recite lamentations and dirges; one recites neither the blessings for mourners nor the consolations for mourners. These are blessings for mourners: what is recited in the synagogue. These are consolations of mourners, what is said in the row<sup class="footnote-marker">142</sup><i class="footnote">After the burial the people attending form two rows between which the mourners walk and are greeted with a wish that “the Omnipresent may console you with all the mourners of Zion and Jerusalem.”</i>. It was stated: But one says words. What are words? The rabbis of Caesarea are saying, eulogies<sup class="footnote-marker">143</sup><i class="footnote">קִילוּס “praise” is derived from Greek καλῶς! “beautiful, excellent”. For the use as “eulogy” compare καλολογέω, same as ἐυλογέω (E. G.).</i>.
What is the reason of the House of Shammai? <i>You and your captives</i><sup class="footnote-marker">144</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Numbers 31:19" href="/Numbers.31.19"><i>Num.</i> 31:19</a>, speaking of the captive Midianite women.</i><i>.</i> Since you could not be impure before you entered the covenant, also your captives cannot be impure before they enter the covenant<sup class="footnote-marker">145</sup><i class="footnote">While it seems from the text there that a Gentile corpse imparts impurity of the dead by touch, it is clear that a living Gentile cannot biblically be impure; the impurities attributed to Gentiles are of purely rabbinic character and must be disregarded in matters of conversions. <i>Sifry Num.</i> # 157 notes that mention of the captives in relation to impurity implies that these had to be converted.</i>. What is the reason of the House of Hillel? <i>You and your captives.</i> Since you need sprinkling on the third and seventh {days}, so your captives need sprinkling on the third and seventh {days}. But it is not logically consistent<sup class="footnote-marker">146</sup><i class="footnote">There is no claim that the restrictive practice of the House of Hillel is biblical.</i>, since Rav Ḥiyya bar Joseph, Giddul bar Benjamin said in the name of Rav: The House of Hillel agree that if he transgressed and poured the blood, that it is accepted.
<sup class="footnote-marker">147</sup><i class="footnote">This paragraph is a reformulation of one in <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Nazir 8:1:9" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Nazir.8.1.9"><i>Nazir</i> 8:1 (Notes 56–63</a>) but, as the quotes in the paragraph show clearly, the source is <i>Nazir,</i> in contrast to the next paragraph which in <i>Nazir</i> is a copy from <i>Pesaḥim.</i></i> A <i>nazir</i> who became impure by a doubt relating to a private domain<sup class="footnote-marker">148</sup><i class="footnote">The general principle is that a doubt about impurity arising in a private domain is treated as certain impurity, in the public domain as certain purity. The rule becomes void if the character of the place itself is doubtful.</i> (on Oassover) [not related to the <i>Pesaḥ.</i><sup class="footnote-marker">149</sup><i class="footnote">The scribe wrote “on <i>Pesaḥ”</i> and the corrector inserted “not”. Both words should be deleted.</i>] The great Rebbi Hoshaia said, the <i>nazir</i> shaves. Rebbi Joḥanan said, the <i>nazir</i> does not shave<sup class="footnote-marker">150</sup><i class="footnote">The essence of a vow of <i>nazir</i> is that the person must let his hair grow, abstain from all products of the vine, and avoid any impurity of the dead. If he should become impure in this impurity, he has to shave, bring required sacrifices, and start his <i>nezirut</i> all over again.</i>, since we have stated there<sup class="footnote-marker">151</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Nazir 7:4:1" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Nazir.7.4.1">Mishnah <i>Nazir</i> 7:4</a>. In <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Pesachim 7:2:1" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Pesachim.7.2.1">Mishnah 7:2</a> it is explained that the <i>Nazir</i> shaves only if the cause of the impurity is a verified part of a corpse; the cases of doubt enumerated in <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Pesachim 7:3:1" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Pesachim.7.3.1">Mishnah 7:3</a> are excluded. The liability for entering the Sanctuary in impurity is for a sacrifice if inadvertent or for extirpation if intentional.</i>: “For any impurity caused by a corpse for which the <i>nazir</i> shaves, [one is liable] if entering the Sanctuary, but any impurity caused by a corpse for which the <i>nazir</i> does not shave, [one is not liable] if entering the Sanctuary.” What kind of doubt? Rebbi Joḥanan said, the start of the Chapter<sup class="footnote-marker">152</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Nazir 8:1:1" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Nazir.8.1.1">Mishnah <i>Nazir</i> 8:1</a>: A person saw that one of two <i>nezirim</i> became impure but he cannot identify whom he saw. Then there certainly is impurity but it is not known to whom it refers.</i>. The great Rebbi Hoshaia said, the one here<sup class="footnote-marker">153</sup><i class="footnote">One of the cases of <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Nazir 7:3:1" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Nazir.7.3.1">Mishnah <i>Nazir</i> 7:3</a>, where t is not known whether actually impurity was created.</i>. A person who became impure by a doubt relating to a private domain for the <i>Pesaḥ.</i> Rebbi Hoshaia said, he should be pushed to the Second <i>Pesaḥ.</i> Rebbi Joḥanan said, one sends him on a far journey<sup class="footnote-marker">154</sup><i class="footnote">For him also the person has to bring the <i>Second Pesaḥ,</i> but he holds that like any other sacrifice it may be brought for a certain, rather than a possible, obligation.</i>. This follows what Rebbi Joḥanan said, if he became impure by the impurity of the broken field<sup class="footnote-marker">155</sup><i class="footnote">A field which contained a grave ploughed under. Not only is the suspected place of the grave impure by biblical standards but the entire field is rabbinically impure since the plough might have caught a bone and transported it to another part of the field.</i>, one sends him on a far journey. The community who became impure by a doubt relating to a private domain on Passover. Rebbi Joḥanan said, they should present it in their doubt<sup class="footnote-marker">156</sup><i class="footnote">If the majority of the public is certainly impure, all <i>Pesaḥim</i> are made in impurity. If the majority is in doubt whether they are impure, the pure minority brings their offerings in purity and the possibly impure majority theirs in possible impurity.</i>. Does the great Rebbi Hoshaia say, it should be made in impurity? Rebbi Hoshaia (said) [also agrees] that it should be presented in their doubt; what Rebbi Hoshaia said referred only to restrictions.
Rebbi Joḥanan in the name of Rebbi Benaiah: One sprinkles on an uncircumcised Jew<sup class="footnote-marker">157</sup><i class="footnote">The position of the House of Hillel in the Mishnah is rejected. It is asserted that the uncircumcised can purify himself from the impurity and, being circumcised later, participate in the <i>Pesaḥ</i> celebration as asserted by the House of Shammai.</i>, for we find that our forefathers in the desert<sup class="footnote-marker">158</sup><i class="footnote">Not in the desert, but after crossing the Jordan on the 10<sup class="footnote-marker">th</sup> of Nisan (<a class="refLink" data-ref="Joshua 4:19" href="/Joshua.4.19"><i>Jos.</i> 4:19</a>). They were then circumcised (<a class="refLink" data-ref="Joshua 5:2-8" href="/Joshua.5.2-8"><i>Jos.</i> 5:2–8</a>) and celebrated the <i>Pesaḥ</i> on the 14<sup class="footnote-marker">th</sup> (<a class="refLink" data-ref="Joshua 5:10" href="/Joshua.5.10"><i>Jos.</i> 5:10</a>).</i> received sprinkling when uncircumcised. Rav Ḥisda said, following him who said that they circumcised on the eleventh<sup class="footnote-marker">159</sup><i class="footnote">If they were circumcised on the 11<sup class="footnote-marker">th</sup> they had to be sprinkled on the 10<sup class="footnote-marker">th</sup>, when they still were uncircumcised, in order to become pure on the 14<sup class="footnote-marker">th</sup>.</i>. But for him who said that they circumcised on the tenth, they did not count sprinkling when uncircumcised. Rebbi Abun said, did they not have to count for sprinkling when uncircumcised in any case<sup>160</sup><i class="footnote">Rav Ḥisda’s argument has to be rejected since if sprinkling on an uncircumcised person is ineffective, the underlying counting (of the third, seventh days) also must be ineffective. But for the <i>Pesaḥ</i> on the 14th, the counting had to start on the 7th, when according to the biblical text everybody (except Joshua, Caleb, and possibly Levites and/or Priests) were uncircumcised. He will hold that the first Passover in Canaan was held in impurity. This argument, represented in the Babli, <i>loc. cit.,</i> by Mar Zuṭra, there is rejected by Rav Ashi.</i>? Rebbi Eleazar in the name of Rebbi Ḥanina: It happened that an uncircumcised Cohen sprinkled<sup class="footnote-marker">161</sup><i class="footnote">In <i>Nazir:</i> “he was sprinkled” (passive voice).</i> and the sprinklings were declared valid. It was stated so: Rebbi Eliezer ben Jacob says, there were soldiers<sup class="footnote-marker">162</sup><i class="footnote">Greek στρατιώτης, ὁ.</i> and gate keepers in Jerusalem who immersed themselves and ate their <i>Pesaḥ</i> in the evening<sup class="footnote-marker">163</sup><i class="footnote">They were Gentiles who converted to Judaism, were circumcised, immersed themselves in a <i>miqweh</i> on the 14th of Nisan, and participated in Passover, not needing cleansing by sprinkling following the House of Shammai</i>.

Chapter 9



Halakhah 1

<strong>MISHNAH:</strong> He who was impure or on a far trip and did not make the First shall make the Second<sup class="footnote-marker">1</sup><i class="footnote">A person impure and/or at a distance from Jerusalem on the afternoon of the 14<sup class="footnote-marker">th</sup> of Nisan is obligated to bring a <i>Pesaḥ</i> on the 14<sup class="footnote-marker">th</sup> of Iyar.</i>. If in error or by force<sup class="footnote-marker">2</sup><i class="footnote">He was pure and in Jerusalem on the 14th of Nisan but forcibly prevented from participating in a <i>Pesaḥ.</i></i> he did not make the First shall make the Second. If this is so, why was it said<sup class="footnote-marker">3</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Numbers 9:9" href="/Numbers.9.9"><i>Num.</i> 9:9</a>.</i> <i>impure or on a far trip?</i> Because these are not liable for extirpation<sup class="footnote-marker">4</sup><i class="footnote">The Second <i>Pesaḥ</i> is a positive commandment for which no penalties are indicated in case of omission, in contrast to the First whose intentional omission is a deadly sin implying extirpation. In contrast to the <a class="refLink" data-ref="Pesachim 93b" href="/Pesachim.93b">Babli (93b</a>), the Yerushalmi does not expect that those who missed the First in error or by force are subject to extirpation if they intentionally miss the Second.</i> but those are liable for extirpation.
<strong>HALAKHAH:</strong> “He who was impure,” etc. <i>Impure by a corpse</i><sup class="footnote-marker">5</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Numbers 9:10" href="/Numbers.9.10"><i>Num.</i> 9:10</a>.</i><i>,</i> I not only have impure by a corpse, from where forced or in error? The verse says, <i>every man,</i> [it added]<sup class="footnote-marker">6</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Pesachim 93a" href="/Pesachim.93a">Babli 93a</a>.</i>. So far following Rebbi Aqiba; following Rebbi Ismael? Rebbi Ismael stated, <i>impure by a corpse</i> is not equal to <i>a far-away trip,</i> nor is <i>a far-away trip</i> equal to <i>impure by a corpse,</i> what is common to them<sup class="footnote-marker">7</sup><i class="footnote">This is the third hermeneutical principle of R. Ismael. <i>Sifry Num.</i> 69, <a class="refLink" data-ref="Tosefta Pesachim (Lieberman) 8:2" href="/Tosefta_Pesachim_(Lieberman).8.2">Tosephta 8:2</a> (in the name of R. Aqiba); Targum Pseudo-Jonathan 9:10.</i> is that he did not make the First and shall make the Second; also I am adding those forced or in error who did not make the First that they shall make the Second. Intentional from where? Rebbi Zeˋira said, <i>but the man,</i> to add the one acting intentionally<sup class="footnote-marker">8</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Numbers 9:13" href="/Numbers.9.13"><i>Num.</i> 9:13</a>: <i>But the man who was pure.</i><br>This contradicts the position of R. Aqiba in the Tosephta, that both those impure by a corpse and those on a far trip are prevented from making the First <i>Pesaḥ</i> and therefore the third hermeneutical principle excludes the one who intentionally omitted the First even though he was pure and not far away. Cf. <a class="refLink" data-ref="Pesachim 93" href="/Pesachim.93">Babli 93a/b</a>.</i>. We have stated; “if in error or by force;” Rebbi Ḥiyya stated, “if in error, or by force, or intentional.<sup class="footnote-marker">9</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Tosefta Pesachim (Lieberman) 8:1" href="/Tosefta_Pesachim_(Lieberman).8.1">Tosephta 8:1</a>.</i>” Rebbi Yose said, the Mishnah implies this, “because these are not liable for extirpation but those are liable for extirpation;” who is subject to extirpation if not intentional?
<i>Impure by a corpse.</i> I have not only <i>impure by a corpse;</i> impure by genital discharge, impure by skin disease, from where? The verse says impure (by the dead)<sup class="footnote-marker">10</sup><i class="footnote">This word should be deleted since there is no verse containing this expression. The argument is that while one would expect the accents to be טָמֵ֣א לָנֶ֡פֶשׁ “impure by a corpse,” the first word carries <i>legarmeh,</i> a dividing accent, טָמֵ֣א ׀ לָנֶ֡פֶשׁ, correctly translated “impure, [e. g.,] by a corpse.” <a class="refLink" data-ref="Pesachim 93a" href="/Pesachim.93a">Babli 93a</a>, <i>Sifry Num.</i> 69.</i>, it added. Why does the verse say, <i>impure by a corpse</i><sup class="footnote-marker">11</sup><i class="footnote">The argument is not really from this quote but from the entire first part of the verse: <i>every single man who would be impure, by a corpse.</i></i>? A man impure by a corpse is pushed to the Second <i>Pesaḥ,</i> but a public impure by the impurity of a corpse are not pushed to the Second <i>Pesaḥ.</i> Those impure by genital discharge or impure by skin disease are pushed to the Second <i>Pesaḥ.</i> They made the impurity of idolatry equal to the impure by genital discharge or impure by skin disease<sup class="footnote-marker">12</sup><i class="footnote">As explained in the paragraph after the next.</i>. If Israel had the possibility to build the Temple<sup class="footnote-marker">13</sup><i class="footnote">If the Temple could be rebuilt after the 14<sup class="footnote-marker">th</sup> of Nisan but before the 14<sup class="footnote-marker">th</sup> of Iyar.</i>, individuals celebrate the Second <i>Pesaḥ</i> but the public does not celebrate the Second <i>Pesaḥ.</i> <sup class="footnote-marker">14</sup><i class="footnote">From here on, the text is from <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Nazir 6:1:9-2:1" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Nazir.6.1.9-2.1"><i>Nazir</i>6:13 (Notes 83–109</a>), <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Sanhedrin 1:2:25-35" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Sanhedrin.1.2.25-35"><i>Sanhedrin</i> 1:2 (Notes 209–219</a>).</i> Rebbi Jehudah says, the public celebrates the Second <i>Pesaḥ</i> since we find that Hezekia celebrated the Second <i>Pesaḥ.</i> This is what is written, for most of the people from Ephraim and Manasse<sup class="footnote-marker">15</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="II Chronicles 30:18" href="/II_Chronicles.30.18"><i>2Chr.</i> 30:18</a>.</i>, etc.
Some Tannaïm state: One intercalates the year because of impurity<sup class="footnote-marker">16</sup><i class="footnote">One does not intercalate a 13<sup class="footnote-marker">th</sup> month to give people time to purify themselves in time for the <i>Pesaḥ</i> on the 14<sup class="footnote-marker">th</sup> of Nisan.</i>. Some Tannaïm state: One does not intercalate the year because of impurity. He who says, one does not intercalate, how does he uphold: <i>for they ate the Passover contrary to what is written</i><sup class="footnote-marker">17</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="II Chronicles 30:18" href="/II_Chronicles.30.18"><i>2Chr.</i> 30:18</a>. Hezeqiah celebrated <i>Pesaḥ</i> a month late; that is exactly what Scripture prescribes for impure individuals.</i><i>?</i> They intercalated in Nisan but only Adar can be intercalated. This follows what Rebbi Simon bar Zavdi said: they found the skull of Ornan the Yebusite under the altar<sup class="footnote-marker">18</sup><i class="footnote">This statement is from <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Sotah 5:2:9" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Sotah.5.2.9"><i>Soṭah</i> 5:2, Note 90</a>; it must refer to the construction of the altar by Solomon. Hezekiah moved the month because the Temple was not usable in Nisan since similarly the Temple was found to be a “tent” over human bones and thus impure. Ornan was the original owner of the Temple Mount <a class="refLink" data-ref="I Chronicles 21:18-26" href="/I_Chronicles.21.18-26"><i>(1Chr.</i> 21:18–26</a>); the text does not imply that Gentiles create tent impurity. <a class="refLink" data-ref="Sanhedrin 12a" href="/Sanhedrin.12a">Babli <i>Sanhedrin</i> 12a</a>.</i>.
It is written<sup class="footnote-marker">19</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="II Chronicles 29:17" href="/II_Chronicles.29.17"><i>2Chr.</i> 29:17</a>. They finished cleansing the Temple of idolatry on the 16<sup class="footnote-marker">th</sup>.</i>: <i>They started on the first of the first month, and on the eighth day ….</i> Could they not have eliminated all idolatry from there in one day? Rebbi Idi said, because of Chaldean idols which were engraved in vermilion. It is written<sup class="footnote-marker">20</sup><i class="footnote"><i>2Chr</i>.30:19. The verse ends: <i>except for the Temple’s purity.</i></i>: <i>With all his heart he prepared himself to seek the Eternal, the God of his forefathers.</i> Rebbi Simon bar Zavdi and Rebbi Samuel bar Naḥman: One said, with all he did for the purity of the Temple, he did not fully establish the purity of the Temple. One said, with all the good works he did, he did not fully do his duty for the purity of the Temple.
Six things did Hezekiah, the King of Judea, do; with three they agreed, with three they did not agree<sup class="footnote-marker">21</sup><i class="footnote">This is the last Mishnah in Chapter 4 of the Babli; Maimonides in his Mishnah commentary declares it to be a Tosephta (cf. 8:5). <a class="refLink" data-ref="Pesachim 56a" href="/Pesachim.56a">Babli 56a</a>, <a class="refLink" data-ref="Berakhot 10b" href="/Berakhot.10b"><i>Berakhot</i> 10b</a>, <a class="refLink" data-ref="Sanhedrin 47a" href="/Sanhedrin.47a"><i>Sanhedrin</i>47a</a>.</i>. For the following they agreed with him. He smashed the bronze snake<sup class="footnote-marker">22</sup><i class="footnote">The bronze snake made by Moses, <a class="refLink" data-ref="II Kings 18:4" href="/II_Kings.18.4"><i>2K.</i>18:4</a>. “They” are the Heavenly Court.</i> and they agreed with him. He dragged his father’s bones on a bier of ropes<sup class="footnote-marker">23</sup><i class="footnote">He buried him in an undignified way to atone for his sins. The basis is a note in <a class="refLink" data-ref="II Chronicles 28:27" href="/II_Chronicles.28.27"><i>2Chr.</i> 28:27</a> that Aḥaz was not buried in the kings’ graves, contradicting <a class="refLink" data-ref="II Kings 16:20" href="/II_Kings.16.20"><i>2K.</i> 16:20</a>.</i>, and they agreed with him. He hid the table of medicines<sup class="footnote-marker">24</sup><i class="footnote">According to Maimonides a book of magical remedies.</i>, and they agreed with him. For the following they disagreed with him. He cut down the Temple doors<sup class="footnote-marker">25</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="II Kings 18:16" href="/II_Kings.18.16"><i>2K.</i> 18:16</a>; to pay tribute to Assyria.</i> and they disagreed with him. He enclosed the upper Giḥon spring<sup class="footnote-marker">26</sup><i class="footnote">It seems that they did not connect <a class="refLink" data-ref="II Chronicles 32:30" href="/II_Chronicles.32.30"><i>2Chr.</i>32:30</a> with <a class="refLink" data-ref="II Kings 20:20" href="/II_Kings.20.20"><i>2K.</i> 20:20</a>. The statement is denied in <i>Avot dR. Nathan A,</i> Chapter 2.</i>, and they disagreed with him. He intercalated Nisan in Nisan<sup class="footnote-marker">27</sup><i class="footnote">As explained in the preceding paragraph, the celebration of Passover was wrong from beginning to end; the intercalation would have to precede Nisan, celebration, and if it was Iyar it should not be a mass celebration.</i>; and they disagreed with him.
If the public was half suffering from gonorrhea and half impure. Rav Ada bar Aḥava said, the sufferers from gonorrhea relate to the impure as the impure relate to the pure. They do not make it; the sufferers from gonorrhea are pushed to the Second <i>Pesaḥ.</i> Rav Ḥuna said, there is no make-up for <i>Pesaḥ</i> celebrated in impurity<sup class="footnote-marker">28</sup><i class="footnote">While sufferers from gonorrhea (and in general, all people whose impurity is generated by their own body) are impure and excluded from the sanctuary, only people impure in the impurity of the dead are counted in determining whether <i>Pesaḥ</i> is celebrated in impurity. The only difference is that in this case, where everybody is impure, the impure celebrate <i>Pesaḥ</i> in impurity if they make up 50% of the population, not 50%+2, and the healed sufferers from gonorrhea and similar impurity then may celebrate the Second. Cf. <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Pesachim 7:6:5" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Pesachim.7.6.5">Halakhah 7:6, Note 154</a>/</i>.
If most of the public were pure but a minority impure<sup class="footnote-marker">29</sup><i class="footnote">Impure in the impurity of the dead.</i>, and some of the pure died between slaughter and pouring. After what are you going? Slaughter [or] pouring? If you are saying after slaughter, one does not celebrate in impurity; if you are saying after pouring, one celebrates in impurity. If most of the public were impure but a minority pure, and of the impure died between slaughter and pouring. After what are you going? Slaughter or pouring? If you are saying after slaughter, one celebrates in impurity; if you are saying after pouring, one does not celebrate in impurity<sup class="footnote-marker">30</sup><i class="footnote">Since the case cannot happen, no answer is required.</i>.

Halakhah 2

<strong>MISHNAH:</strong> What is a far-away trip<sup class="footnote-marker">31</sup><i class="footnote">That a person being there on the 14<sup class="footnote-marker">th</sup> of Nisan be obligated for Second <i>Pesaḥ.</i></i>? From Modiˋin<sup class="footnote-marker">32</sup><i class="footnote">In the foothills West of Jerusalem.</i> and farther away, and the same distance in every direction, the words of Rebbi Aqiba. Rebbi Eliezer says, outside the doorstep of the Temple Courtyard. Rebbi Yose said, therefore there is a dot on the ה<sup class="footnote-marker">33</sup><i class="footnote">The masoretic text is רחקה̇, using the technique that instead of deleting letters one makes dots over them.</i> to indicate not that it be really far but outside the doorstep of the Temple Courtyard.
<strong>HALAKHAH:</strong> Rebbi Simeon said, the Great Rebbi Ḥiyya and bar Qappara disagreed. One said, that he could come and eat<sup class="footnote-marker">34</sup><i class="footnote">A person is not ”far away” to be absolved from participating in the First <i>Pesaḥ</i> if he can reach the walled city of Jerusalem in time for the eating of the <i>Pesaḥ,</i> i. e., between nightfall and midnight.</i>; the other one said that he could come and pour<sup class="footnote-marker">35</sup><i class="footnote">He must be there at the time of pouring the blood at the altar walls, in the late afternoon.</i>. And even following him who said, that he could come and eat; on condition that he be within the two thousand cubits of the [Sabbath] domain before nightfall<sup class="footnote-marker">36</sup><i class="footnote">Since on the holiday he is not permitted to walk more than 2’000 cubits from the place at which he started the holiday, it is clear that nobody farther than 2’000 cubits from Jerusalem at sundown can participate.</i>. Rebbi Zeˋira said, there<sup class="footnote-marker">37</sup><i class="footnote">In Babylonia. In the text of the extracts from the Yerushalmi in <i>Yalqut Šimony</i> published by L. Ginzberg in his <i>Genizah Fragments</i> (p. 321): “Tannaim state.”</i> they stated, if he happened to be closer than Modiˋin but his feet were bad, I could think that he be liable, the verse said, <i>he refrained</i><sup class="footnote-marker">38</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Numbers 9:13" href="/Numbers.9.13"><i>Num.</i> 9:13</a>.</i><i>,</i> this excludes one who did not refrain. If he happened to be farther than Modiˋin but had a horse at his disposal, I could think that he be liable, the verse said, <i>and he was not on a trip,</i> this excludes this one who was on a trip. If he happened to be closer than Modiˋin before noontime but left before noontime, I could think that he be liable, the verse said, <i>he refrained from doing,</i> he who refrains at the time of doing is liable, not at the time of doing is not liable.
Rebbi Abbahu in the name of Rebbi Joḥanan: Both of them<sup class="footnote-marker">39</sup><i class="footnote">R. Aqiba and R. Eliezer, quoted in the Mishnah.</i> explained the same verse, <i>there, there</i><sup class="footnote-marker">40</sup><i class="footnote">It is said about the <i>Pesaḥ (Deut.</i> 16:6) <i>there you shall slaughter the Pesaḥ in the evening,</i> and it is said about Second Tithe <a class="refLink" data-ref="Deuteronomy 14:22" href="/Deuteronomy.14.22"><i>(Deut.</i> 14:22</a>): <i>you shall eat before the Eternal, your God, at the place which He will select to have His Name dwell there.</i> Both <i>Pesaḥ</i> and Second Tithe have to be eaten at the place of the Sanctuary, and Tithe has to be accompanied by a sacrifice of appearance. Therefore “there” may be interpreted either as place of the sacrifice, in this case the Temple, or the place of consumption, Jerusalem, with the corresponding meaning of “far away”.</i><i>.</i> One said, away from doing it, but the other one said, away from its enclosure.
The colleagues in the name of Rebbi Joḥanan: <i>But the man who is pure and was not on the road</i><sup class="footnote-marker">38</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Numbers 9:13" href="/Numbers.9.13"><i>Num.</i> 9:13</a>.</i><i>,</i> this excludes the one on the road. Rebbi Zeˋira in the name of Rebbi Joḥanan: when He warned, He mentioned <i>far away,</i> when He punishes He does not mention “far away”<sup class="footnote-marker">41</sup><i class="footnote">“Far away” is mentioned in <a class="refLink" data-ref="Numbers 9:9" href="/Numbers.9.9"><i>Num.</i> 9:9</a>, where the Second <i>Pesaḥ</i> is defined, but missing in 9:13 where omission of both <i>Pesaḥim</i> is declared to be a deadly sin.</i>. But the rabbis are saying, in case that the letters are more than what is dotted, one explains the letters and disregards what is dotted; in case that the dotted is more than the letters, one explains the dotted and disregards the letter<sup class="footnote-marker">42</sup><i class="footnote">As in <a class="refLink" data-ref="Genesis 18:9" href="/Genesis.18.9"><i>Gen.</i> 18:9</a> where א֗לי֗ו֗ is read as איו “where?”</i>. Rebbi<sup class="footnote-marker">42</sup><i class="footnote">As in <a class="refLink" data-ref="Genesis 18:9" href="/Genesis.18.9"><i>Gen.</i> 18:9</a> where א֗לי֗ו֗ is read as איו “where?”</i> said, even though that in this case there is only one letter dotted on top, one explains the dotted and disregards the letters. The <i>he</i> in רחוקה is dotted: the man is far away, not the road far away.

Halakhah 3

<strong>MISHNAH:</strong> What is the difference between the First and the Second <i>Pesaḥ?</i> The First is forbidden [leavened matter] to be seen or found. For the Second, leavened matter and <i>mazzah</i> are with him in the house. The First needs <i>Hallel</i> when it is eaten, but the Second does not need <i>Hallel</i> when it is eaten<sup class="footnote-marker">44</sup><i class="footnote">The First is a family celebration, the Second a ritual restricted to adult males.</i>. Both need <i>Hallel</i> when it is offered<sup class="footnote-marker">45</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Psalms 113-117" href="/Psalms.113-117"><i>Pss.</i> 113–117</a> sung by the Levitic choir in the Temple, not the family at the table.</i>, and they are eaten roasted, with unleavened bread and bitter herbs, and push the Sabbath aside.
<strong>HALAKHAH:</strong> It is written: <i>they shall not leave anything until morning</i><sup class="footnote-marker">46</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Numbers 9:12" href="/Numbers.9.12"><i>Num.</i> 9:12</a>, stating the rules of the Second <i>Pesaḥ.</i></i><i>.</i> If it relates to eating, this is the relevant positive commandment. <i>No bone of it may be broken,</i> that is the relevant prohibition. So when He says, <i>according to all rules of the Pesaḥ they shall make it,</i> I could think that I have to add the elimination of leavened matter and <i>mazzah</i> for seven days. The verse says, <i>on mazzot and bitter herbs they shall eat it</i><sup class="footnote-marker">47</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Numbers 9:11" href="/Numbers.9.11"><i>Num.</i>9:11</a><i>.</i> Cf. <a class="refLink" data-ref="Pesachim 95a" href="/Pesachim.95a">Babli 95a</a>.</i><i>.</i> Nothing external to its body impedes it except <i>mazzot</i> and bitter herbs. And following Rebbi Ismael? Since Rebbi Ismael says, a principle followed by a detail, everything is in the principle, I could think that everything impedes it; the verse says, <i>on mazzot and bitter herbs they shall eat it.</i> Nothing external to its body impedes it except <i>mazzot</i> and bitter herbs<sup class="footnote-marker">48</sup><i class="footnote">In <i>Sifry Num.</i> 69, the argument is based on another hermeneutical principle of R. Ismael: “Anything mentioned in one setting and repeated in a different setting cannot be considered part of the original setting unless referred to explicitly by the verse.” Since the details, to be eaten with <i>mazzah</i> and bitter herbs, not to be left until morning, and no bone being broken, are repeated from the laws of the First <i>Pesaḥ,</i> they and only they are transferred to the Second.</i>.
Some Tannain stated, he is punished by extirpation for the Second, he is not punished by extirpation for the First. Some Tannain stated, he is punished by extirpation for the First, he is not punished by extirpation for the Second. And there are Tannaim who state, both for the First as for the Second he is punished by extirpation. He who says, he is punished by extirpation for the First; <i>he shall bear his sin</i> about the First. He who says, he is punished by extirpation for the Second; <i>he shall bear his sin</i> about the Second. He who says, both for the First as for the Second he is punished by extirpation, <i>he shall bear his sin</i> about the First and the Second. He who said, for the Second, he is not punished by extirpation except if he missed the First: <i>For the sacrifice of the Eternal he did did not bring at its appointed time,</i> the First, <i>his sin he shall bear,</i> about the Second<sup class="footnote-marker">49</sup><i class="footnote">While <a class="refLink" data-ref="Numbers 9:13" href="/Numbers.9.13"><i>Num.</i> 9:13</a> is written with the laws of the Second <i>Pesaḥ,</i> it is formulated in terms of the First. Therefore it is not clear whether it refers to the First (as understood by <i>Sifry Num.</i>70 and Pseudo-Jonathan), the Second, or both.</i>.
Rebbi Joḥanan said in the name of Rebbi Simon ben Joṣadaq: It is written, <i>the song shall be for you like the night at the start of the holiday of</i><i>pilgrimage</i><sup class="footnote-marker">50</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Isaiah 30:29" href="/Isaiah.30.29"><i>Is</i>. 30:29</a>; <a class="refLink" data-ref="Pesachim 95b" href="/Pesachim.95b">Babli 95b</a>.</i><i>.</i> The Passover night comes to instruct about the downfall of Sanherib and taken instruction from it. Since the one needs <i>Hallel.</i> so the other needs <i>Hallel.</i> But then since the one needs a sacrifice of pilgrimage, does the other need a sacrifice of pilgrimage? Rebbi Zeˋira said, <i>like the night at the start of the holiday of pilgrimage,</i> anything needing <i>Hallel</i> needs a sacrifice of pilgrimage; anything not needing <i>Hallel</i> does not need a sacrifice of pilgrimage.
It pushes aside impurity. You say, in itself it only comes because of impurity, and you are saying, it pushes aside impurity<sup class="footnote-marker">51</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Pesachim 95b" href="/Pesachim.95b">Babli 95b</a>, <i>Sifry Num.</i>70<i>.</i> It is clear that the Second <i>Pesaḥ</i> only can be offered in purity.</i>?

Halakhah 4

<strong>MISHNAH:</strong> What is the difference between the First and the Second <i>Pesaḥ?</i> The First is forbidden [leavened matter] to be seen or found. For the Second, leavened matter and <i>mazzah</i> are with him in the house. The First needs <i>Hallel</i> when it is eaten, but the Second does not need <i>Hallel</i> when it is eaten<sup class="footnote-marker">44</sup><i class="footnote">The First is a family celebration, the Second a ritual restricted to adult males.</i>. Both need <i>Hallel</i> when it is offered<sup class="footnote-marker">45</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Psalms 113-117" href="/Psalms.113-117"><i>Pss.</i> 113–117</a> sung by the Levitic choir in the Temple, not the family at the table.</i>, and they are eaten roasted, with unleavened bread and bitter herbs, and push the Sabbath aside.
<strong>HALAKHAH:</strong> It was stated: Rebbi Meïr declares liable but Rebbi Simeon declares not liable<sup class="footnote-marker">54</sup><i class="footnote">The people whose impurity is caused by their own body who eat from <i>Pesaḥ</i> slaughtered for people impure by the impurity of the dead. The Mishnah is R. Simeon’s. In <a class="refLink" data-ref="Sifra, Tzav, Chapter 14" href="/Sifra,_Tzav,_Chapter_14"><i>Sifra Ṣaw Pereq</i> 14</a>, the argument is attributed to R. Josua, in <a class="refLink" data-ref="Tosefta Pesachim (Lieberman) 8:9" href="/Tosefta_Pesachim_(Lieberman).8.9"><i>Tosephta</i> 8:9</a> R. Simeon in the name of R. Joshua; in the <a class="refLink" data-ref="Pesachim 95b" href="/Pesachim.95b">Babli 95b</a> it is anonymous.</i>. What is Rebbi Simeon’s reason? <i>The meat, every pure person shall eat meat. But the person who would eat meat from the well-being sacrifice</i><sup class="footnote-marker">55</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Leviticus 7:19-20" href="/Leviticus.7.19-20"><i>Lev.</i> 7:19–20</a>.</i><i>,</i> for any which is permitted to pure persons one is liable for impurity, but for any which is not permitted to pure persons one is not liable for impurity<sup class="footnote-marker">56</sup><i class="footnote">But naturally he still is liable for a sacrifice to atone for the unauthorized use of <i>sancta</i> (מְעִילָה).</i>. If he ate elevation offerings, if he ate parts<sup class="footnote-marker">57</sup><i class="footnote">The fat to be burned on the altar and forbidden for human consumption (<a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Pesachim 5:10:1" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Pesachim.5.10.1">Chapter 5, Note 50</a>).</i>, since they are not permitted to pure persons one is not liable for it.
If he<sup class="footnote-marker">58</sup><i class="footnote">The persons whose impurity is caused by their own body, who are excluded from the sacred domain, entering at a time when the <i>Pesaḥ</i> (which is to be brought in impurity) cannot be slaughtered. The question presupposes that practice follows R. Eliezer.</i> entered in the night, if he entered before noontime? Rebbi Yose said, if Rebbi Eliezer would hold with Rebbi Simeon, what is the reason on <i>she may not touch any sancta and into the Sanctuary she may not come</i><sup class="footnote-marker">59</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Leviticus 12:4" href="/Leviticus.12.4"><i>Lev.</i> 12:4</a>, of the woman after birth and before she brought the sacrifice which permits her to enter the sacred domain.</i><i>?</i> In case one be liable for eating <i>sancta</i> one is liable for entering the Sanctuary, and in case one be not liable for eating <i>sancta</i> one is not liable for entering the Sanctuary. If Rebbi Simeon would hold with Rebbi Eliezer, what is the reason on <i>she may not touch any sancta and in the Sanctuary she may not come?</i> In case one is liable for entering the Sanctuary one is liable for eating <i>sancta</i> and in case one is not liable for entering the Sanctuary one is not liable for eating <i>sancta</i><sup class="footnote-marker">60</sup><i class="footnote">The Mishnah is consistent; the anonymous part and that attributed to R. Eliezer express the same principles.</i><i>.</i>

Halakhah 5

<strong>MISHNAH:</strong> What is the difference between Passover in Egypt and the Passover of generations<sup class="footnote-marker">61</sup><i class="footnote">Passover for future generations.</i>? The <i>Pesaḥ</i> in Egypt was bought on the Tenth<sup class="footnote-marker">62</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Exodus 12:3" href="/Exodus.12.3"><i>Ex.</i> 12:3</a>.</i>, and needed sprinkling with a bunch of hyssop on the lintel and two door-posts<sup class="footnote-marker">63</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Exodus 12:22" href="/Exodus.12.22"><i>Ex.</i> 12:22</a>.</i>, and was eaten in a hurry<sup class="footnote-marker">64</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Exodus 12:11" href="/Exodus.12.11"><i>Ex</i>. 12:11</a>.</i>, during one night<sup class="footnote-marker">65</sup><i class="footnote">The following day was a common workday on which they left Egypt.</i>. But Passover of generations is all of seven [days].
<strong>HALAKHAH:</strong> Some Tannaim state, membranes over the eyes and cataracts were disqualifying for it<sup class="footnote-marker">66</sup><i class="footnote">As they are disqualifying for sacrifices; <a class="refLink" data-ref="Leviticus 22:22-24" href="/Leviticus.22.22-24"><i>Lev.</i> 22:22–24</a>. <i>Mekhilta dR. Isamel Bo</i> 4.</i>. Some Tannaim state, membranes over the eyes and cataracts were not disqualifying for it<sup class="footnote-marker">67</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Tosefta Pesachim (Lieberman) 8:11" href="/Tosefta_Pesachim_(Lieberman).8.11">Tosephta 8:11</a>.</i>. He who said, membranes over the eyes and cataracts were disqualifying for it, is understandable, since it is written, <i>a perfect lamb</i><sup class="footnote-marker">68</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Exodus 12:5" href="/Exodus.12.5"><i>Ex.</i> 12:5</a>.</i>. He who said, membranes over the eyes and cataracts were not disqualifying for it, how does he confirm <i>a perfect lamb?</i> <sup class="footnote-marker">69</sup><i class="footnote">The next sentences are from <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Sotah 9:5:5" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Sotah.9.5.5"><i>Soṭah</i> 9:5, Notes 109–112</a>.</i> Even for offerings of the descendants of Noah it is impossible! Did not Rebbi Yasa say that Rebbi Eleazar made it clear to the colleagues, <i>from all living, from all flesh</i><sup class="footnote-marker">70</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Genesis 6:19" href="/Genesis.6.19"><i>Gen.</i> 6:19</a>. <i>From all living creatures, each one with its entire flesh,</i> i. e., a whole body. <a class="refLink" data-ref="Avodah Zarah 5b" href="/Avodah_Zarah.5b">Babli <i>Avodah zarah</i> 5b</a>.<br>Since Noah sacrificed some of the pure animals after the Flood, they must have conformed to the rules of sacrificial animals. But the <i>Pesaḥ</i> in Egypt was not an altar sacrifice.</i><i>,</i> that they were complete in their limbs. There, some of them were for the altar, here nothing is for the altar. <sup class="footnote-marker">71</sup><i class="footnote">This sentence belongs to <i>Soṭah,</i> it has no place here.</i>(Rebbi Ḥuna in the name of Rebbi Joḥanan, since you say, purgation is written there as for sacrifices, but here the altar has no part) But is was stated thus: Our forefathers in Egypt had three altars, the lintel and two door-posts. Some Tannaim state, four: the door-step, and the lintel, and two door-posts. Some Tannaim state, סַף is a vessel. Some Tannaim state, סַף is the door-step. He who said, סַף is a vessel, <i>the cups, and the pruning knives, and the vessels for pouring</i><sup class="footnote-marker">72</sup><i class="footnote"><i>1K.</i> 6:50. The words are badly misspelled. The word is סף I.</i><i>.</i> He who said, סַף is the door-step, <i>when they used My door-step and their door-step</i><sup class="footnote-marker">73</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Ezekiel 43:8" href="/Ezekiel.43.8"><i>Ez.</i> 43:8</a>, סף II.</i><i>.</i> He who said, סַף is a vessel, is understandable<sup class="footnote-marker">74</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Exodus 12:22" href="/Exodus.12.22"><i>Ex.</i> 12:22</a>.</i>; <i>from the blood in the</i> סַף. He who said, סַף is the door-step, how does he confirm that סַף may mean a vessel? He brings a cup as סַף, puts it down on the door-step, dunks and sprinkles.
It was stated: Ben Bag-bag says, <i>a perfect lamb,</i> shorn is not perfect. But was it not stated, <i>of small cattle</i><sup class="footnote-marker">75</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Leviticus 1:2" href="/Leviticus.1.2"><i>Lev.</i> 1:2</a>. As always, prefix <i>mem</i> is read as: from some, not all.</i><i>,</i> to exclude the smooth of them. Rebbi Abun said, to exclude those which the Torah separated<sup class="footnote-marker">76</sup><i class="footnote"><i>Sifra Wayyiqra I (Nedavah) Pereq</i> 2.</i>, the male or female used for bestiality, one dedicated for idolatrous worship, and one worshipped.
Rebbi Yose said, also Rebbi Yose the Galilean is with them<sup class="footnote-marker">77</sup><i class="footnote">With the author of the last statement in the Mishnah, that Passover in Egypt was only one day. <a class="refLink" data-ref="Tosefta Pesachim (Lieberman) 8:21" href="/Tosefta_Pesachim_(Lieberman).8.21">Tosephta 8:21</a>, as minority opinion.</i>, as it was stated: Rebbi Yose the Galilean said, I am saying that Passover in Egypt was only one day, as it is said, <i>no leavened matter shall be eaten; today</i><sup class="footnote-marker">78</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Exodus 13:3-4" href="/Exodus.13.3-4"><i>Ex.</i> 13:3–4</a>.</i><i>.</i>

Halakhah 6

<strong>MISHNAH:</strong> Rebbi Joshua said, I have heard that the substitute of a <i>Pesaḥ</i> is sacrificed and that the substitute of a <i>Pesaḥ</i> is not sacrificed, and I cannot explain it. Rebbi Aqiba said, I shall explain it. The <i>Pesaḥ</i> which is found<sup class="footnote-marker">79</sup><i class="footnote">An animal had been designated as <i>Pesaḥ</i> when it was lost and another animal was designated in its stead. If then it is found before the afternoon of the 14<sup class="footnote-marker">th</sup> of Nisan, it remains dedicated but cannot be sacrificed since only one <i>Pesaḥ</i> is possible for one group. A sacrifice which could not be used for the intended purpose cannot be used anymore.</i> before the time of slaughtering the <i>Pesaḥ</i> shall graze until it becomes unusable<sup class="footnote-marker">80</sup><i class="footnote">Either is develops a defect which disqualifies it for the altar or it becomes too old. Then it may be sold and the dedication is removed from the animal and transferred to the money, which only may be used to buy sacrificial animals.</i>, then be sold, and for the money one shall bring well-being offerings; the same holds for its substitute<sup class="footnote-marker">81</sup><i class="footnote">This refers to unauthorized substitutes, where the act of substitution is sinful but the substituted animal nevertheless acquires the status of the animal for which it is substituted <a class="refLink" data-ref="Leviticus 27:10" href="/Leviticus.27.10"><i>(Lev.</i> 27:10</a>).</i>. After the time of slaughtering the <i>Pesaḥ,</i> it shall be brought as well-being offering<sup class="footnote-marker">82</sup><i class="footnote">Since the dedication as <i>Pesaḥ</i> after the 14th of Nisan automatically becomes dedication as well-being offering.</i>; the same holds for its substitute.
<strong>HALAKHAH:</strong> Rebbi Yudan asked, is it the same for the substitute of a reparation offering, that the substitute of a reparation offering is sacrificed and the substitute of a reparation offering is not sacrificed<sup class="footnote-marker">83</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Leviticus 27:10" href="/Leviticus.27.10"><i>Lev.</i> 27:10</a> prescribes that the status of an (illegal) substitute of a sacrifice is that of the sacrifice for which it is substituted. But this condition cannot be fulfilled for a reparation sacrifice since for one obligation only one sacrifice is possible. Therefore it is decreed (Mishnsh <i>Temurah</i> 3:3) that in all cases the substitute of a reparation sacrifice (in contrast to substitutes of purification sacrifices) should be sent to graze until it becomes unusable, then be sold, and for the money one shall buy elevation sacrifices. The question is why, if the animal was lost and only found after the original had been sacrificed, it cannot be used directly as elevation sacrifice. No answer is given. As S. Liebermann points out, in the opinion of <a class="refLink" data-ref="Tosafot on Pesachim 73a:10:1" href="/Tosafot_on_Pesachim.73a.10.1">Tosaphot (73a, <i>s.v.</i>אשם</a>), by biblical standards any substitute of a reparation sacrifice could be brought as elevation offering and the circuitous route via grazing is purely rabbinic; since the original rule does not mention exceptions, the question should not have been asked.</i>? <sup class="footnote-marker">84</sup><i class="footnote">This sentence is copied from <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Pesachim 4:1:6" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Pesachim.4.1.6">Chapter 4:1, Note 27</a>. However, only the first part is relevant here. It defines “the time of slaughtering the <i>Pesaḥ”</i> mentioned in the Mishnah: this is the afternoon of the Fourteenth of Nisan. Therefore, in the following, “Thirteenth” really means “Thirteenth and morning of Fourteenth”, and “Fourteenth” means “Afternoon of the Fourteenth”.</i> Rebbi Yose said, a <i>Pesaḥ</i> which one sacrificed [in the morning] is no <i>Pesaḥ;</i> an elevation offering which one sacrificed in the morning is an elevation offering.
If he substituted for it on the Thirteenth, Rebbi Zeˋira said, the substitute is brought as a well-being offering<sup class="footnote-marker">85</sup><i class="footnote">Since the dedication of a <i>Pesaḥ</i> animal which is not used automatically is that of well-being sacrifice.</i>; Rebbi Samuel ben Rav Isaac said, the substitute is not brought as a well-being offering<sup class="footnote-marker">86</sup><i class="footnote">But it must be sent to graze, as spelled out in the Mishnah.</i>.
